On the day they arrived, the new students were escorted to the back of our classroom. As they introduced themselves, Nathaniel Bennon was directed to the seat next to me. Wanting him to feel welcome, I smiled as he approached. Later in the year, Nathaniel asked me, "The day we came to your class, why were you smiling at me?" I replied that I wanted to make him feel comfortable. That seemed to satisfy his curiosity, and we became good buddies thereafter.

What did you do during recess?

We had a playground with swings, monkey bars, and a jungle gym. We also played kickball.

Who were your favorite teachers?

In elementary school, my favorite teacher was my second grade teacher, Ms. Burbage, because she had this deck of reading material color-coded by difficulty level. We would take one out, read the story and answer questions about it. If we passed, we went to the next one. She was very encouraging, and I was very proud to have reached the 'purple' level.

Did you ever get in trouble at school as a child?

I do not remember ever getting into serious trouble at school, but I recently found some old report cards from elementary school my mother had kept that had several comments about my talking too much, but that is all I can remember.

Times Were Different

What I do remember is that I probably would never have persisted in doing anything enough to get into serious trouble, because I would have been terrified of the teacher or the principal first, and then having them send a note home from school to my parents. That is how they contacted parents back then. Youd have to take the note home and bring it back signed showing they saw it. I would never have considered forging their signature, probably because I couldnt have done it right and then Id get in more trouble.

This doesn't seem to be the case any longer. It seems that parents take the side of the kids over the teachers and teachers get very little support if not outright resistance from parents in maintaining discipline. Of course, there are also cases where the teacher is in the wrong. This is a difficult situation, because society has changed so much that teachers can have far different values than parents. So, in some cases, parents should stand up more for their children. But on the other hand, teachers cannot teach in an environment where the students will not control their behavior.

What school activities did you participate in?

The Violin

One day everyone rotated into the cafeteria/auditorium to listen to a small orchestra with string and wind instruments. When it was over, they asked if anyone was interested in learning to play one of the instruments. I went home and asked my mother. She said, "We'll have to ask your father." When he got home, I hesitantly asked him, afraid he might say no. It really surprised me that he instantly said yes! I came to find out he would support us in whatever we wanted to do.

I started playing violin in the fifth grade and continued in the sixth grade when I changed schools. I could read music and was playing the 'first' chair, which meant the lead violin player. I'm not sure how good we were, probably not very good, but I enjoyed it, and it gave me confidence.

What games did you play at school?

The only game I remember playing at school was kickball. Sometimes we would get to school before it was read to start and we would play. And then at recess, we would play kick ball or climb on the playground equipment.

What do you remember outside of school about this time?

Creighton Street

In 1965, we moved from Woodbine Terrace in Spartanburg to Creighton Street in Taylors, SC. I turned 6 years old that year and began to become much more aware of myself and my surroundings.

The House

This was the first house Mom and Dad owned. If I remember correctly, they paid $17,900 for it. It had three bedrooms. A kitchen that opened into the den. It had a separate dining room and living room, which we almost never used. Scot and I shared a room, Greg and Mark shared a room, and Mom and Dad had the master. It only had a window air conditioner in the den. In the summer, when it would got hot, Dad would put a fan in our window blowing out and sucking air through the rest of the house to cool it. Initially, it had a septic tank in the front yard, and it would leak. When I cut the grass I would have to cut through the wetness and the smell.

The picture is from after we moved out, because what is now a garage was an open carport that can be seen in some other pictures. It is quite a nice house. The slope of the driveway and the front yard is far less than I remember. We would sled down the driveway and the hill in the front used to give me a hard time with the lawn mower.

My Bike

My bike was my life. I practically lived on it. It was a blue Schwinn Sting-Ray with raised handlebars and a banana seat. Eventually I learned to do wheelieslifting the front wheel and pedaling while riding on the back wheel.

Cub Scouts

I was in cub scouts for a while. My mother was the Den Mother and Dad was the pack master, and we would have the meetings at our house. I remember doing the tasks to achieve the awards, the arrows and the pins that would go on the tassels on our arms. Getting promoted to Webelo. At the cub scout picnic at Paris Mountain, all the boys were standing on the shoal of a river throwing rocks. I bent down to pick up another rock and when I stood up a kid behind me hit me in the back of the head, requiring 4 stitches.

Pinewood Derby

The Pinewood Derby was (is) an annual cub scout race. Each scout bought a kit that consisted of a block of wood, some axle pieces, plastic wheels and nails to hold them on. The objective was to carve the car into an aerodynamic shape and attach the wheels in a way that they spun smoothly. Weight could be added to the car, but only up to a certain limit. Usually, the cars were painted and decals added. The race consisted of a series of heats. Narrowing down to the winner. I remember carving and sanding, drilling holes and melting lead to pour in. Painting.. Trying to glue the axels in without getting glue in the axel or the wheel hole. Dad forced me to do all the work, as he should have, and it was about as good as a kid could build with no experience. But l was surprised, disappointed and thought it was unfair when I saw that some of the cars had clearly been done more by the parent than the kid. I heard that some sanded down the nails and the insides of the wheels to reduce friction. It was already a science back then. Im sure I was out of the race quickly, but it was still fun.

Yo-Yos

Duncan yo-yos became a fad in the late sixties, when I was around 7-9. We lived on Creighton Street and the Duncan yo-yo rep would come to the little country store (Leee Road Grocery) , line us up in the parking lot and have us show him the yo-yo tricks we could do. If we could do the tricks he asked about, he would give us a free yo-yo. I won one of the contests and won a butterfly yo-yo. I could do the Sleeper, Walk the Dog, Around the World, and Rock the Baby. Part of the secret is to keep the string tightness around the axel loose enough. If it gets too tight, it will grab and come out of the trick too soon.Not tight enough and it wont rwind after the trick.

Knocked His Teeth Out

In the beginning, we had linoleum floor from the kitchen all the way through the living room. Later we installed indoor/outdoor carpet. We would get a running start in our socks and slide as far as we could. There was a couch about halfway down. One time I was sitting on the end of the couch as Scot was beginning to run and take his turn. I had this idea in my head that if I stuck out my arm, I would catch him and he would loop around my arm like in the cartoons. I stuck out my arm, caught him right in the mouth and knocked his two front teeth out. They flew all the way down to the end of the hall under the door.

The Fire

On the last day of fifth grade, I was wearing a pair of new shorts one day and decided to paint one of my model cars. In the process, I dropped the brush and got paint on my new shorts. Dad told me to get a toothbrush, dip it in the gasoline and clean off the paint. As I was dipping the brush, I dropped it into the gasoline jug. Dad told me to get the brush out or it would dissolve and ruin the gasoline.

I poured the gasoline into a large bowl and got the brush out. But to get the gasoline back into the jug, I didnt have a funnel. All I could find was a large bearing that had a big hole on one end and a small hole on the other end. All of my brothers were gathered around in the storage room as Scot and I tried to pour the gasoline back into the jug.

The utility room was where the washer, dryer and hot water heater were. As we poured the gasoline, Scot held the bearing. It poured out to fast and overflowed onto Scots hands. He jerked his hands away, spilling all of the gasoline on the floor. We are not sure whether it was the bearing hitting concrete or the pilot light of the gas water heater that ignited the gasoline. But it all went up in a huge swoosh noise.

My brothers were on the door side and were able to run out. I was in the fire. I tried to jump up onto the washer and dryer but was not tall enough to get on them. At that point, which had only been a few seconds, I ran through the flames and out through the back door.

I ran around the back of the house into the back door screaming fire, fire, fire. Everyone had heard the gasoline ignite and ran out through the kitchen door into the garage and utility room. I ran through the kitchen door and was met there by my mother who had apparently heard me and came back. She pointed me toward the street and told me to run down to the end away from the fire.

As I got about halfway down the driveway, I started slapping my legs as if something was itching. I looked down and saw enormous blisters on the outside of one leg literally what seemed to be one or 2 inches high.

I ran back up the driveway as my mother was coming for me to have me continue down the driveway. When she saw that I had been burned she took me to the water spigot on the front of the house and started spraying my legs. And my chin was burned so badly I grabbed the hose and let it run down the chin to cool it off.

From that point all I remember is Gil Grahams father driving the car to the hospital. I was in the back seat with the windows open and my legs up so the wind would keep them cool. When we stopped at a red light the pain was excruciating. And I believe he ran red lights all the way to the hospital.

Luckily, I only had mainly second-degree burns. I still have a line that marks where my shorts were. I slept on the pull out couch in the living room for 6 weeks until I could stand and the pressure would not hurt.

Cement Fight

When we lived on Creighton Street, they were still building houses in the neighborhood. One day, geniuses that we were, we stole a bag of cement and made cement balls, like snowballs, and we were going to have war across the road. One group would be on one side and another group on the other side, and we were going to throw cement balls at each other. I think we figured out before we threw any that that was going to be a bad idea. Not much foresight in little kids.

Award Winning Decorations

One Christmas, for decoration, Mom and Dad set up a Santa Claus climbing in the front window. You could only see his legs hanging out. I think they won an award of $5 for it.

Three Men Died

When our streets were originally paved, we did not have sewers. All of the houses had septic tanks. So, when they upgraded to sewers, they cut a deep trench in the middle of the street and installed concrete pipe. The trenches were deep, and the men doing the work were well below the top of the trench. We found out later that they were supposed to be using supports on the sides of the trenches to keep them from collapsing, but they weren't, One day, they were working on an area down near my friend's house and the sides collapsed and trapped and killed three of the men. They tried to dig them out but couldnt reach them in time.

Penny Collection

We had these books for saving pennies. There were slots for many pennies. Each slot was numbered with a year and sometime the letter of the mint it was minted in. Mom would go to the bank and get $3 of pennies and let us go through them to find the years we didnt have. I had a couple of these books well filled up, and one day I decided I needed some money to go to the store for candy. I pulled the pennies out and went and bought candy. They would be worth a lot today. Kids cant always make good value judgments.

Yard on Fire

We lived a few blocks away from the corner store (Lee Road Grocery) and would walk there to buy candy. One day we were taking a short-cut through yards and for some reason I had a book of matches. I would strike one, blow it out and throw it down, and strike another. On the way back from the store we passed this yard we had crossed through, and the whole thing had been burned. I dont know who might have done that but it wasnt that way when we crossed the first time!

Mistletoe

Before all of the houses were constructed, we would take walks through the woods on the weekends with Dad. Near Christmas, hed bring his .410 shotgun and wed take turns shooting down mistletoe.

Haircuts

We used to get haircuts on the back porch sitting in a high chair. That may explain the awesome cuts we were sporting as kids. Buzz cut with bangs.

Umbrella Parachute

In the vacant lot next to our house, Dad had built a bit of a platform between some trees that we called a tree house. One day I convinced Mark to jump out using an umbrella as a parachute. It wasn't that high, but high enough. When he jumped he dropped like a stone and knocked out one of his teeth. When Mom came home from work, Mark showed her, and I remember Mom running around the outside of the house trying to find me crying, "You knocked my baby's tooth out!" I was in big trouble.

Sheet Parachute

I think I was on the roof cleaning out the gutters when I got the bright idea that I could jump off the roof with a sheet as a parachute. I climbed down, ran inside, got a sheet, climbed back up and after quite a bit of contemplation, I jumped. I hit the ground hard and it hurt very badly, but luckily didnt break a leg. I support earlier physics training in schools.

Burning Leaves

Sometime after the fire that burned my legs, we were raking leaves in the back yard. When burning leaves was acceptable, we had this wire mesh thing we would load the leaves into and burn them. Things were going as planned and the leaves were being burned. I was loading a rake load full every so often. One time, when I was trying to put in another rake load, the end of the rake caught on the edge of the wired and pulled the entire thing over, and fire spilled out over the ground. Ordinarily, it would not have been a big deal, but the fire spilling out like that scared me to death and I panicked running around screaming until my mother came out and calmed me down.

Brick on a String

One day I took a broken brick with a hole in it and tied a piece of string through the hole. With no real purpose, I swung the brick up over a tree limb and the string wrapped around the limb a few times. I pulled on the string and the brick unwound around the limb and came off. I thought, hey that was fun. I did it a couple more times, but then the brick crossed over the string essentially tying it to the limb. I stood directly under the brick looking up. I pulled a little, then harder, then harder. Eventually the string broke and the brick came down and hit me under the eye requiring 4 stitches. Not the sharpest tack.

Flying Glass

The lots next to our house were vacant for a while and we played in the woods there quite a bit. One day we were walking through one of the trails. Mark found a piece of glass, and for some unknown reason, threw it in my direction. It hit be right behind the knees and cut me requiring 6 stitches.

The Runaways

When I was about 8 or 9, which would have Mark about 4-5, for some reason, we were not happy with Mom and Dad. They had likely punished us for something. Anyway, we got the great idea that we were going to run away from home. One Saturday morning we woke up before Mom and Dad and packed our things. We literally put a few random clothes and cereal boxes for breakfast in the old-style brown paper grocery bags and we headed out. I had a Sucrets cough drop box with some change. We went down to the corner and turned left. About that time, we all started reconsidering and went back home. Unpacked everything and went into Mom and Dads room and all climbed into the bed, like we used to do, and everything was fine.

Boy Scout Accident

At a boy scout picnic at Paris Mountain, some of us went down to the side of the creek and started skipping rocks. Other kids came down, and soon almost the entire troop was down along the sandy rocky beach throwing rocks. I bent down to pick up a rock and as I was coming back up, another kid nailed me in the back of the head with a rock from close range requiring 4 stitches.

Sheltered

On another boy scout trip, we went to this small river. Everyone was told to takeoff their clothes and swim in the river. Everyone else was doing it, but I was too shy.

The Tattle Tail

As four boys close in age, we were bratty. We would complain and tell on the others if they did something we didnt like. Finally fed up, our grandmother who was keeping us during the day told us that if either of us tattled on the other, she was going to make them wear a tattle tail. We all were out playing, and Greg made the poor choice of going to tattle on us for something. He ran into the house and came out a little while later with a piece of cloth hanging out of the back of his pants. He was so embarrassed he wouldnt leave the yard.

Bicycles in the Mud

At the end of our street there was a long section that had not been paved and there were no houses there. The street wound around and came back out to another paved area part of the neighborhood. One day my brother Scot and I decided we were going to ride around the curve. But it had been raining, and the dirt road was almost all mud. We rode through it for a while, but our bikes had fenders over the tires, and they filled with mud to the point the tires would not turn. We debated whether to go back the way we came or continue. Either way would still be a long way, but we guessed incorrectly that we were more than halfway. So, we had to drag our bikes the rest of the way and had mud all over us. When we got back, our grandmother who was keeping us had been looking for us and we had been gone a long time. She was not happy with us. We had been lost, late, and now we were muddy, and our bikes messed up. She switched us as we walked our bikes back up the hill a very long way to our house.

Christmas Tree

One year, when I was maybe 8 or 9, Dad piled us all in the car to go find a Christmas tree. I do not know where it was, but it was not a tree lot. We drove along a road until he found one he wanted. He parked the car, told us to stay in the car and he would be right back. We watched as he jumped over a ditch, climbed up a hill, over a barbed wire fence to a tree just on the other side. A neighborhood kid, that turned out later to be a lot of trouble (Steve Burgess) was with us, and he dared Greg to do what turned out to be taking the car out of park into neutral. After a lot of prodding, Greg did, and the car started to roll down the hill. We immediately started screaming, I remember looking out the window seeing Dad recognize that the car was rolling. He stopped sawing, jumped over the barbed wire fence, fell down the hill into the ditch, climbed out of the ditch and chased down the car and was able to stop it before it went too far. Greg got a spanking right there. Dad then got the tree, and I dont remember much else.

Ink Blots

One day I was doing something with a red permanent marker. It was low on ink so I started shaking it to get the ink toward the tip. For some reason I was walking around the house shaking this pen only to find I had been staining the carpet throughout the house.

Manmade Sledding

When it would freeze, we would wet the driveway with a cup from the outside spigot and sled down it the next day. I remember the driveway as being steep and we would have to stop ourselves at the bottom to avoid going into the neighbors yard. But seeing the driveway now, it is not steep at all.

First Pet

Our first pet was a German Shepherd named, Pud, short for puddy dog. My mother named him. He followed us around everywhere, but he must have been mean to others, because he killed my mothers best friends baby cat. We were told he was given to some people on a farm where he had more space. Im not sure if that is true.

Poor Frog

I once found a frog in the woods next to our house. My cousin Jimmy was visiting. I had put the frog down to let it jump and Jimmy took a long stick on its back to hold it down. I asked him to take it off. He held it there a moment and then jammed the stick into the frog killing it. I was horrified as he laughed.

Dads First and Last Deer

Many of the guys that worked in Dads manufacturing shop would hunt deer. But many people go a long time before getting a deer. They invited him one weekend. He was not a hunter so he said he didnt have the equipment. So, they loaned him a gun, gave him the shells, gave him a location and stand to wait in, and on his first trip saw a deer come in front of his stand. He took the shot and got his first (and last) deer, with borrowed equipment. After they got the deer back, Dad called mom and she cried knowing that he had killed one. He asked her to take us to where they were and this picture is me, Robbie Edwards and Tim Graham with the deer. At the time I could not understand, but they put the deers testicles in a jar of formaldehyde and stored them on a shelf in the shop.

Burning Leaves

Sometime after the fire that burned my legs, we were raking leaves in the backyard and Mom was burning them in this wire contraption. You put the leaves in the top and as they burn the ashes fall out the side and you put more leaves in. I was putting leaves in with the rake and one of the rake tines got caught in the wire and pulled the entire thing over spreading fire for several feet. The sight of the uncontrolled fire sent me into a panic. Clearly an overreaction, but Mom handled it calmly and got it under control quickly. I was surprised how panicked I became so quickly, but I guess the mind remembers.

Punt, Pass & Kick

When I was 10 years old, one day at football practice, I got my hand caught in someones helmet and broke the bones in my hand. I wore a cast for 6 weeks. The day after I got the cast off was the annual Punt, Pass and Kick tournament. I had been able to practice punting and kicking but couldnt practice passing. My hand was very weak from being immobilized in the cast. I could barely hold the ball, but I wanted to compete anyway. I won the kicking and punting parts, but because I couldnt throw, I came in third overall. I am certain I would have won with a healed hand. I still have the trophy.

First Black Person

I tread carefully on this subject because it is so widely misunderstood and mislabeled. But desegregation only happened beginning in 1967. So only white people went to my elementary school until 5th grade.. One afternoon I was picking blackberries in a vacant lot. The bushes were tall and thick. I walked around a bush and saw a black boy standing there looking at me. Both of us were equally surprised to see each other. It was likely the first time I had ever seen a black person in-person. We nodded at each other and continued picking.

Constant Competition

Life with four boys close in age was pretty much constant motion and competition. We were constantly arguing and competing over everything imaginable. We would claim sitting in the front seat. We'd see a cereal commercial and claim the first toy inside if we ever got that kind of cereal (which we never did). We'd argue over which of the three TV channels we were going to watch, whether someone was sitting too close to them or on their side of the car, or who ate the last cupcake. The list of things we could and would argue about was endless.

This will likely appear somewhat normal. However, I have learned over the years that our beliefs are shaped by our experiences. And, while we have to learn to compete with others, too much of it leads to an unhealthy criticism and competition with others. We should also learn compassion and sharing in these situations.

Battle Scars

Between Greg, Mark, and me, we have over 100 stitches from various injuries. Somehow Scot had none! Mark threw a piece of glass and hit Greg in the forehead requiring 10+ stitches. Greg threw glass and hit me in the back of the leg requiring 6 stitches. I convinced Mark that he could jump out of the tree house (probably 10 feet off the ground) with an umbrella and it would work like a parachute. It didn't, and it knocked his tooth out. We were sliding on the linoleum on our sock feet when I stuck my arm out because I had seen on a cartoon that the character would swing around the arm - instead, I knocked out Scot's two front teeth.

Creative Mishaps

Our attempts at play could take unexpected turns. Scot and I were playing Martian or robot or something, and Scot put Q-Tips in his ears to look either like a Martian or a robot. I fake shot him. He fell on the bed sideways and punctured his ear drum. Miraculously, it grew back. Looking back now, I'm amazed at how many of our "creative" ideas led to some kind of accident or injury!

Big Brother Tricks

Being the youngest, Mark was often the target of our schemes. I once convinced him that the onions on his Krystal hamburger were rice so he would give it to me. And since he wasn't quite up to speed on vocabulary, we'd all pile on when he made mistakes. His classic mix-ups included:

  • "Felete o Fish" for Filet O Fish at McDonalds
  • "Maindain" for the median separating lanes
  • "Locomotive" for the song Locomotion
  • "Lee Torino" - He saw a Torino and said "Hey, that is just like Lee Torino" (It's Trevino)

Home Life

Our house had three bedrooms. Scot and I shared a room, and Greg and Mark shared a room. It only had a window air conditioner in the den. In the summer, when it would get hot, Dad would put a fan in our window blowing out and sucking air through the rest of the house to cool it. In the winter, we would spray water on the driveway when it would freeze and have the whole neighborhood over the next day to sled down.

YMCA Days

On some days, instead of going home from school, I would take another school bus to the YMCA for swimming and basketball for the afternoon and then it would bring us back The YMCA was a pretty long distance from the school. Even by todays standards, it was far. I would guess 15 or 20 miles. I would get back to the school late. It would be dark by then and mom would pick me up. Other times Mom would have to drive us to practice. One of the reasons we eventually moved to Greenville was to be closer to the Y.

Bambi

Bambi was one of the first movies I ever saw and I was devastated when Bambis father was killed. Could not understand how that could be allowed to happen.

My Baseball Experience

I had not thought about this in a long time, but I was generally decent at most sports. My first baseball team was called Toolmation, named after the company that gave the money for the uniforms. We werent the Tigers or the Braves. Our uniforms were a black t-shirt with white , square, iron-on letters and numbers. In one game, I hit a home run. We went to dairy queen after and a parent gave me a dollar for the home run. I was so proud!.

Another time I was playing right field and the batter hit a fly ball. The centerfielder and I started running in toward it. I thought it was going to him, so I stopped, but the sun was bright so I held up my glove hand to block the sun and the ball landed in my glove!.

Later when I was about 11 or 12, I was a pitcher, and doing well from what I remember. The coach taught me the knuckle curve that I eventually taught William. The next step in baseball was to play for the Optimist team. I dont remember details, but I think the coach was allowing me to play as a sort of tryout. We were playing a game and he put me in to pitch. As a sign of the level of coaching we got back then, I had no idea what a balk was.. I tend to remember that I was pitching relatively well, but for no reason that I could understand, the umpire called a balk on seemingly every other pitch. I dont recall, but I can only imagine there were guys on base and I was turning my shoulder. The coach called timeout. Came out to talk with me. Probably explained it, but I didnt understand, So when I started to pitch again, the umpire called another balk. The coach took me out and after the game told Mom that I wasnt ready for the team. Well, that was devastating. And ended my baseball. It seems that I could have been taught, and I dont know exactly what happened, but that was the last game I ever played.

Woods Lake

Occasionally we would go swimming at Woods Lake a short drive from our house. It was a lake built up as a public swimming pool. It has a huge slide in the middle.

Camp Greenville

The YMCA had a camp in the mountains called Camp Greenville. Scot and I went as kids. I think I was 10 years old. It had a swimming lake, with a diving platform in the middle. You could go canoeing, do archery, take hikes. Every morning reveille would sound and we would get up an march to breakfast. At night they had lodge where they would put on programs.

We also went as a family one time. In the middle of the night, a bat got in our cabin and Dad and Mr. Edwards were standing in the middle of cabin with a broom and tennis rackets trying to get the bat out.

O Wah Tay Goo Si Am

When we went to Camp Greenville as a family, they had a program one night where they brought all the kids up to the front and wrote what they said was Indian language on the chalk board and we were asked to figure out what it meant, whisper it to one of the counselors and then we could go sit down.

I happened to be one of the older kids there, and I could not figure it out. I was taking the task too literally and did not recognize that the words were Oh what a goose I am. I was very embarrassed not to have gotten it.

How did you spend summers?

Summer Movies

During the summers, the movie theater would sell cheap tickets. We would go on Saturday mornings. One of the movies I remember was Fireball 500, a racing movie.

Lake Hartwell

Lake Hartwell played a large part in my early life. In the late 60s, about 1967, Dad bought a houseboat. As Ive said, he always knew what he wanted out of life and went after it. It was the same with the houseboat. He saw it as a vehicle to enjoy his family and friends. He bought the boat at Harbor Light Marina, and we stayed there for only a little while. But we used to fish on the dock. Very shortly afterwards, he moved the boat to Portman Shoals Marina

We spent many summer days and nights there by ourselves as a family and occasionally with other families of the people Dad worked with.

Many weekends during the summer, we would pack the station wagon with food and clothes and head to the lake. Some weekends, we would leave on Thursday or Friday, leave the dock and not come back until Monday.

We would find coves to anchor in and sleep.

So many memories of the lake. Building camp fires, cooking breakfast in a cast iron pan over the fire. Lying on the top at night and seeing the stars, seeing falling stars occasionally.

Occasionally when the water level would drop, we would hit sand bars and get stuck.

We would jump from the top ding tricks, but only after we were sure to ensure there were no trees or shallow places.

We slept in bunk beds in the back. Mom and Dad would drag a mattress to the front deck and sleep outside.

Caught my first fish trolling off the back of the houseboat as we travelled from one cove to another. Dad cleaned it and Mom cooked it, but I could not being myself to eat it.

Friends would bring their speed boats and we would spend the weekend skiing.

One summer Dad had the boat taken out and he and Ed Edwards spent the next several weeks stripping the bottom and repainting it.

Elementary Reflection

Personal

What were you like in Elementary School?

I dont remember a lot about myself from back then. but my mother had kept a lot of old report cards of mine. We used to get them every 9 weeks. And while it didnt happen in every report, it was written enough times that it must have been an issue.

The notes read something like, Alan could do much better work if he didnt talk so much. Ha! Doesnt sound like me now, but I must have been oblivious to it. I only remember getting one note sent home from school. And I remember I was very worried about it.

What achievements were you proud of?

Who were your role models?

This is something I have thought about over the years. I never had any role models that I know of when I was growing up. I didnt want to be a super hero or a fireman or police officer. I never had posters in my room of celebrities. I dont know why.

Family

What was your daily routine?

Our routine was very routine. Get up, get dressed, eat breakfast, catch the bus to school, go to school, catch the bus home, get a snack, play outside or watch TV, eat dinner, take a bath, go to bed.

What chores did you have?

Cleaning my room and cutting the grass., raking leaves.

What did you do after school?

We mostly played outside, riding our bikes, playing football or exploring in the woods and the creek. We had TV, but only 3 channels. Dad had an 8-track tape player, but we kids had no music. We could listen to the radio in the car, but we didnt have one inside. Video games were not to be invented for another 15 years!

What were family dinners like?

Mom made dinner almost every night. We would wait for Dad if he were coming home, but sometimes he would be late. Mom would make his plate and put it in the over so it would be warm when he got home. Our family dinners were always very reserved and orderly. People would take turns talking, if we talked at all. I didnt realize how different this was until I experienced dinner at other peoples homes.

Social

Were you shy or outgoing?

I was shy.

Who were your friends?

I think my social life at school was similar to most kids. My friends were the kids in my class, and I had a couple that were closer than others. I remember a kid named Dennis in third grade that got his arm pinched by Ms. Ford. A girl named Frieda that I liked and exchanged loved letters with. Also, Nathanial, one of the first black kids in our class.

What memorable social experiences?

 

Middle School

 

What was the name of your middle school?

When I left the fifth grade for the sixth, the state was experimenting with the education system. Instead of moving us to sixth grade in middle school, they sent us to Taylors Elementary School for sixth grade thinking it would be better not to be exposed to seventh and eighth graders so early. I assume they didnt find much difference because middle school still includes 6th grade.

Sixth grade was the first time that we changed classrooms during the day. We rotated to 3 different classes. I dont remember my classes, my teachers, the subjects, my grades, which I assume were average or barely above average.

After the sixth grade, we moved to Cleveland Street I went to a different middle schoolBeck Middle School

How did you get to middle school?

In middle school, I remember a combination of riding the bus and mom taking me and picking me up, but I dont recall how much or why. I liked riding the bus, because it was a fun time to spend with your friends. At that time, no one wore seat belts. I cant imagine being the driver because kids were moving around all the time. Three to five kids crammed in a seat. Not because the bus was too crowded, they just all wanted to sit together. And one group was turned around talking to the group behind. It was loud with everyone trying to talk over the others. Fun for us, but probably a nightmare for the driver.

From what I remember, we didnt have bookbags. We just carried the books and notebooks in a stack. We would make book covers out of brown paper grocery bags, then draw on them and put stickers on them.

Which teachers influenced you most?

I remember very little about middle school except for a few small snippets. We were only two years into integration and there was a big white guy and a big black guy, and the school was buzzing about how they were going to get together and fight. I remember what seemed like throngs of kids sunning across campus to the gym. I think the teachers interrupted it before it could actually happen. Other than that, I dont remember any racial issues. As far as I was concerned, we all got used to it pretty quickly.

What subjects interested you?

I was interested in biology because we were dissecting giant grasshoppers and frogs.

How were your grades?

My grades were likely just barely above average, because I was not the least bit focused on it except on report card day. I dont think Mom and Dad had anything to compare it to except their own experience, which was not academically strong. I remember sme discussion about it around report card time, but very little in between. I was just more focused on the social side of life at the time. But, I couldnt tell you what that was either.

What was your favorite class?

I guess it was biology, but also band. I enjoyed playing the trumpet and participating in the Christmas parades.

What did you find challenging?

I suppose this started earlier I the sixth grade. But, this is when I started noticing my awkwardness with girls. I tell the story later about us putting our arms around girls we liked and the lab partner crush I had, but I was terribly awkward with girls. I did not have any sisters, and while I probably didnt ask, my parents never offered anything on this. Probably because they didnt know either. I was left to my own thoughts, and I developed the belief that girls didnt like boys.

What extracurricular activities did you join?

New Musical Direction

For seventh grade, we had moved to Greenville, and I went to Beck Middle School. I wanted to play in the marching band, so I switched from violin to trumpet. I was also seemingly pretty decent - playing 'first chair', but in hindsight, I don't think we were all that good. In the fall, we would wear uniforms and perform in parades. That was my favorite part. I had held on to the guitar until I moved from Andelle Avenue in 2021.

Educational Guinea Pig

Continuing to experiment, for some reason, for part of the year in my seventh-grade year, they had us go to Nickeltown. It had previously been an all-black school, but they had converted the classrooms for the experiment. The backs of the classrooms were completely open to the hallway. There was no wall or door. Anyone walking down the hall could see and hear in and everyone in the classroom could see and hear anyone that walked by. The only two things I remember about this school s having to memorize and deliver the Gettysburg address, which I likely did less than great., and my friend unfolding a big paperclip and shotting it with the big fat rubber band and a guy walking at least 50 yards away along the street. It didnt hit him, but he came to the office and told the principal that it had whizzed in front of his face. They cam and got my friend.

Pretend Girlfriends

As eighth graders we were also into girls more. We had this little game that would get us into trouble. We would go up to the girls we liked and put our arms around them like we were walking with them. Of course, they would pull away, but I think in hindsight they liked the attention.

Lab Partner Crush

I had a lab partner in biology named Abbie. She was a black girl, and I had a crush on her. I think she liked me too, but we were both too shy to say anything to each other.

Off Campus Lunch

As eighth graders, we were allowed to leave campus for lunch (as long as we came back). I would walk down to the store a block or so away and buy candy (bubble pops) and come back and sell it to people that couldn't or didnt leave. Always the entrepreneur.

Moving to Cleveland Street

Our move from Taylors to Greenville was the most difficult for me. We had lived there for about 7 years, from about age 5 to age 12. It was the home we had lived in the longest and were firmly rooted there in school and friends.

But we were involved in sports at the YMCA, which was about a 30 minute trip each way almost everyday for Mom. So, as he did, Dad searched for a solution. He found a house right across the street from the Y.

The move turned out to be the best thing we could have done, because it gave us so many more opportunities, but, when we first heard, we were devastated.

How did you personally change during these years?

Its really hard to say how I changed. I was not that self-aware. I think I gained some confidence

What social changes occurred?

The social events that affected me were mostly cultural and fashion influences. The music we listened to and the clothes we wore. As I reflect back, I really wasnt particularly engaged in anything outside of my school bubble.

What world events do you remember?

This was the early 1970s. I suppose it was a lot like it is today. We saw things on the news, but they didnt directly affect us. The cultural things did, in terms of music and clothes, but

Casualty Reports

Dad would watch the news when he got home from work, They would report the daily Vietnam casualty reports. I dont recall the numbers, but remember recognizing that it was a lot of people and feeling bad about that.

  The Kent State Shootings.

  Nixon ending the Gold Standard and implementing price controls.

  The Munich Olympics and the athletes being killed.

  The OPEC embargo and the long gas lines.

         Thankfully, world events didnt seem to affect my life. The long gas lines did to some degree as my parents had to wait in them. I wasnt yet driving.

What cultural events influenced you?

This was about 1972, and the styles were influenced by the hippies. Flared jeans and wide belts. Wide and long collars on shirts. I had a pair of red, white and blue striped pants with stars on them. I wore them with a wide white leather belt with multiple holes in them. I grew my hair long and hated to get it cut. In hindsight, it looks horrific, but at that time you could not have convinced me otherwise.

 

High School

What was the name of your high school?

I went to Greenville High School.

What was the mascot?

They were called the Red Raiders, and the mascot was a guy dressed in a pirates outfit..

Was there anything unique about it?

It was a large school for the time. But not very big compared to some today. But even in the late 70s it was an old school, built in 1936! The part that made it seem old was the radiators for heat.

What was high school like?

New Friends

Unfortunately, the middle school I went to was separated into 2 different high schools. Some of my better friends went to J.L. Mann and I went to Greenville High. I think Dad looked into what could be done to change where I went, but I had to go to Greenville High because of the district we lived in.

The school itself was an old three-story building built in 1936. It was 40 years old when I started there, and I dont think it had been significantly renovated since it was built. It was big for the time, with capacity for 1,300 students. My class was just over 300. It had radiators for heat. There was a coal burning stove in the basement that would heat water and circulate it through pipes to the radiators that were below the big tall windows in the rooms. The heat would be controlled by turning on or off the valve. They would get quite hot near them, but the heat would not be circulated by fan or air, so the temperature was uneven throughout each room and the building. It is now almost 90 years old and it has been renovated

What courses did you take?

I took whatever the core curriculum for graduation was, like math (Algebra, Geometry, Calculus), English (Literature), history, science (biology, chemistry). As electives I took Spanish (3 years) and Mechanical Drawing (3 years).

Who were memorable teachers?

My most memorable was my senior Spanish teacher. I tell a separate story about her. Mrs. Richardson is memorable. My chemistry teacher was about 65 years old and drove a Porsche 911. My biology teacher was a football coach. My

What were your academic strengths?

Ha! I did not have many academic strengths. I suppose Spanish and Mechanical Drawing were relative strengths, but I had not yet discovered the joy of learning! I was decent at math, but I hated history. I took Latin for about a week and then changed it for something else. I was terrible at chemistry. I was too busy discovering the joy of having a good time with my friends, trying to be cool, thinking about girls and not ever dating any of them.

What achievements are you proud of?

I am proud that I made the golf, team, but I did not have any particular achievements. I

How did you prepare for college/future?

When I was in high school, other than having this belief in the back of my mind that I would go to college, I had no actual plan. I certainly had no plan for getting good grades, and I only haphazardly prepared for the SAT. The lunchroom to the left, although much more colorful now, it was likely just white and that is where I took the SAT test. In hindsight, I am thankful that getting into South Carolina or Clemson was not as competitive as it eventually became, because I would not have been attending either.

As much as Dad wanted us to go to college, either because he had not gone and didnt know how or because he was so busy running his business, he did not engage with us on how to prepare. I consider myself very lucky to have managed to get in with very average grades and SAT score.

Did you participate in high school sports?

My first and second year in high school, I played football on the junior varsity team. I was playing the line because I had not yet started getting tall. We would practice in the late summer, and it would be brutally hot. The turf would get so torn up that it was nothing but black sand and dust and blowing your nose would come out black. The players started getting so dehydrated they had to start taking salt pills and drinking prune juice. This was before Gatorade!

I really did not like it. For one thing, I was playing the line. Our field was right behind the school, and we played on it so much the grass was gone in the middle and what was underneath was some sort of blackish sand. After groveling around in the sand during practice, it would be in every crevice and even in my nose.

Another thing I didn't like about it was scrimmaging the varsity. They would use us as human punching bags. Its against the rules now, but there was one defensive end that played outside of me (I was the left tackle). I had to be in a three-point stance, so my head was down. He would stand close to the line with his hand cocked, and as soon as the ball was snapped, before I could even move or stand, he would hit me in the side of the head. I was completely defenseless. Helmets back then were not very good either, and I was just getting beaten. The coaches saw it and did nothing about it. It was miserable.

We were playing a game behind the school one day against Mauldin. I was on the kickoff team. Somehow before the kickoff, a player on the other team and I locked eyes, and it was taken for granted that we were going to take each other on. The ball was kicked and he and I ran at each other and hit helmets pretty much full speed. We both fell to the ground. I got up and tried to run, but the entire field seemed tilted about 40 degrees. I could not run or even stand. I fell multiple times trying to get up. Eventually it passed and I was able to get to the sidelines.

Going into my junior year, I had gotten several inches taller and was slimmed down a good bit. Had I continued playing football, I would have probably moved to tight end and the game would have been a lot more fun. My biology coach was one of the coaches and he would talk to me about playing and I culd tell he wanted me to play. But I had gotten good enough at golf to make the golf team, so I quit playing football. Golf was far better. We would get out of class early on match days. That always seemed to be a good thing at the time.

Sports back then were seemingly not as competitive as they are today. People certainly did not have private coaches and there were few if any travelling teams. Our golf coach was the science teacher. He knew very little about golf, and he just basically arranged the matches and kept score. I wish I had had the opportunity for more coaching because I was never able to improve enough on my own.

Golf Team Failure

In ninth grade I tried out for the golf team but didn't make it. On one hole where I was in a sand trap. I didn't know the rule about not touching the sand, so I was taking practice swings hitting the sand. In hindsight, Im embarrassed. One of the seniors was on the green and yelled out, "What are you doing?" I said, "I'm taking a practice swing." He dropped it in exasperation. I didn't make the team.

Sophomore Year

Tenth grade brought English with Ms. Richardson. She was probably 65 years old. A very proper, black lady. When anyone would misbehave, and, yes, we did, she would say in this long drawn out southern sweet voice, "Sillly people." My friend Ray Mason would sit in the back of the room and make wolf howl noises that no one could tell where they were coming from.

Golf Team Success

I made the golf team in the tenth grade.

Golf Team Disappointment

One of my biggest disappointments in high school golf came during the state tournament. The coach had to designate four players to compete. We were competitive with each other. I had been playing reasonably well, but the coach chose not to include me in the four. I was crushed. Any one of us would have been hurt, because we were all similar in capability. He saw that I was hurt and tried to console me, but the decision didnt change, and I felt very low. I dont remember how we did. We didnt win and were likely not expected to. But I was very disappointed not to have been chosen.

Errant Shot

One day before leaving school for a match, we all grabbed a wedge and went to the football field, which was literally three car lengths from the back of the school, to practice chipping. I shanked one and it flew right into the a large bank of windows on the back of the building. Luckily the shade had been pulled down, so it didn't hit anyone. The teacher looked out the window, but couldnt tell it had been me. We all scattered and went to the match.

Summer Golf

In the summer, I would go to the golf course almost every day. Some days, I would practice on the range and the putting green, but most days, I would just play. Some days I would get there before the sun came up and start as soon as I could see the ball, and I would walk, carry my own bag and play 54 holes. That is 3 18-hole rounds. Some days I would have to stop because I could no longer see the ball for darkness.

College Golf

While I was likely a better than average golfer, I was not good enough to play at the college level. I wish there had been the emphasis on coaching and developing sporting skills as there was later. But, while I took a series of 10 lessons when I was about 16-17, I just basically played all the time. I practiced some, but it was more like warm up than practicing. I could shape shots and hit from different lies, but was not really good. I would occasionally shoot under par on 9 holes, but never under par for 18. When I first went to USC, I dont know what my Dad did, but somehow I got a tryout for the golf team. The coach had me hit balls on the range, shaping shots left and right. I thought I did a pretty good job. He then paired me with another guy trying out and sent us out to play. Neither of us played well enough to get considered. And I was disappointed with that.

When I transferred to Clemson, even though I had not been playing, again, somehow I got at least an interview with the golf coach. I dont recall a lot about the interview, but I think it was clear that I just wasnt of the caliber to play college golf at that point.

The Golf Dream Expired

While I didnt make the college teams, I still felt like I had the capability if I just had the practice. When I lived on Linbrook Drive, I was either working for USC or NCR. I was toying with the idea of making an effort to get coaching and see if I could make golf a career. I never really did anything with it and the dream faded. However, I remember a conversation with someone at SQL Financials several years later that I had hopes that I would be able to continue playing, get better and eventually play on the Senior Tour. Well, of course, that never played out either. The closest I got was playing in the ProAm of the Senior Tour Championship. I had a fan approach me for an autograph and another fan tell me, Youre really good! That was heartening.

In hindsight, I was likely far underestimating what it would take and overestimating my capabilities, but it was a pipe dream I had held for some time. Now, the best I can hope for is to interest one of my grandkids in the game and hope I can help them play and enjoy it as much as I have for most of my life.

The Haunted House

There was a house near the school that for at least a couple of years was abandoned. Each year, at Halloween, the seniors would put on a haunted house. When I was a senior, I helped. There were two rooms next to each other separated only by the wall studs. In the back room, we set up a Frankenstein laboratory. We had a table and an electric device with two metal rods that pointed out at an angle. When plugged in, it would send an arc of electricity up the rods and make a noise.

As people came through the house, they would be directed into this room and asked to get up close to the wall to watch. At any one time, there would be 10-20 people crowded into the room to watch.

I was dressed as Frankenstein, lying on the table. Another guy was dressed as Dr. Frankenstein. He would put these battery jumper cables on the fake screws on my neck that were supposedly connected to the electric device. I would awake slowly, get off the table, and there was a girl dressed in a wedding dress. Supposedly Frankensteins monsters wife. I would pick her up and start walking. Then I would obviously notice the people, gradually lower my bride to the ground and then turn toward the people and reach through the wall studs grabbing people. They would scream and be scared. Then I would step through the wall, and they would freak out screaming and running. It was great fun.

Friday Night Lights

Our high school was unusual in that it, it did not have a dedicated stadium. We used a separate stadium call Sirrine Stadium. The Furman Paladins used it for their games on Saturday, and we used it for our games on Friday. It was a very large stadium for a high school to play in, and the atmosphere was very exciting on Friday nights.

Our biggest rivals were Spartanburg and Daniel. We were a middle of the pack team.

Senior Honor

The twelfth grade is where things started aligning for me academically and ultimately professionally. I had been taking Spanish for the two prior years, and I had a youngish Spanish teacher named Mrs. Key. She really encouraged me. One day, a day or so before 'Honors' Day, she asked me if I would be going. I told her yes, but I don't think I really had any intention to do that. It just wasn't something I was focused on.

The next week when I came into school, she asked me why I didn't go. I didn't have a good excuse. I was probably just out with my friends. She had given me the Spanish Award for the year and wanted me to receive it at Honors Day. I felt bad that I hadn't gone. Not as much for the award, but because I had told her I would go and didn't and she had been trying to do something for me. Just that recognition alone started to turn my thinking and focus on studying and getting better grades.

Petes Drive-In

Our favorite hangout was Petes Drive -in. It was, and still is, a very nondescript drive-in hamburger restaurant, run at the time by a bunch of Greek guys. What we like about it was it had a large parking lot. We could go park our cars and then walk around and talk, although often we just sat in out own cars and talked with whoever we were with.

On Halloween, guys would steal pumpkins and bring them to Petes and sit them on the back wall. At midnight they would take them and roll them into the street for the cars to hit and run over, making a colossal mess.

Nicknames

I have only really had two nicknames that stuck for very long. The first was in high school. It really doesnt make a lot of sense except to say that high school kids can be creative and goofy. One afternoon, I was hanging out with my friends and they started calling people different names. Everyone was having names made up for them. Now that I think about it, maybe they were trying to name people by older names. One of the names they chose for me was "Egbert". Everyone thought that was extremely funny. Except me. But like kids will do, they modified it into a shorter nickname, Bert. Everyone from high school and even my brothers recognize me as "Bert."

Who was your favorite teacher in high school?

My favorite teacher in high school was my senior year Spanish teacher, Mrs. Key.

I had started taking Spanish in the 10th grade and was reasonably good at it. Up until my senior year in high school, I had not been the greatest student. I made Bs and Cs mostly. I got better grades in subjects that interested me more, like Mechanical Drawing and Drivers Education! I was equally interested in my friends and having fun as I was getting good grades. (Its funny, I recently came across my report cards from elementary school. My mother had saved them for all these years. I didnt remember this, but I had several comments over multiple 9-week periods over several years where the teacher had said something to the effect, Alan can apply himself more diligently and spend less time talking. Haha! I dont remember getting in trouble for talking too much. Maybe I was talking too much to notice!)

But Mrs. Key changed that. She noticed that I was pretty good at Spanish, and she encouraged me. One day, nearing the end of the year, she asked me if I was going to attend awards day that was coming up in a few days. She wasnt making a big deal about it, and I wasnt thinking that much about it either, But I told her yes and then forgot about it. The day came and I was completely oblivious to it. I dont remember what I was doing, but I didnt go. The next day I had Spanish class, she asked me why I hadnt gone. I don't remember what I was doing or what I said, but I also wasnt thinking it was a big deal. I was kind of surprised she was asking me about it. Then she told me she had given me the Spanish Award for that year, and she had wanted to give it to me during the ceremony.

I was very happy, proud and honored to have received it, but I also felt really badly about letting her down. She had gone out of her way to recognize me, and I had just not gone, with nothing better to do after I had told her I would go. I felt really bad about that.

She was understanding and still encouraged me. It was the beginning of my change in perspective about grades. I had more to learn in college, but she was the initial spark that put me on a better track.

The twelfth grade is when things started to click for me academically and ultimately professionally. I had been taking Spanish for a couple of years, and my teacher, Mrs. Key, was youngish, energetic, and incredibly encouraging.

One day, just before Honors Day, she asked me if I was planning to attend. I said yes but wasnt really giving it much thought.

The following week in class she asked me if I had gone to Honors Day. I didnt have a good answer. Thats when she told me she had selected me for the Spanish Award and had wanted to present it to me at the ceremony.

In that moment, I wasnt concerned about missing the award, but the fact that Id told her Id be there and didnt follow through. She had gone out of her way to recognize me and I had let her down.

She didnt make a big deal about it and dropped it. But that simple act of recognition made an impact on me. Up until then, I wasnt exactly an academic powerhouse. My report cards were a mix of Bs and Cs, and I got better grades in subjects that held my interest, like Mechanical Drawing and Drivers Ed. Socializing was more important to me. (I recently pulled out my old elementary school report cards my mom had saved. My teachers repeatedly noted that Alan talks too much and needs to apply himself more. I dont remember it that way!)

But Mrs. Key saw potential in me and that Spanish Award became a turning point. I didnt instantly become a straight-A student, but it planted a seed that grew.

What was your favorite class?

My favorite class in high school was mechanical drawing. I think I took it as an elective for three years in a row. Of course, back then, everything was mechanical. It was done with triangles and a compass and a wooden triangular ruler, with lead pencils and gum erasers. Initially, we would make two-dimensional drawings, but we eventually got to the point where we would create three 2-dimensional drawings and then create a three-dimensional drawing from them using angles and perspective.

There was a time when I considered being an architect. And in some ways, I wish I had. I think I gravitated to finance simply because of computers and the ability to move numbers around. I am not particularly good at math, although I can figure it out, it is not my greatest strength.

What was your least favorite class?

My least favorite class was chemistry. In hindsight, I am much more interested in it today than then. Oh, I just remembered history may have been my least favorite, and it too has become something I am much more interested in today. In chemistry, I could never figure out valence and how electrons moved from one level to the next. It is likely simple, but I didnt put a lot of effort into learning it. In history, I thought it was so boring. I also had a hard time keeping different periods in perspective as to when they occurred relative to other periods. Again, today, I am interested in history, partially because I am much more interested in the human side of things that led to the decisions they made and created history.

The Bicentennial

In 1976, the US celebrated its 200th year as a country. There were celebrations all over the country, but New York had a special one planned, and Dad planned a vacation for us to go see it. One of the highlights for all of us was watching the tall ships sail into the harbor and up the Hudson river and later going down to see them docked. There were so many people vying for vantage points that they were climbing trees and lamp posts, the sides of buildings. It was packed everywhere, but it was still great. The fireworks show at night over the harbor was magnificent.

Parkins Mill Road

When I was 17, we moved to another house in Greenville, into another school district so my brothers could follow their middle school friends to J.L. Mann High School. I had the option to transfer also, but by that time, I had already established friends at Greenville High and I was going to be a senior.

Personal

How did you change during high school?

Freshman Ignorance

The first day of ninth grade started out with a show of my naivete and ignorance and provided a small but needed lesson. My homeroom number was something like 301. After walking around the hallways and up and down various stairwells for over thirty minutes, I finally asked and was informed that rooms that start with 3 are on the third floor!

Cultural

What cultural events impacted you?

What music was important to you?

I have always liked a range of music, from the oldies to pop and some of almost every genre there is. In high school I listened to Chicago, Elton John. I remember lying on the floor in Scots bedroom listening to his Elton John Yellow Brick Road album over and over. Reading and learning the lyrics.

In middle school, Scot collected Chicago albums and we would listen on my record player. Three Dog Night was a bad I like.(song?)

What TV shows did you watch?

What movies influenced you?

There were several influential movies in high school.

         Jaws This scared everyone out of the water.

         One Flew Over the Cuckoos Nest Jack Nicholson

         Dog Day Afternoon Al Pacino

         Monty Python and the Holy Grail Run away, Run away!

         Rocky Gonna Fly Now Theme is still on everyones workout list.

         All the Presidents Men - Watergate

         Star Wars -

         ET; Close Encounters of the Third Kind -

         Saturday Night Fever Inspired or was inspired by the disco music and fashion.

What fashion trends came about

While a lot of people wore jeans, I never did. I didnt like the way they felt or looked on me. I wore corduroy pants a lot. I also wore Sperry Topsiders. I wore them until the soles fell off. The more beat up the better. I also remember wearing converse tennis shoes and what I remember being called Wallabes. They were like suede half boot with rubber gum soles.

Long hair

Leisure suits.

Man-made fabrics, wide lapels, long collars, bell bottoms, wide ties, plaids.

What science/technological advances happened?

The only technology advances that I would have been aware of that were changing were the technology to play music. We had albums and 45s. Then 8-track tapes. Then cassette tapes. We had in-dash tape decks, speakers, equalizers, power boosters, watts per channel.

What world/political events do you remember?

In 1976, Jimmy Carter beat Gerald Ford. While I couldnt yet vote, I remember being for Carter, because Nixon had created so much trouble. However, Carter turned out to be the worst president ever to that point and for many years after until Obama and Biden. But that is a later story. The economy under Carter was a disaster, with inflation reaching double digits, and the last 400+ days of his presidency was marred by the Iranian hostage that we watched every night.

 

In High School I remember:

         Nixon resigning as a result of Watergate.

         Gerald Ford assuming the presidency and pardoning Nixon, which I could not believe.

         Saigon falling and losing the Vietnam War.

After the Vietnam war was lost, there were many Vietnamese people that came to the US. Several Vietnamese kids came to Greenville High. We made friends with one I remember. His last name was Ng, which is hard to pronounce, but it is a very common name, like Smith. I think I remember him talking about how they had to hide and run to get out. So while the war did not affect my life, I met someone whose life it had.

What business/economic conditions affected you?

 

 

Childhood Reflection

Do you consider your childhood to have been a happy one?

I do consider it happy. I dont remember ever being sad. I was shy and there were situations where I did not feel comfortable, but I wasnt sad.

Adulthood

 

I turned 18 in 1977 in my first semester of college, beginning my journey as an adult. Looking back, I was still very nave about so many things. I was not particularly prepared for college. I had friends mostly because of their proximity and shared school experience,, but was not social outside of that. I had hardly dated and knew very little about girls/women. I had only a vague idea what I wanted to do for a career. Perhaps this is not uncommon for eighteen year olds, and I dont blame my parents, because I truly believe they did the best they knew how to do, and given their upbringings, they had not been taught many things themselves.

I wish I had been better prepared and I would advise my younger parent self to be more aware of the need that children have to be better prepared for adulthood. In fact, looking at my parenting, I think there are more things I should have taught my children, but I was not as intentional as I should have been.

.

College

Did you go to college?

Yes, I was the first in our family on either side to go to college.

How did you decide to go to college?

Dad either chose or never had the opportunity to go to college. I recall him telling me that he was telling the kids he knew that were going to college, namely Georgia Tech, in Atlanta, that by the time they got out, he would already be ahead of them. I dont know if this was because he didnt want to go or because he didnt have the money or grades and couldnt go. But, nevertheless, he took night classes at Georgia Tech, he never got a degree. For a short time, but never got a degree.

However, as we were growing up, it seemed a forgone conclusion that we were going to college. He told me about the meetings he would go to, and even though he was the President of his own company, the people from his company and the one they were meeting with would initially exchange stories about which college they went to, what their degrees were, who they knew, stories that came to mind, etc., and how unworthy and left out he felt.

He was determined that we would have the opportunity to go. So, there was almost no doubt I would go. And there didnt even seem to be any concern about how I would get in. In hindsight, I did not have good grades, and I didnt make a high score on the SAT. I am just thankful the standards had not yet been raised.

I didnt put a lot of thought into where I would go. The choices were likely either Clemson or South Carolina. I dont think I even considered anything out of state. Not because of the money, but because my world view and ambition were so small.

How did you decide where to go to college?

Im not proud of this story. I initially decided to go to Clemson and room with a high school friend of mine. However, one night during the summer before college, I met the sister of a friend of my brother. She was already at USC, told me how great it was and that I should go there. My conviction to Clemson (and apparently my friend) was so high that I blindly and unthinkingly decided to cancel my plans to go to Clemson and go to USC. That was the depth of my ignorance. Mom and Dad didnt have any college experience to guide me, and they wanted me to go where I wanted to go. So, they allowed and assisted me.

What was your major and why?

The only major I ever considered was business because I was following a poorly planned idea to work for my fathers company when I graduated.

What were your most/least favorite college courses?

My favorites were Economics, Computing and Spanish. One of the first things I remember learning in Economics is about opportunity cost. That has had an influence on me even today. I cant say that I use it perfectly, but I am aware that everything thing we do or do not do has an opportunity cost.

I even liked psychology. My least favorite by far was math. It was horrifically boring. I was not a particularly willing student, but the teacher was also terribly boring. You have to find a way to make the material interesting. I stopped going to class a few classes in partially because it was at 8am, but also because it was so boring. I tried to read the entire book the night before the exam and managed to make a D in the class.

What college achievements are you proud of?

This is not that great, but I am proud of the fact that I went from a 2.8 my first semester to a 3.9 the second semester. There were extenuating circumstances that I tell about elsewhere that led to the turnaround. But that experience taught me the value of focus and hard work toward a goal.

How did your academic interests evolve?

When I first got to college, I had no idea how to study. That I knew of, there were no classes on studying and I was not likely looking for one either. I just showed up like I had in high school.. In my Economics

What activities did you participate in outside of college?

I did not participate in activities outside of college. I had a couple of part time jobs, that I talk about elsewhere, but I was either going to class, studying or hanging out with friends.

Who were your influential professors?

The answer to this question, is a bit complex. I didnt have many influential professors in college. That was due to my perception of how college was supposed t work. I viewed it like I had viewed all of the school. You had to take classes,. You did the work assigned, took the tests and you got a grate. I did not see it as a collaborative activity. I viewed most teachers more like an adversary than a helper. It didnt help that I was not particularly academically motivated.

In hindsight, I was just not very well prepared for college or life in general. My parents gave me every thing they possibly could have. The encouragement, the opportunity, the funding, the support, etc. But they had not been to college or operated at a higher academic level. They couldnt give me what they didnt have to give. They would have if they could have.

A professor that turn out to be influential in an accidental way, was my statistics professor. He was the only one that I developed any sort of relationship with, and that was mainly because during a test, I was having trouble with a problem and I tried to get him to help me in how to start solving the problem. He gave me hints, but he was not going to give me the answer, and after I heard the answer, I would not have known how anyway.

When I applied to graduate school, I found I needed recommendations from at least one professor. He was the only one I knew. He reluctantly agreed to give me a recommendation. I could see the surprise on his face when I asked him. Thankfully, he gave me one because I do not know who else I could have asked. But his recommendation was almost a backhanded compliment. It was something like, Alan is not one of the more intellectual students I have ever had, but he earned his A in my class through hard work. I still winch when I think about it. But it helped me get into grad school.

Did you work in college?

When I went to USC I had a couple of part-time jobs. I delivered pizzas at night for a restaurant called Chanellos. It was around for a long time before me and after me, but I think it may have closed eventually. But I would ride around listening to Billy Joel on my 8-track tape player and delivering pizzas, getting essentially nothing for tips. I think the biggest tip I ever got was $5. Usually it was $1 or $2 or the coins left over from the change. Everything was cash, so I had to have change and then deliver the cash back to the store.

The other job I had was with a t-short screen printing company. I dont remember the name of it. I would work a couple of afternoons a week preparing the screens that they used for printing the shits. The process was coating the screens with this mixture, letting them dry, then putting on the image and exposing to light for a period of time. The light would solidify the material exposed and the material not exposed to light would wash off when put under water. That would allow the ink to go through the holes in the screen onto the shirt.

For some reason, I applied for an assistantship. I think they gave me like $1,500 as a loan, but I also had to work in the computer lab working the giant printer, that was a central resource. That turned out to be a bad idea. After I graduated, I was paying $50 per month on the loan and it seemed to take forever to payoff.

No one had personal printers back then. People would submit their jobs (programs) through the card readers and the printouts would come to the central printer. I would tear off each print out and stack it on the counter. Students would come pick up the printout and sometimes ask for programming help.

When I went to Clemson, I did not work.

Did you join a fraternity in college?

When I first went to USC a girlfriend from high school of mines brother was in a fraternity, and he invited me to the parties and later called to offer me to join. But I was very introverted, didnt know enough about fraternities, and was intimidated. Also, I have three roommates that were not being invited to the parties, so they were anti-fraternity. I called him back to decline the offer. He was very surprised and tried to convince me, but I was just too unsure.

Ironically, when I transferred to Clemson, I went to the parties and eventually joined a fraternity--Kappa Sigma--the same fraternity that had offered me at USC.

What memories do you have of college?

Move-In

My parents helped me move to Columbia and into the dorm the first semester. When I walked into the room for the first time, there was only one other roommate (out of the four of us) moved in. I happened to look at his desk and there was a bag of marijuana rolled up. I dont think my parents saw it. They might not have known what it looked like anyway. But that was an interesting start to college.

First Night

A little while after we got my stuff moved in, we said our goodbyes. I was a little bit nervous, but at the same time I was "in college"!!

I called one of my friends who was also going there--and he knew some other people. We got together and all went to a place called Chanello's for pizza and beer.

Coincidentally, it was my 18th birthday. It was the first time I had been able to legally drink beer. (The drinking age was 18 back then.) We had a great time the first night.

That was my first night in college and away from my parents' house. I would go back for summer's but never totally moved back in.

First Dorm

I lived in Woodrow, the second row off the quad in the center of campus. I had three roommates. There were two bedrooms with bunks and desks in each for 2 people and then a large den room that had a sink and a mirror. There was no cabinetry. Just a sink attached to the wood paneling with the underneath plumbing exposed.

Scheduling

Today, I think scheduling classes takes place completely online. Back then, there were two days scheduled at the basketball coliseum where either professors or their assistants would sit at tables, and based on the classes we needed to graduate, we had to find and walk to every table and try to sign up for the class.

There were hundreds of tables all around the walkways of the coliseum, upstairs, downstairsall over. It was a zoo. You had to choose the days (MWF or TTH) and the times. If a class was already full, you had to put your name on the wait list, in case someone dropped the class later, and go find a replacement class. It literally took two days.

The Bookstore

Buying books was as crazy as scheduling. You would have a list of books required from each class and go to the store and search through the store packed with students and books piled in large stacks all around the store.
