Relationships

 

When was your first girlfriend?

I did not have many girlfriends growing up. In the fourth grade I exchanged I like you, Do you lie me notes with Frieda. My first official girlfriend was in the sixth grade.

When was your first kiss?

In the sixth grade, 1971, I liked a girl named Valerie Klengson. She was from Minnesota, had an interesting accent, was pretty and outgoing.

Valerie was the first girl I ever kissed. She was from Minnesota and had moved down to Taylors, SC. She had an accent from there. I had never kissed a girl. But apparently, I was not her first. She was very outgoing, and surprise, I wasnt. I still remember what a strange sensation it was to kiss a girl. First on the lips and then touching tongues.

Spin the Bottle

One day after school she and another friend and his girlfriend went home to his house and we played spin the bottle in the woods. It was just an excuse to be able to kiss, and that is as far as it went.

Unavoidable Fight

One day at lunch, she and our other friends had gone outside, and I was finishing lunch. One of my friends came running in and said that this kid named 'Tandy' was picking on Valerie. At first, I wanted to ignore it because Tandy was kind of a troublemaker, and I didn't really want to get involved. But, the kid said I had to go. It made me feel guilty, so I went out there. It was on the front lawn of the school. I dont remember exactly what he was saying or doing to her. Probably just saying things to her. I went up to him and told him to stop bothering her. Of course, he turned to me and asked what I was going to do about it. I said, just leave her alone. He said something like, "Make me." and pushed me. I have not been in many fights in my life. Maybe 3 or 4. And I have always been very reluctant to fight. I avoided it as long as possible. But if pushed, when my trigger gets pulled, I would just go off on whoever was taunting me. That happened with Tandy, I just lit into him. I hit him two or three times and then he started running away. And he never bothered me or Valerie again.

First Disappointment

I bought her a gold ring with her initials on it. I think maybe it was supposed to have my initials on it but I didnt know any better. But it turned her finger green and she stopped wearing it. Near the end of the school year there was a party. She broke up with me at the party and that was about as bad as I had ever felt until then. When my mother came to pick me up, there there was a popular song on the radio called Dont Pull Your Love by Hamilton, Joe Frank and Reynolds. One of the lines was, Dont pull your love out on me, baby, If you do then I think that maybe, Ill just lay me down and cry for a hundred years. Thats how I felt.

How did you meet your wife?

We met in college. I was sitting behind her in statistics. I thought she was attractive. She had long blonde hair and the seats were so close I could smell her hair. I got my nerve up and invited her to one of our fraternity parties.

What is your definition of love?

I have thought a lot about this question over the years.

In my study of the mind and beliefs, I came to the idea that everything we do is for the survival or validation of the self. I believe that love is taking someone as a part of oneself. And as a result, you act in the best interest of that person or persons for their survival or validation.

For example, doing things for others can be self-satisfying, but it can also mean sacrificing what one might want for the benefit of the other. I have certainly felt that about my children and my parents. I am not just willing to sacrifice for them, I want to sacrifice for them, if something I can do will benefit them.

Sometimes in relationships, especially early in relationships, love can be confused with getting what one wants from another person. Looking at what the relationship can do for them in any number of ways.

But, in my opinion, love is about caring and sharing. Caring for oneself and the other person and being willing to and wanting to compromise for the benefit of the other and the relationship between them.

This balance is different for different people. Sometimes the balance will be 50/50, other times will be 20/80, 10/90, maybe even 0/100. And other times it might be the other way around. It doesnt necessarily have to always balance out.

But whatever the distribution, it has to ultimately satisfy both people. If things average 75/25 or 25/75 and both are satisfied with that, then that is the right balance. But if one person likes the balance and the other one doesnt, that is going to lead to problems.

So, my definition of love is caring and sharing for another as yourself..

What was it like the first time you fell in love?

I dont know if it was really love, but I remember sending love notes to a girl in the fourth grade. They were the typical, I like you. Do you like me? with Yes and No check boxes. Haha! Thankfully I didnt get a no, or I would have been crushed.

Another time I was about 14 and went the Six Flags with a girl with her parents. On the way home we held hands in the back seat and my stomach was doing somersaults every few minutes the entire way home. We lived far apart and went to different schools so that didnt go anywhere.

The first semi-serious girlfriend I had was in the summer of 1977 before I went to college and my first semester. She was going into her senior year, and I had just graduated. I think I was partially holding on to something at home as I went off to college that I was unsure about, but I was head over heels about her. She was so sweet. She gave me an unexpected Just because gift. Her eyes were beautiful and they gleamed when she smiled. I wrote her letters from school. I came home almost every weekend the first semester. She came down to one football game at USC.

One night I was at her house getting ready to go back to my house before going back to school the next morning. We were sitting on her porch, and she told me she wanted to break up. I was so infatuated I did not see it coming and it hit me like a truck. I was really devastated. Of course, whatever I tried to change her mind just made it worse. I only learned later having been on the other side, that once it has gone that far, there is no going back. The other person has just moved on, and the more you do, the worse you feel about yourself.

In a way it was the worst thing that had ever happened, but in another way it was one of the best.

The first semester, at least partially because I was going home so much, I made a 2.8 GPA. After she broke up with me, I threw myself into school and working out. The next semester I made a 3.9 (should have been a 4.0 but this marketing professor from Europe that literally wore the same suit every single day to class and apparently didnt shower all semester wouldnt give me the 1 point that I needed for an A.)

On the positive side, the devastation focused me on myself and my school work.

I also worked out and was in the best shape of my life. I had a routine. I would get up early for classes. I scheduled all of my classes back-to-back. As soon as class was over, Id go work out, play basketball, punch the speed bag, shower, eat in the cafeteria then go to the library until about 11pm. Then Id go home and go to bed and do the exact same thing the next day.

Some good came from it, That discipline helped me tremendously from then on. but I really think that experience scarred me and affected all of my relationships afterwards. I had been so blindsided, that I was always hyper concerned about it happening again. It probably led me to behave in ways that were defensive and not always the best.

Have you ever had your heart broken?

What is your idea of perfect happiness?

I would not have been able to answer this question up until recently. I have even read books being happy and none of them seemed to help. It probably sounds clich, but happiness is not something that happens from the outside. In terms I developed in MentalEdge, happiness is when you can value yourself as you are, accepting the past as a blessing or a lesson, confidence in the future as a blessing or a lesson and gratitude for either. You can always strive for achievement, but not as validation or yourself, but rather just from the enjoyment of the challenge and the accomplishment.

That said, happiness is also seeing those you love happy.

What was one of the most romantic moments in your life?

One of the most romantic moments of my life was in the mountains of Colorado at night in a hot tub outdoors on the porch of a hotel room overlooking the mountains with the full moon reflecting off the snow and the water and steam rising looking across at a woman I deeply loved and I knew deeply loved me.

What do you think are the secrets to a happy relationship?

Under the circumstances, Im not sure I would be the one to ask this question, but the circumstances have led me to think quite a lot about relationships and how they can be happy.

I share this is another story, but after all of the ins and outs I think it comes down to two people willing to and wanting to be caring and sharing with each other. Circumstances are never going to be always 50/50. They will range from 0/100 to 100/0 and every split in between. And whatever the average split turns out to be, each has to be content with it. If its 75/25 in your favor, both have to be content. If its 25/75 in the other partys favor, both have to be content. If one or the other is not content with how things are going, it leads to trouble. What helps each be content with whatever the balance is commitment to sharing and caring. Sharing with the other person and caring about what the other person is experiencing.

How have love relationships influenced you?

I am sorry to say that love relationships have led me to be so cautious as to not allow myself to give into them for the fear of the pain of rejection or their negative outcome.

I think it goes back to that relationship I had leading into my freshman year at Carolina. I was hit so totally unexpecting, that it has caused my to try and retain control of the situation even when it shouldnt be. If it is going to end, I want to protect myself against such colossal devastation.

I have also toughened my heart to relatively easily not care, and purge myself of any feelings I may have had for that person almost completely. It almost sounds pathological. It may be.

 

Politics

 

How would you describe your politics?

I believe that the government should be of the people, by the people, for the people. But the more you observe how people operate and how governments operate, you see more and more of the genius that the very young founders had in setting up the government. It has withstood attacks for almost 250 years.

Still, I think we have strayed very far from what the founders intended. Neither party represents the people. I am hopeful that Trump and those he brings in will be able to do something to permanently alter the balance of power back toward the people and rid the government of a significant portion of the corruption. But I am not nave enough to believe that it will ever be ideal.

However, there is a danger in that also, because crowd mentality is not always the most wise. .

Which Presidents have you voted for and why?

  • 1980 Jimmy Carter (D) vs Ronald Reagan (R)

The first presidential election I could vote in after turning 18 in 1977 was 1980. I voted for Jimmy Carter because I was nave, didnt see the error of his decisions and thought he was kinder and more empathetic to the people. Unfortunately, he turned out to be the worst president in history until Obama triumphantly stole that title later and then Biden exceeded even that low point after Trump. I was too young and nave and unfamiliar with the ways of the world. Carter stoked inflation and much of his term was marred by the failed Iran Hostage Crisis that lasted over a year. He gave away the Panama Canal. I turned decidedly conservative and as a result Republican, although I still had issues with them.

  • 1984 Walter Mondale (D) vs Ronald Reagan (R)

I voted for Reagan because of his success with Iran and improvement in the economy. Reagan had made some deal behind the scenes and within days after the election, the hostages were freed, which made Carter look even worse.

  • 1988 Michael Dukakis (D) vs George H. Bush (R)

I voted for Bush because he had been vice president under Reagan and Dukakis was a lunatic. Only found out later how corrupt Bush was.

  • 1992 Bill Clinton (D) vs George H. Bush (R)

I voted for Bush because he was VP under Reagan and thought policies would stay the same or improve.

  • 1996 Bill Clinton (D) vs Bob Dole (R)

I voted for Ross Perot because I didn't like Clinton or Dole. Perot was a small, whiny voiced rich guy, that I thought had the ability to make things different. Looking back, this may have been when the massive cheating started. It could have been sooner, but the Clintons brought in a despicable era.

  • 2000 Al Gore (D) vs George W. Bush (R)

I voted for Bush because Gore was a leftist redneck. The election was contested over voting irregularities and hanging chads. Ultimately the Supreme court stepped in and stopped the suit and Bush was declared the winner.

  • 2004 John Kerry (D) vs George W. Bush (R)

I voted for Bush, still not realizing how stupid and corrupt he was. He instigated the war against Iraq claiming there were weapons of mass destruction, which he knew there were not. This further destabilization of the middle east spread millions of refugees around the world taking their beliefs with them and are the seed of many of the problems the receiving countries are experiencing.

  • 2008 Barack Obama(D) vs John McCain (R)

I voted for Obama with his promises of hope and change, which immediately turned out to be a lie. He was worse than Carter on policy and more corrupt than any president, probably including Biden. He just didnt get caught. Again, in hindsight. he was not born in the US and was never eligible. The media lied to cover it up.

  • 2012 Barack Obama (D) Mitt Romney (R)

I voted or Romney because I saw Obama was the fraud. I voted for Romney because I had seen that Obama was a disaster.

  • 2016 Hillary Clinton (D) vs Donald Trump (R)

I voted for Trump because Clinton is a non-prosecuted criminal. The democrat fraud machine was in full swing during this election, they just didn't have enough fraud to overcome the movement for Trump.

  • 2020 Joe Biden (D) vs Donald Trump (R)

I voted for Trump. The election was riggedno question. The democrat fraud machine stopped voting in the middle of the night and injected millions of votes and managed to steal the election with a few thousand vote margin in some key states. The extent of the corruption will eventually come out, but far too late.

  • 2024 Kamala Harris (D) vs Donald Trump (R)

I voted for Trump. Thankfully the cheating was held at bay.

How have your political opinions changed over time?

I heard something once that said, if you are a young person and you are not a liberal you have no heart. If you are an older person and not a conservative, you have no brain.

That might describe my evolution. While I have always considered my self conservative, I have leaned liberal on certain issues. I leaned toward Carter and at times when I thought it might help people in general (Obama), but those exceptions did not help. The results were worse than the predecessors.

Overall, I am a conservative, but I still recognize that the excesses of capitalism are not good overall for the people.

 

Sports

 

How have sports influenced your life?

Sports have been apart of my life as either participation or entertainment since very early. Our participation was a factor in why we moved from Taylors to Greenvile.

Football

I started playing football at the YMCA at about 8 years old and played through my 10th grade.

However, every year the season would come around, we didnt want to play, because we were just being lazy. But Dad would insist we go to practice and after a practice or two we would be back into it.

At first, Mom would drive us to practice across town. But eventually Dad moved us to across the street from the YMCA so we could just walk.

After practice wed come back after dark and really eat. We could put away some food. I remember opening the refrigerator and chugging almost a quarter gallon of milk from the jug and putting it back. Mom didnt like that very much.

Baseball

I started playing baseball a li

Basketball

Basketball has never been my favorite sport. I think I might have been on 1 YMCA team and a church team, but I didnt play long.

Swimming

I was never on a swim team, but I learned to swim at the YMCA. I took lessons and was expecting to earn the first beginner level, which was something like Guppy. I was pleasantly surprised when I earned the next level upthe Minnow!

Golf

First Experience

My first exposure to golf was going with Dad to Donaldson Air Force base. It had its own golf course. I was very young. Maybe 6-8. He let me pull the golf clubs in the pull cart. The only thing I remember is following him with the cart as he walked onto the green. When he realized I was pulling the cart onto the green, he quickly let me know I needed to leave the cart on the side. I didnt know any better and it was my first exposure to golf etiquette.

First Play

When I was 12, Dad got a membership at Ramsgate Country Club and he allowed me to play. Mom would drive me there in the morning and drop me off, sometimes with my brothers and other times by myself. Wed play all day and she would come pick us up.

I Wasnt Very Good

I was not very good. I had a big slice like most beginning golfers. One day, Greg was caddying for me. I hit a bad shot and tossed the club backward and said, Throw that club in the woods. And started walking toward my ball. I heard something rattling into the woods. I whipped around thinking Greg had thrown my club, but he had just thrown some rocks to make me think he had! I deserved that.

The Monster Snake

One day on the second hole I had hit my ball into this area near a river and I went to find it. I found my ball and was climbing up the face of this almost vertical grass wall so I didnt have to walk further backward to get out an easier way.

The face of the wall was about 2 feet in front of me. I reached to grab some grass a little higher to pull myself up and through the grass saw about a foots worth of snake about 6-8 inches wide, meaning it was either going up the hill or down the hill. It was huge. I didnt know how much of the snake was above or below me, so I just jumped backward off the wall down about 8 to 10 feet. Luckily, I landed in sand, and then scurried out the longer way. I never went back in that area for balls again.

Scavenger for Golf Balls

Golf balls are expensive, especially when you are first learning and losing a lot of them. I never had to buy golf balls because I would go find balls where others had lost them.

Some days I would go to the course and instead of playing, I would walk into the woods are areas where people would lose their balls. I once even waded into a water hazard up to my neck feeling for balls with my feet.

I would find dozens of practically brand new balls. For some reason, I would carry them around in my bag, which made it much heavier than it needed to be.I think that is why I have stiffness in my right hip, because I wore it down with the excess weight over so many years.

Greenville Country Club

Some time later, Dad left Ramsgate and joined Greenville Country Club. This is where I spent most of my free time after that.

My Only Sport

After my sophomore year in high school, I gave up all other sports for golf. I loved it and played all the time. I would play every day in the summer. I even played starting in the pouring rain with no umbrella. Many days I played 54 holes, walking, carrying my own bag. I started as soon as it was light enough to see the ball and only stopped when it wasnt.

Golf is a Valuable Skill

Golf has been such a valuable skill both for the enjoyment and the engagement with other business people. Business naturally revolves around golf and when you can play reasonably well, it helps with those relationships.

Did you ever want to be a professional athlete?

I never wanted to be a professional athlete in sports until golf. I wish there had been the training programs for golfers when I was learning like there are today. I had a package of 10 lessons when I was about 15 or 16 years old, and that has been it. With coaching I could have been better. How much better well never know. But I do know that what the professionals can do is so far above what even a scratch amateur golfer can do. The level is incredibly high.

What was your favorite sport?

Golf.

What was your favorite sports team?

While it didnt start out that way, Clemson has been my favorite team. I started out a Carolina fan because thats where I went to school. And when I transferred to Clemson, my transition did not happen right away. I didnt like it that Clemson won the first year I was at Clemson. But, I did transition and with Clemson winning the national Championship in my senior year, that cemented the Tigers as my favorite team.
I have never been much of a professional sports fan. I liked the Falcons when we lived in Atlanta, but I was a fair weather fan.

What was your favorite player of all time?

When I was a teenager, my favorite was Johnny Miller. He was a young phenom. But I would have to say Tiger Woods took over that position.. He was absolutely superman on the golf course. The shots he made when he had to make them have to be some of the greatest that will ever occur. I dont think people appreciate today how dominant he was. Heres a video of Tiger Woods 20 Greatest Moments. The problem is the top 20 is not enough to capture his awesomeness.

Many say that Jack Nicklaus is the greatest golfer to ever play. He won 18 majors to Tigers 15 and he came in second 19 times to Tigers 6. Some say that the equipment and course conditions differences suggest Nicklaus did it with inferior equipment and tougher courses. However, while there were a few other top golfers like Arnold Palmer, Lee Trevino and Tom Weiskopf, Tiger was competing with players that had been better trained. I would have to concede Nicklaus is the winningest (and probably the better gentleman), but Tiger is the GOAT for the excitement he brought to the game. It is a lesser game without him now.

What sporting event would you most like to attend?

I would love to attend the British Open. I have been to the Masters, and I would love going there again anytime.

What is your favorite sporting event attended?

Masters

My first professional sporting event was the Masters on Sunday in 1975. Jack Nicklaus, Johnny Miller and Tom Weiskopf battled on that last day, with Nicklaus winning his 5th Masters. Weiskopf and Miller tied for second one shot behind.

As most people did, I wore my golf shoes for traction walking up hills. Back then, they had metal spikes. We were standing in a crowd of people and a guy backed up and bumped into me making me take a step back. I stepped on a womans foot wearing sandals and one of my spikes dug into the fat part of her little toe! I felt so bad.

French Open

In 1995, I was in Paris on business with Lanier helping buy a dealership there. I woke up on Sunday and saw in the newspaper that the French Open was being played. I took the subway to the stadium. Negotiated for a ticket outside the gate. Had a midcourt seat reasonably close to the court and watched Michael Chang beat Stefan Edberg in the final 6-1, 6-4, 6-2. The tennis is played on clay and that was fun to watch. I was proud of myself for negotiating the city and event in French.

Is there a sporting event you remember as a kid?

I have very vague memories of going to a Clemson football game as part of a YMCA trip. I remember nothing about the game at all. Some vague memories of walking around the stadium and when the game was over, everyone went down on the field. The players seemed gigantic. The kids that I went with were experienced and knew to ask the players for their sweat bands or chinstraps. I was too shy to ask.

What is your favorite sports movie?

Id have to say my first and favorite is the first Rocky movie (1976). I was in high school and remember walking out of the theater so revved up. The theme song Gonna Fly Now is always motivating.

Miracle (2004) about the 1980 USA hockey team winning gold medal is motivating.

Field of Dreams (1989) is interesting in how it brings the past to the present.

For golf, my favorites are:

Caddy Shack (1980)

Tin Cup (1996)

Happy Gilmore (1996)

 

Cars

 

What was your first car?

My first car is not the greatest of memories. When I first got my license, Dad gave me a car that he had been driving before he got a new one. This was about 1975, and it was an 8-year old, 1967, white Cadillac Sedan de Ville with a black vinyl top. It was huge. And, it had something wrong with a spring or something in the front-end suspension. When I would go over a bump that pressed the wheel and axel arm upward, it would catch on to something and when it would come back down and release, it made this terrible 'bong' sound. To me, as a young high school kid, it was very embarrassing.

Gas Money

Dad gave me $5 per week for gas, which was $0.57/gallon. It got 9 miles per gallon! 60 miles a week.

Stolen Battery

Before I was a senior and able to park in the senior lot that was within the school gates, I had to park on the street. The area around the school was fairly dangerous. One day, I came out of school to go home, and found someone had stolen the battery! This was before hood locks.

First Accident

I used to pick up my friends on the way to school. One winter morning, the back window was iced over, because it didnt have a defroster, and I didnt scrape it. I picked up my friend, and backing out of his driveway, I hit the neighbors car that was parked on the street. I didnt get out and look. I got scared and left.

When I got to school, I looked at my car, and the entire rear bumper was bent up in a V-shape. When I got home, I didnt say anything. I just parked it in the driveway, hoping maybe no one would notice. When Dad got home, the first thing he asked was what happened to the car? Im embarrassed to say that I lied and told him I didnt know. That someone at school must have hit me. I could tell he wasnt sure he could believe me, but he dropped it.

After a few days, I could not stand the lie. I got up early and drove to the man's house whose car I had hit. I rang his doorbell. When he came to the door, I explained that I had backed out and hit his car. We went out to look at it, and there was no damage. He thanked me for telling him and told me not to worry about it. Then I drove back home, went into my father's bathroom where he was shaving and explained what I had done. He was standing in front of the mirror with his foot up on the counter as he used to do and he really didnt react. He just continued shaving and looking at me as he rinsed the razor. He might have already known I was not telling the truth. He thanked me for telling the truth. I walked out and he continued shaving. I got my stuff together and went to school.

The End of My First Car

Some time later, on one of the nights we used to get together as friends and drive around, (There wasnt much else to do at the time.), we decided to switch cars and let the other drive their car. I drove my friends VW beetle and he drove my Cadillac Sedan de Ville. I should have known better. He was a wild man, and he drove it going too fast over a dip and hump in a driveway, slammed the underneath into the road and broke the engine block and the radiator. I pulled up to the place we met to swap back and there was steam rising from the entire front end. That was the end of the Ville.

Second Car

My second car was a Mercury Capri. My friend and I found it on a used car lot. It had a modified exhaust system and it was loud. I went home and told my Dad about it and the next weekend we went to the lot to look at it. I test drove it and loved it. It was a manual transmission, which means you had to use a clutch and change the gears. I really liked revving the engine up in each gear and shifting to the next. Then downshifting to as I slowed down. The altered exhaust system really accentuated the sound. I was shocked when he agreed to buy it for me.

I didnt get a another car right away. One day my friend and I went to a dealership to look at used cars. We found this 1972 (think) Mercury Capris. It was manual transmission and the exhaust had been modified to be very loud. I told Dad about it. He took us up there and ended up buying it for me. I loved it! I took great care of it. I washed it and waxed all the time. Cleaned the interior. As cars used to do back then, the brakes made a terrible squeal, even when not breaking. It would just squeal all the time. We of course didnt have the internet ack then, but somehow probably by asking a dealer and talking to an auto parts store, figured out there was this spray rubber you could put on the back of the brake pads that was supposed to help. So I pulled into the garage. Jacked it up, took off the wheels and break pads, put the spray on the pads and reinstalled them. In hindsight, I surprised I did this, and am glad I got them back on correctly. It helped a little, but not much.

I drove that car for a couple of years. I would work on it when it needed to be worked on. I tuned it up. Which means I had to adjust the gap in the spark plugs and the gap in the distributor cap. Cars dont have distributor caps anymore and rarely need tune-ups. When my brake pads started squealing. Brake pads don't do that anymore either, but I took off all four wheels. Removed the brake pads and applied this rubber spray product that was supposed to stop the squealing. It didn't do much but looking back. I was pretty handy to do that myself. One day I took all the seats out of the car for some reason. I think I was just cleaning it really well. When I had the seats out my friend suggested we go see how fast it would go. So we drove over to this long straight back road. I left the driver seat in it but he sat on the metal floor. I think we ended up getting close to 100 mph before I took my foot off the gas. Terribly dangerous in hindsight, but it was a fun car.

How did you learn to drive?

My Dad taught me to drive, and I learned to drive in a Pontiac station wagon. It was long and wide and hard to drive. On one of our test drives, Dad was in the passenger seat, and we were approaching some road work. There were orange barrels setup blocking part of the lane and there were cars to my left with no room to change lanes. As we approached, Dad thought I was going to hit them. He was telling me to stop, pulling his feet up and leaning away from the barrels, but I didnt. I kept going and just barely missed them. I looked over and he was all twisted in his seat trying to use his body to help me miss the barrels.

I took my first drivers test in the station wagon and failed. It was so long and wide that I couldnt make a three point turn and I couldnt get it in the parallel parking space. That was so disappointing. But I went back and practiced and made it on the second try.

Later, Dad had bought a Triumph Spitfire as one of his toys. It had a manual transmission, meaning you had to manually change the gears using a clutch pedal. Mom taught me how to drive it while Dad was at work. Knowing how to drive a manual transmission came in handy later.

The Firebird

My next car has a story I dont think I ever told my dad. I was a senior in high school. Not the best story, but on Friday nights we would get together with friends, get some beer from somewhere (we were not 18 at the time, which was the legal age). And we would hang out at Petes or someones house or just sit in the car somewhere. Sometimes, wed go to the country clubs driveway.

One day, after one of our nights out, I was lying on the floor in the den watching tv, probably football. Dad came into the room with a dour look on his face and motioned for me to come with him. I wasnt too concerned, but puzzled. As I followed him, I could tell he was headed for the backdoor toward the driveway where our cars were parked. I suddenly remembered that I still had a Styrofoam cooler in my trunk with a few left-over beers. I was panic stricken. I assumed he had found it and was taking me to ask me about it. My mind was racing.

Well, he reached the back door, opened it and started out. He stopped to hold the door so I could come out. As I stepped out of the doorway, he nodded toward the driveway. I looked down and saw the attached picture. He surprised me with a new car for my high school graduation! I had never looked at other cars or even mentioned wanting another one I dont think. But it was perfect. That car became my all time favorite.

My favorite car was my Pontiac Firebird. One afternoon, I was lying on the floor watching television and my Dad came in and motioned for me to come with him, with a solemn look on his face. I immediately thought I was in trouble for something. I hopped up and started behind him. He walked toward the back door and turned to make sure I was coming. He walked partially out the door and stood there, as if he wanted me to come out with him. When I did, he looked down at the driveway and then I looked. Sitting in the driveway was a baby blue 1977 Pontiac Firebird. It had a bow on it and a sign. I could not believe it. I went from being afraid I was in trouble to instant ecstasy. It was a great car. It had a white vinyl top on it. Every few weeks I would wash it and wax it. I had to scrub off the old wax from the vinyl and then put a new coat on. It had an 8-track tape player, which I loved, but eventually replaced and added new speakers and an equalizer. I drove that car all through the rest of high school, which was about a year, and then all through college. Every year, I would pack it to the gills to go to school and then pack it again to come home. My first year in college we took it on a road trip to New Orleans with two friends for Mardi Gras. We took a road trip to University of Georgia. I drove it to deliver pizzas for a company called Chanelo's. I still remember listening to Billy Joel's 8-track tape of his album 52nd Street as I drove back and forth from the pizza place to dorms and houses around campus. When I got a new car for graduation, I was sad to be leaving such a great car with so many high school and college memories.

Audi

When I graduated from Clemson, Dad gave me an Audi. I was so cost and environment conscious that I wanted a deisel engine. The car was nice, but only a 4 cylinder and manual transmission. I t was very slow.

One weekend I stopped for gas before heading back home. After I filled it up, I realized that I had filled it with regular gas. I had to pay about $50 to get the gas drained and then replace it with diesel. Had I driven it, it would have ruined the engine. This was before they changed the size of the nozzles (making the deisel nozzles bigger)because so many people were doing this.

I rove that car for at least 10 years and then I think I either gave it to Scot or charged him a small amount. He drove it for several years after that. It was a good car.

When I got rid of the Audi, I drove Mammas Buick Regal for a while.

Then I went to leasing cars. I had at lease 3 Maximas, at least three Infiniti G37s.

In Europe I had a company car. It was an Audi also but gasoline.

After the Infinitis I started leasing BMMMMMMMMMWs. I thin I had a 64 and andt least 2 540s before buying the 540 I have now.

Nissan Maxima

Buick Regal

Infiniti G35

 

Infiniti G37

 

 

What car trouble have you had?

I have had surprisingly few car quality and or repair issues. I have run out of gas probably at least 3 or 4 times, before I stopped trying to run it all the way to empty before filling it up. At the time, I thought it was a way to save cash flow, but it is such an insignificant anout that it really doesnt pay.

What accidents have you had?

Thankfully, I have had relatively few accidents. My first accident was in the 196 Cadillac. I backed into a car parked on the street when picking up my friends fo high school, and I rear-ended a guy at a yield sign. It was a bad intersection and people did it all the time. The car in fron of my stopped, looked back and then seemed to be proceeding, so I moved forward and started look back for traffic. The guy in front stopped and I hit him.

The Station Wagon

It wasnt an accident, but it was almost one. I was driving my monthers station wagon with Ashley. It had been raining and I was using the shigeter on the steering collar to change gears from 1 to 2 to 3 to D. Just as I hit D, we must have hit a uddle of water ad we hydroplaned, spun around backwards. I was turned around looking out the back window to see where we were going, We crossed the oncoming lane and thankfully no one was there. Then we came to a stop at the stop sign for one of the intersecting streets. On either side of the road was a10-foot stone wall . We had missed the wall and come to a stop as if we had been coming out of the side street. I stopped doing that.

Thanksgiving Deer

In 2021, I was leaving Atlanta early to visit the kis in Nashville for Thanskging Day. It was pitch black when all ofa sudden my lights picked up a deer jumptin in front of the car. I hit is full speed. I managed to drive to an intersctiion with a gas station and lights to find that the entire front end had been demolished and the radiator was leaking. I was not going to be driving to Nashville in that car. Icalled William and managed to get him to drive my for the weekend. That is the worst accident I have had.

Poor Dog

I still remember and incident on my way back to Carolina one night. I was folling a car when suddenly his light caught the shape of a dog. He was standing in the emergency lane but with just his head over the line into the lane. The car hit it and sent it spinning down the road and off to the side. It made me feel sick the rest of the trip. Poor dog.i

 

Moves

 

What moves have you made?

It wasnt until I started answering this question that I realized how many time I have moved., especially in college.

Then I moved back to Columbia for 2 years while I was in graduate school. Started in a house with 3 other guys. Then when I came back from internship, we rented an apartment. When I graduated, I was going to move back to Greenville and look for a job, but I was offered a job with the University, so we moved to another apartment in Columbia.

In about 1984, we bought a house in Columbia, on Linbrook Dr.

In 1988, right after Elizabeth was born, we moved to Atlanta. We rented an apartment until the house we bought and built was ready.

In 1990, we moved to Belgium.

In 1993 we move back from Belgium.

In 2000, we bought and built another house in Atlanta in Edgewater, living in another apartment while it was being built.

In 2007, we bought and built another house in Atlanta, in Gates at Luberon.

In 2022, I moved to Nashville to be closer to family.

 

Vacations

 

Wow, What a Pool!

We were in Jacksonville when we were small. Greg must have been 5 or 6. So I would have been 8 or 9. Uncle Toby and Aunt Nell took us all to the beach. I dont know if we had ever been to a beach. Greg was riding on Uncle Tobys shoulders, and as they crested the sand dunes, Greg said, Wow, what a pool! Uncle Toby enjoyed that quite a bit.

Glad you got to meet me!

Speaking of Uncle Toby, he was a big man, but he was one of the kindest that you would ever meet. When we would leave, he would say, Glad you got to meet me! Come back when you cant stay so long! Still makes me smile.

         Breckenridge

         LakeTahoe With the Knauses. So much snow the slopes were closed.

North Carolina

Sugar Mountain When I was going to Carolina, I went with the girl that had convinced me to go to USC to Sugar Mountain for night skiing. It was so icy, you really couldnt call it skiing. On one of the runs, she lost her ski and it went down into a ravine. I had to climb down and get it because the rental was on my license.

Beech Mountain

 

Winterplace, West Virginia

 

The Beach

The beach has been one of our favorite vacation spots.

The first I remember about the beach is that sensation you get when you are standing near the shore and the waves are rushing back out. It feels like it is sucking back out to sea with it.

Body Surfing

From flimsy plastic blow up floats to serious canvas covered air mattress, to Styrofoam boards made for the task, body surfing was always part of the beach routine. All the failed attempts were worth it if you caught one that rode you all the way into the shore.

Vacations with the Meltons

Ted would rent a house at the beach each year and we would all go down together. So many memories. Being chased away by a hurricane.

Myrtle Monsters

Kyle and Robin, Kim and Jimmy, Kerri and I went out together to see a beach music band (I dont remember their names) at a place in Myrtle Beach. We got there early and ordered the specialty drink--Myrtle Monsters. After two rounds, Kyle and I looked at each other and didnt feel we were getting the effect we were looking for, so Kyle ordered a round of tequila shots. Alan ordered a round. Jimmy ordered another. The effect kicked in. Jimmy ended up on stage singing with the band. momma wrote me a letter. We stumbled home and gathered outside on the porch trying to get our acts together before we walked in with the rest of the family. Kim walked in first, and with no questions being asked stated something like, If you think Im bad, you should see the rest of them! We all got a great laugh out of that one. I spent the entire next day in bed.

Bachelor Party

I was in grad school and there were two other guys scheduled to get married. We decided to have a joint bachelor party at our house. It was a fairly large open area, and we must have had 30 or 40 guys there. We had music and drinks. And, in full transparency, someone had planned for a stripper. I can still picture everyone sitting or standing around the sides of the room as this barely attractive woman danced in the center. It was fairly benign, and we were a bunch of young nave kids. She left and nothing else happened. By the end of the night, I was drinking bourbon and orange juice. Another time I spent the next day in bed.

Grilling Shark

One year, Jimmy Hallman and I went to the seafood shop to get something for dinner. We stumbled across shark steaks and we decided to try them. They have to be soaked in water to remove the urea, because sharks are so ancient, they dont have a system of removing the toxins from their bodies. We told everyone it was Grouper so they would try it and only told them after they tried it.

Wake Boarding

One of our pastimes was to wakeboard along the shore. We would spend hours running along the waters edge dropping the board and leaping aboard for as long a ride as we could manage. Some were awesome glides for 20 or 30 yards. Others were faceplants in the sand. But always fun. The next day we would always be sore.

College Spring Break with Eddie Memmot Daytona Beach

Egg toss. Schlitz ball.

Road Trip to Daytona in the Saab

Clemson Football Games

Clemson football games while in a fraternity are always an event. Where, at Carolina, people might go with one or two friends. A fraternity gets a block of seats together, so you were with all of your friends. The day would start early, first with getting dressed, at times even wearing a tie. Sometimes the fraternity would hold a cookout. Other times, there would be tailgating with family or friends, but it was always a party

 

Technology

 

How has technology influenced your life?

It is truly amazing how fast technology has changed across a number of areas in what seems like the short time of my life. The things that we thought were revolutionary have been revolutionized over and over again. Not only have technology changes affected my life in the use of the products, but it has affected my career.

I was always the first to want to experiment with and adopt technology. When personal computers first came out, Dad bought an Osborne and a Compaq. I experimented with VisiCalc and learned to operate a spreadsheet relatively early. I even wrote a program in Basic that I showed my professor at USC. I helped Dads business implement a computerized accounting system. In my internship, I helped a team program an accounting system. At Lanier, I figured out how to send escape codes to the idle laser printer so people could begin using it. Also, at Lanier the first What You See Is What You Get (WYSIWIG) graphical user interfaces for spreadsheets became available, and I was the pioneer in figuring out its uses and sharing with others. I built consolidation and reporting systems on new applications. I implemented the first financial analysis package at Lanier and later took the same technology to McKesson.

In the late 90s software companies were booming, and I left Lanier to join one in the hopes of participating in the run. When I left Caribiner, I was looking to get into technology and healthcare, which were booming industries at the time and found McKesson, a natural combination of the two. I used technology to improve controls and analysis capabilities of the company.

What inventions have had the biggest impact on your day-to-day life?

At first glance, it would be hard not to say that the computer, software, the internet, and now Artificial Intelligence (AI) have been the most impactful, but cellphone communication, air travel is far safer,

Music

When I was very young, the only way to listen to music was on records. Records were made of vinyl. Somehow the music was recorded into the plastic, and it was read with a needle made of diamond. Records were made to be played at different speeds. 45 were typically one song on each side and the rotations per minute or RPM had to be set at 45. Albums were larger records that had multiple songs recorded on both sides. Albums were played at 33 1/3. Some had to be played at 78 RPM and were called 78s. I dont know why they didnt call the 33 1/3 one 33s. Maybe because saying thirty-three and third was too many words to say quickly.

Some people had reel to reel tape players, but for us that was rare. We never had one.

But soon, someone figured out how to thread tape through a cassette in a way that it never had to be rewound. It was called an 8-track tape cassette. Of course, the music was laid down in 8 tracks. I never knew how they worked. One night a friend of mine and I spent the night in his car at Paris Mountain. Not a smart idea. It was very cold, and we had no blankets.

When we woke up the next morning a big Oldsmobile 88 had tried to cross a walking bridge at night. It had no railings, and I guess the driver thought he could get across. He missed one of the tracks with his tires and the car fell into the creek below it. No one was there, but there were 8 track tapes thrown all over the inside. We took some out and took them apart and found out how they work.

After the 8-tracks, the industry shifted to much thinner tapes called cassette tapes. They were much smaller but had to be rewound. Or some players could play on one side and then switch and start playing in the opposite direction. Eventually the players were designed to play the tape in reverse, so it didnt have to be rewound.

One of the first portable players was the Walkman. It was a smaller, but still bulky cassette player that ran on batteries.

After the cassette tape came the first digital players. At first, they were very bulky, but eventually they were reduced to the iPod and nano size.

At first digital music had to be downloaded, and each song or album had to be paid for. But some sites came up like Napster that would get the music from some source and others could download and share with each other. Because the music companies lost so much money, they eventually sued and shut those sites down and the model eventually morphed into what we have as Spotify, Apple Music, Amazon Music, etc. You dont have to pay for each song. You pay a subscription and you can listen to any song on the service.

The stereo system I had in college included an amp to power the turntable, the tape deck, and the speakers, The speakers were 3 feet tall and 1.5 feet wide. Now all of that can be done with a pair of speakers the size of a tissue box and a wireless connection to the internet. Its easy to take it for granted because it now exists, but to come from a place where it didnt exist is really impressive.

Computers

Before the 1970s, there was no such thing as a personal computer. The first personal computers processing power and speed and storage was amazing at the time, but nothing compared to today. Initially, there were no hard drives. The system had to boot up from floppy disks. These were 8 discs sealed in thin plastic sleeves. They were called floppy because they were flimsy. They reduced the size to 5.25, then to 3.5 wrapped in a harder case. Then USB drives. The computing power in a cellphone is many times more capable than the early computers.

Laptops.

Dad bought us one of the first laptop computers. It was called the Osborne. Later he also bought a Compaq. It was compact compared to desktop computers, but it was the size of a sewing machine and weighed 19 pounds. The screen was about 5 across. I took it to school one day to show a professor a program I had written. I had to park about a block away and had to keep putting it down and switching hands to carry it because it was so heavy.

There is more computing power in our cellphones than the early mainframes that occupied entire rooms.

The first 8MB hard drive was the size of a refrigerator and cost $25,000 (back then, around 1988). The smallest thumb drive is now bigger than 8MB and can exceed gigabytes.

WYSIWYG (What You See Is What You Get) was first introduced for PCs in the early 1980s. The first widely known WYSIWYG word processor was Microsoft Word in 1983. However, it was WordPerfect and Aldus PageMaker that contributed to the evolution of WYSIWYG editing for desktop publishing.

Microsoft Word 1.0 was a key early example of WYSIWYG on PCs, but true WYSIWYG desktop publishing and graphical design took off with Aldus PageMaker in 1985. It enabled users to design documents exactly as they would appear in print, which was revolutionary for graphic designers and publishers at the time.

By the mid-to-late 1980s, WYSIWYG editors became more prevalent, paving the way for the graphical interfaces we use today in word processing and web design.

Email

Email is so taken for granted today. It has become so efficient that it has become its own problem. As I think about this, I cannot believe how we used to do it.

When I was at Lanier about 1989, everything was on paper, or it didnt exist. Two times a day a person with a cart would go around every floor and collect the items out of our outbox and deliver things addressed to us in our inbox. They would take the outbox items to the mail room in the basement where they would be sorted for delivery on the next run.

If we wanted to write a memo or letter or report, we would get out a dictating machine, verbally dictate the memo with as much instruction on punctuation or tables or anything we wanted represented on the page and we would put the tape in a plastic envelope that had a place for the small tape and the paper to be returned. The mailroom would collect the envelope in the morning, deliver it to the dictation room, which was a room full of typists that would do nothing but type all day long. They would put the typed pages in the envelope, put it in the outbox, the mailroom would pick it up, sort it and deliver it on the next run. We would make the correction manually in ink, put it back in the outbox and the process would repeat until the memo was as we wanted it. Then, if it were to go to more than one person, the mailroom would copy it and deliver the manual copies. Sometimes, it would take several days and several roundtrips to get one memo completed.

It's incredible to think that is how it was done.

Cameras

We used to have to take pictures on film, develop the film into negatives and then create a print from the negative on to paper.

Internet

The internet was originally wired. There was no wireless. To communicate, the computer had to use a modem and make this crazy sound the other computer could hear and somehow use to connect. The speeds were measured in kilobytes not megabytes and certainly not 100s of megabytes.

Artificial Intelligence

Alexa and Google are literal miracles. Computers can not only understand spoken words, but they can reply in spoken words having accessed vast information on any subject in the world in nano seconds. But this is still the beginning. AI is going to change the word in ways we cannot even imagine at the moment.

Cars

Electronics, Computers and Quality

The first cars I was involved with still had to be tuned up with distributor caps, and spark plug gaps. Gasoline was fed into a carburetor. That has all been replaced by electronics that directly inject the fuel and ignite it with electronic timing. Everything about cars has gotten so much more reliable. Car problems are so much rarer than they used to be. Flat tires, ignition failures, radiator valve sticking causing overheating, fuel line issues, etc.

Self-Driving

I think I was in too much of a hurry to want to ride in a self-navigating car. I bought into the hype that they would be here already. But given the problems they have had; I am okay waiting longer. But they will eventually be here.

Electric

Also cars are electric. Initially the electric cars were the low end, had limited power to accelerate or go any distance. Now they are the most powerful, faster than gasoline powered cars and the battery technology is advancing to the point where they will start to replace gasoline powered vehicles.

 

Music

 

COV - Cover Search Engine

How has music influenced your life?

 

What did you listen to over the years?

 


It is impossible to express the impact of music in our lives. It soothes or amplifies our emotions in every experience or actually is the experience.. The advances in the delivery of music have moved it from voluntary episodes to a perpetual companion.

Sound of My Fathers World

My exposure to music started through my dads collection of 8-track tapesId lie on the floor in front of the hutch where he kept the player and listen with headphones on to his favorites: Ray Charles, Dionne Warwick, Ella Fitzgerald, John Denver, Glen Campbell, my mothers favorite, Tom Jones, and others. At the lake, hed hook up the speakers on top of the houseboat, as he and Mom and their friends danced and played.

As I became more aware Id watch shows like American Bandstand and eventually Soul Train. The only other source was the radio,

To try an encapsulate my music experience over the years for myself and anyone else interested, I enlisted Chat GPTs help in tracking the most popular music over the years and remembering the experiences

Rock and Shock

The first and one of the only concerts I ever attended was Kiss. I dont remember the setlist, but Ill never forget the overwhelming smell of marijuana that hung over the arena.

Around the same time, I got my first record player. Chicago became a favoritemy brother Scot collected their albums, and I followed suit. But my most memorable early foray into records came when a friend gave me a George Carlin album titled The Seven Words You Cant Say on Television. I naively decided to play it in the den with my mother and grandparents sitting across the room. When Carlin began rattling off the forbidden words, I practically dove across the room to stop it. My mother, with a calm but definitive tone, said, That will be enough of that. I traded the record for a ZZ Top album soon after.

The Firebird Years

High school was a time of cruising in my Firebird with an 8-track blaring Earth, Wind & Fire and The Commodores. Later, cassette tapes took over, and my tastes expanded to Boston, Elton John, Gerry Rafferty, Jackson Browne, and James Taylor. These were the sounds of my teenage yearssongs that carried me through late-night drives, school dances, and summer adventures.

College and Discovery

In college, music became a social glue. My New York roommate introduced me to Neil Young, Fleetwood Mac, and Dire Straits, and I added them to my playlist alongside disco hits from Michael Jackson and Rod Stewart. I delivered pizzas with Billy Joels music playing in the car, thinking how much I loved staying connected to the latest tunes. I even made a vow to myself: I would never lose touch with popular music.

But as time went on, pop music grew away from meor maybe I grew away from it. My tastes remained rooted in the classics, even as music changed around me.

The Joy of Sharing Music

One of my favorite memories of music is driving in my Audi with the kids, the sunroof open, playing "Saturday in the Park" by Chicago. Moments like that remind me how music connects generations and creates shared joy.

At college parties, music was always the centerpiece. DJs played everything from pop hits to beach music. I never quite mastered the shag, but I soaked up the atmosphere. During those years, songs like Peter Framptons "Do You Feel Like We Do" and Aerosmiths "Dream On" became anthems for the good times.

The Changing Technology of Music

Over the years, the way we listen to music has transformed dramatically. Ive lived through the transition from vinyl to 8-tracks, cassettes, CDs, Walkmans, iPods, Napster, and now Spotify. The speakers have changed tooJensen, JBL, Onyx, Boston Acoustics, and now Sonos. Each new technology has made music more portable, more accessible, and more personal, but I sometimes miss the ritual of flipping a record or rewinding a tape.

A Fathers Favorites and an Unforgettable Night

My dad loved music, and his favorites were Ella Fitzgerald and Aretha Franklin. Ellas voice was smooth as silk, wrapping around songs like Summertime and A-Tisket, A-Tasket with an elegance that defined an era. Aretha, on the other hand, brought soul and fire. Respect and Natural Woman were more than hitsthey were anthems.

A Mothers Crush

Tom Jones was my mothers favorite, and I think a lot of women felt the same. With his booming voice and showmanship, he could make any song sound irresistible. Hits like Its Not Unusual and Shes a Lady became staples in our home, much to my dads amusement.

Brothers, Buffett, and Margaritaville

My brother and I had our share of musical adventures too, like the Jimmy Buffett concert we attended with his friends. Margaritaville came alive that night, along with Son of a Son of a Sailor and Cheeseburger in Paradise. Buffetts music wasnt just about songsit was about an attitude, a carefree escape to a world of sunshine and cold drinks.

James Taylor: The Passage of Time

More recently, I saw James Taylor in concert. They played a montage of his performances over the decades as he sang one of his classics. Watching him transform from a young man with a guitar to an elder statesman of music brought a mix of emotionshappiness, satisfaction, and a touch of sadness. His music, like Fire and Rain and Carolina in My Mind, has been a constant for so many, including me. Its remarkable to think about the joy hes brought to millions of people over the years.

Evolving Tastes and Country Roads

I havent always been a fan of country music. Early country, with its twangy vocals and themes, never resonated with me. But the modern, more polished version has grown on me. My daughters, Elizabeth and Caroline, have always loved country music, and their enthusiasm has rubbed off. I recently saw Dierks Bentley live and found myself genuinely enjoying it. As corny as some country lyrics can be, theyre often about real lifestories I can relate to now more than ever.

The Beats of Hip-Hop and Cultural Storms

Hip-hop, on the other hand, has been more hit-or-miss for me. While some beats and songs are undeniably catchy, much of the genre seems to dwell on the darker sides of life. That said, every now and then, a song comes along that unites everyone, like American Pie or The Macarena. Its fascinating how certain songs can capture the spirit of a moment in time and bring people together.

The Technology and True Artists

Music has evolved in so many waysvinyl, 8-tracks, cassettes, CDs, iPods, and now streaming platforms like Spotify. Alongside these changes, the way artists create music has shifted. Auto-tune and mixing have made it easier for anyone to sound polished, but theyve also diluted the artistry. It makes you appreciate the truly great voices of the pastElla Fitzgerald, James Taylor, and others who relied on raw talent and discipline rather than technology.

Ive also developed an appreciation for classical music. The idea that composers like Beethoven and Mozart created such intricate, enduring works with the limited technology of their time is humbling. Its a reminder that great art transcends the tools used to make it.

Closing Note: Music and Life

Music doesnt play as loudly in my life as it once didliterally or figurativelybut its still a source of joy and reflection. Whether its the deep nostalgia of a classic or the discovery of something new, music continues to shape how I see the world. And as I think back on the songs and artists that have come and gone, Im grateful for the soundtrack theyve providedone filled with memories, emotions, and the simple, enduring beauty of a good tune.

MTV (Music Television) officially launched on August 1, 1981. It revolutionized the music industry by broadcasting music videos 24/7 and introducing a new era of television programming.

Observations and Summary of Music Trends (19592024):

Looking back at the evolution of music from 1959 to today, we see significant shifts in style, technology, and the way we consume music. The changes in music genres, from the golden age of rock to the rise of hip-hop, pop-punk, and even trap, reflect the cultural shifts and technological advancements of each era.

From the smooth, sophisticated vocals of Ella Fitzgerald and Aretha Franklin to the rebellious spirit of rock bands like The Rolling Stones and Led Zeppelin, music has always served as a mirror to societys values and struggles. In the 1980s, the advent of MTV brought music videos into the mainstream, transforming artists into visual icons. The 1990s marked the rise of hip-hop and R&B, with artists like Tupac, Biggie Smalls, and Whitney Houston leaving an indelible mark on the soundscape.

The 2000s saw the emergence of digital music formats, with Mapster and iTunes disrupting traditional models. This was also the period where pop-punk, emo, and indie rock took over, with bands like Blink-182, Green Day, and The Strokes becoming the soundtrack for a generation. Today, with platforms like Spotify and YouTube, music is more accessible than ever, leading to an explosion of genres and international collaborations.

Genres like country, hip-hop, and pop continue to evolve and merge, creating new soundscapes that reflect the cultural fusion of our globalized world. Country music, once seen as a niche genre, has seen a resurgence with artists like Luke Combs and Morgan Wallen. Hip-hop, still dominating the charts, has expanded into a broader influence on pop culture, with artists like Kendrick Lamar, Travis Scott, and Cardi B making waves.

Moreover, as technology continues to improve, the art of music production has changed drastically, with auto-tune and digital effects now a common part of the sound. However, as we see from the continued success of artists like Adele and Taylor Swift, there is still a deep appreciation for raw talent and vulnerability in music. This balance between digital production and traditional musicianship speaks to the timeless nature of music as both an art and a reflection of our experiences.

         Simply Red Lady in Red

In early high school, I would go to David Gallitzens house and he introduced me to Edgar Winter and Cheech and Chong.

In later high school I listened to a combination of things, from Sara Smile, to The Isley Brothers, Earth Wind and Fire, The Commodores. There was always a radio, 8-track or cassette playing. No such thing as an iPod or Spotify at the time.

American Pie was a phenomenon for a while. The local radio station had a contest for people to guess what the motivation or inspiration was for the song. It seemed to go on for weeks. One morning, they had McClean on for an interview and he basically said there was no inspiration, it was just a bunch of words he string together. The interviewer was clearly exasperated. They had hyped this contest for weeks only to have him let all the air out of the balloon. But I can still recite the words.

Travel

 

I

 

 

 

have always been interested in travel. It has been an education in itself, and I continually love it.

What countries have you been to?

I have been to 28 countries:

What states have you been to?

I have been to 43 US States, and DC.I have only not been to 7 states

Did you ever take any great road trips?

Mardi Gras

In the Spring Semester of my first year at USC, my roommates and I took a road trip to New Orleans for Mardi Gras. They invited me because I had a car to get us there. I was such a nervous nelly that I had to call my parents to ask if I could go. Of course, they said yes, but it shows how sheltered I was. My friends didnt want me to ask because they were afraid theyd say no.

Pledge Trip

In my first year at Clemson, we took a road trip which was a pledge trip that was a scavenger hunt. We had to go to the hometown of one of the senior brothers, Rafe Dixon and collect various items along the way. One was a G-String from a stripper at The Chettah 3, which later closed, but has since reopened.

Fortunately, I have been to a lot of places. I mostly like going to new places because there are so many places to see, Id like to see something new each time. However, there are a couple of places that I would really love to go back to.

The first is Rome. I was never a big fan of history before travelling, but once you start to see how places used to be, it gets a lot more interesting. I am just fascinated with Rome. How sophisticated they were so many years ago and what they were able to buildthe Coliseum, the Circus Maximus. The size and complexity is just amazing.

I also always love going to Paris. The downtown area is fascinating, but also Versailles which is just a little way outside the city.

Best trip

Wow, we have had many great trips, but Id have to say that the best was the 2014 Europe trip.

Worst trip

There was a trip when we were kids to Jacksonville. We were driving through Edgefield, SC and had a flat tire. Mom and us kids had to stay in the car while Dad went to get help. I think he walked and hitchhiked. It was summer and the gnats were swarming. It was hot and miserable. I dont know how long we were stranded, but it seemed like an eternity. He finally returned, got the tire repaired and we were on out way.

On the way the way back, the highway ended into a stop sign. Preceding the sign was a series of strips in the road that would make a sound when the tires rolled over them. We hit the first one and Mark, having been traumatized like the rest of us, said, disgustedly, Flat tire! Luckily it wasnt.

Longest trip

I once took a trip through South and Central America with the University trying to place students that lasted six weeks.

Ski Trips

Besides the cities, I always love going to the mountains in the west during ski season. It is so beautiful.

 

         Arapahoe Basin

         Park City

         Lake Tahoe

         Steamboat

Learning to Windsurf

On a trip to Hilton Head, Dad asked if we wanted to take windsurfing lessons. Of course I did! We first practiced the basics on some mechanical trainers on land. There we were led into this very calm bay area, and we practiced going back and forth for some time. I have loved windsurfing ever since.

As part of Dads outdoor furniture business, he received some windsurfers from Coleman that he kept at the lake. I would often get them out and head to the lake. It was touch because the trees around the cove area blocked most of the wind. If I wanted to get going, I would have to limp out to the main water area. Out there was just great. The wind was strong enough to get going, but not too fast to stir up the water and make it harder. The sense of freedom and motion on a windsurfer is just great. It is you, the surfer, the wind and the water all working together to propel you across the water in any direction you wish to go. It is exhilarating!

Windsurfing in Grand Caymen

On our senior Cruise to Grand Caymen I rented a windsurfer. The wind was really tough and the current of the water would pull you away from the island. After several attempts, I was having fun, but I continued to get further and further away from the shore and could not surf back toward it. So I laid down the sail, laid on the board and paddled back. With the sail dragging in the water, it took a long time to paddle back. I had not used sunscreen and by the time I got ack my forearms were fried. Normally a sunburn hurts later. This one hurt immediately. It was so painful that at dinner, I would hold my iced tea glass up and down my forearms to cool the pain.

Windsurfing in Hawaii

I had been to Australia and New Zealand and was returning through Hawaii, but had an 8 hour layover. When I got to Honolulu, I asked at the information desk if there was something I could do for the wait. She said, I could get on the bus and go to Waikiki Beach. So, I hopped on the bus. I saw there was a windsurfer rental place. I went into a gift shop and bought a bathing suit and t-shirt. Changed in the public dressing rooms near the beach, stuffed my suit in a bag and put it in a locker. Rented a windsurfer for an hour, rinsed off, got dressed, took the bus back to the airport and arrived just as they were calling the flight.

Windsurfing in Aruba

While in Aruba, I rented another windsurfer. This one was different. Until then, the windsurfers I had learned on and used, would float with my weight on them. This one was smaller and not as buoyant. You had to drape your leg across the top of the board, then lift the sail into the wind pulling the board forward, dragging your body in the water until the board picked up enough speed that you could pull yourself out of the water and put both feet on it. Then you wore a harness that had a hook on it. You could dip your hips catching the hook onto the sail handle, then you could lean your weight against the wind and flay across the water, sometimes just clipping the tops of the ripples in the water. That was probably the most fun I ever had windsurfing.

Davos, Switzerland

While working in Europe, one of the trips I took was to our subsidiary in Switzerland. On the way home, I scheduled a stop in Davos, a place my Dad had talked about having visited. I realized later, watching CNBC, that this is where they hold a big worldwide business leader meeting every year.

I took a train from Bern, it arrived late at night and I could not see much. The next morning, I awoke to a winter wonderland. Rising behind the hotel and the town was an enormous mountain. Everything was covered in now and so beautiful. I rented skis and got on the chairlift to the top of the mountain. When we got there, it was so cloudy that you could not see three feet in front of you. I got in line behind the crowd that was shuffling single file toward something. I could hear people in front and behind but could not see anyone. Some of the jokers would fake screaming as if they were falling off a cliff and their voices trailing off in the distance. Eventually, we got to a area where we waited until the cloud lifted. When it did the view was spectacular. You could see for miles and the slopes seemed to be football fields across. I spent the morning just gliding back and forth across the face of the mountain having the time of my life.

I would ride the interim lifts that were partially down the mountain and traveled back to or near the top. On one of the trips up, the tip of my boot that was tucked into the ski binding broke off and the ski fell a hundred feet or so into a craggy area between the slopes. I had rented the skis and had to return them. So, when I got to the top, I informed the lift operator, and he shrugged his shoulders as if there was nothing he could do. So, I took off the other ski and hiked down the steep rocky slope to retrieve my ski and back up again. I was quite exhausted in the thin air.

I took the lift back down to the town and the rental shop, exchanged my boots for another pair and took the lift back up. I skied for a few more hours. As it was getting later, I suddenly realized I was skiing down this side of the slope by myself. I could see others going down another wide area to my right. I stopped and had to sort of ski back uphill for a way to get back on that side of the slope. I found out later that that lift had stopped and had I continued, I would have been unable to get back down. Thankfully, I noticed and got back on track. I skied to the bottom and ended a thrilling ski trip in a gorgeous Swiss town.

Have you ever missed a flight?

Haha! Yes, I have missed more than one flight!

Missed Christmas Flight

One year, Elizabeth, Caroline, and I were going skiing on Christmas day. While I thought we left on time, obviously we didnt. We had all our luggage and couldnt check it because we were passed the deadline, and we were lugging it through Atlanta airport to get to the gate. I don't remember where the gate was exactly, but the law of the universe says that the later you are, the further down the concourse the gate is. It seems like it was one of the ones at the end of the concourse. We ran as fast as we could struggling with the luggage. When we got to the gate, the plane had already left. We rescheduled and had to go all the way home and wait for a flight the next day. We found one of the few restaurants open on Christmas day, a Chinese restaurant. We had a nice meal, a good nights rest, got there early the next day and made the flight.

Travelling Baseball

During Williams travelling baseball years, we missed a flight coming back from a baseball tournament. The crazy thing is we were sitting just across from the gate as they loaded the plane, made a last call, closed the door and left. We didnt hear the call and didnt realize what was happening.

Close Call

I had another very close call. When I worked at USC, I travelled throughout Latin America meeting with companies offering them interns to work for them. This was well before TSA and the horrendous security lines of today. In Buenos Aires, I finished my meetings with the companies, then headed to the airport. As I got there, I could tell I was running tight on time. By the time I got to the gate, everyone else had already boarded, they checked my ticket and I headed down the rampway. When I got to the plane, they had already closed the door. I looked through the window, they opened the door and let me in. I found my seat and we left! Perfect timing!

What things from home did you miss the most while living overseas?

Its funny what you miss when you get away from the food you are used to at home. I loved the food in Colombia (mostly). But there were times when we would sit around and dream about having a US style pizza. The pizza there was not very good. The crust, the sauce, and the cheese were just not the same. Whats really bad, is the pizza we wanted was Pizza Hut pizza, either thin or pan style. Not very good pizza either.

I also remember missing a good hamburger. They had beef there, but it just wasn't the same. The bun was different too.

How has travel influenced you?

I have always loved to travel. I enjoyed our early vacations as a kid, all the way up to business travel. Travel has been a great experience in several ways. It teaches you independence, and organizational skills to plan and execute the trips. It exposes you to different languages and cultures of behavior of food. It exposes you to the vast size of the world. Seeing the land from the sky and travelling for hours and hours in one direction and still only covering a small portion of the earth is humbling. It gives you confidence to take on new challenges, to go to new places.

 

Books

 

I was not the most prolific readerespecially fiction. I remember reading several when I was 9-11, but I didn't become an inquisitive student until late in high school. So, the books I can remember reading are pretty few. I have read a couple of Dan Brown books, The DaVinci Code and Angels and Demons, the prequel.

When I was a toddler, I liked the Dr. Seuss books. A couple by P.D. Eastman.

My all-time favorite though was The Shy Stegosaurus of Crooked Creek. I remember liking it because a boy finds a stegosaurus and befriends it. I think I read a couple of Hardy Boys books, maybe a Nancy Drew or two. I remember liking the analysis and the suspense type books.

After graduate school, I realized just how much I didnt know about business and being successful. I had learned some basic discipline and responsibility from Dad, but I did not know much else. I began to read everything I could get my hands on or sounded interesting about business. Most of it was self-help books like speaking in front of people, etc.

Today, I dont enjoy reading books, because they tend to be too long and I am not interested in all of the back story. I just want the facts. I rarely read fiction. I prefer nonfiction. There is so much to learn about reality.
