Over the years, I have preferred to read non-fiction over fiction because there is so much to learn. I can see the educational and entertainment value of fiction, but I have leaned toward non-fiction.

Heres a decade-by-decade list of the top 10 influential business books from each era, highlighting titles that shaped business thinking and management trends:

1970s

  1. "Future Shock" by Alvin Toffler (1970)
    • Explored the effects of rapid technological and societal change.
  2. "Winning Through Intimidation" by Robert Ringer (1973)
    • A controversial take on achieving success through assertiveness.
  3. "The Peter Principle" by Laurence J. Peter and Raymond Hull (1970)
    • Examined the concept of people rising to their "level of incompetence."
  4. "Up the Organization" by Robert Townsend (1970)
    • A candid look at leadership and management strategies.
  5. "Small Is Beautiful" by E.F. Schumacher (1973)
    • Advocated for sustainable economics and human-scale enterprises.
  6. "Quality Is Free" by Philip B. Crosby (1979)
    • Introduced the idea of "zero defects" in quality management.
  7. "What They Dont Teach You at Harvard Business School" by Mark H. McCormack (1979)
    • Insights on practical business strategies and negotiation.
  8. "Management: Tasks, Responsibilities, Practices" by Peter F. Drucker (1973)
    • A seminal work on management as a discipline.
  9. "Positioning: The Battle for Your Mind" by Al Ries and Jack Trout (1978)
    • Introduced the concept of positioning in marketing.
  10. "Corporate Strategy" by H. Igor Ansoff (1970)
    • A pioneering text on strategic management.

1980s

  1. "In Search of Excellence" by Tom Peters and Robert H. Waterman (1982)
    • A groundbreaking study of successful companies and management practices.
  2. "Competitive Strategy" by Michael E. Porter (1980)
    • Defined the framework for analyzing industries and competitors.
  3. "The Art of War" by Sun Tzu (Business Edition, 1983)
    • Applied ancient military strategy to modern business.
  4. "The One Minute Manager" by Kenneth Blanchard and Spencer Johnson (1982)
    • Simplified lessons in effective management.
  5. "Thriving on Chaos" by Tom Peters (1987)
    • Emphasized adaptability and innovation in business.
  6. "Barbarians at the Gate" by Bryan Burrough and John Helyar (1989)
    • A dramatic account of the RJR Nabisco leveraged buyout.
  7. "Reengineering the Corporation" by Michael Hammer and James Champy (1980s concepts, published 1993)
    • Introduced business process reengineering.
  8. "Megatrends" by John Naisbitt (1982)
    • Identified key social and economic trends shaping the future.
  9. "The Goal" by Eliyahu M. Goldratt (1984)
    • A business novel introducing the Theory of Constraints.
  10. "Good to Great" by Jim Collins (1980s research, published 2001)
    • Research into why some companies excel and others don't.

1990s

  1. "Built to Last" by Jim Collins and Jerry Porras (1994)
    • Examined the traits of visionary companies.
  2. "The Innovators Dilemma" by Clayton M. Christensen (1997)
    • Introduced the concept of disruptive innovation.
  3. "Emotional Intelligence" by Daniel Goleman (1995)
    • Explored the role of emotional intelligence in leadership and business.
  4. "First, Break All the Rules" by Marcus Buckingham and Curt Coffman (1999)
    • Insights on great management practices based on Gallup research.
  5. "The Fifth Discipline" by Peter Senge (1990)
    • Introduced systems thinking for organizational learning.
  6. "Only the Paranoid Survive" by Andrew S. Grove (1996)
    • Lessons from the former Intel CEO on managing in crises.
  7. "Who Moved My Cheese?" by Spencer Johnson (1998)
    • A parable about managing change.
  8. "The Lexus and the Olive Tree" by Thomas Friedman (1999)
    • A primer on globalization and its impacts.
  9. "The Cluetrain Manifesto" by Rick Levine et al. (1999)
    • A revolutionary look at internet marketing and communications.
  10. "Reengineering the Corporation" by Michael Hammer and James Champy (1993)
    • Revisited as a transformative concept in the '90s.

2000s

  1. "Good to Great" by Jim Collins (2001)
    • A continuation of his exploration of high-performing companies.
  2. "The Tipping Point" by Malcolm Gladwell (2000)
    • Analyzed how small changes can create big trends.
  3. "Freakonomics" by Steven D. Levitt and Stephen J. Dubner (2005)
    • Explored economics through unconventional lenses.
  4. "The Long Tail" by Chris Anderson (2006)
    • Showed how niche markets thrive in the digital age.
  5. "Blue Ocean Strategy" by W. Chan Kim and Rene Mauborgne (2005)
    • Introduced strategies for creating uncontested market space.
  6. "The Black Swan" by Nassim Nicholas Taleb (2007)
    • Examined the impact of unpredictable events.
  7. "Outliers" by Malcolm Gladwell (2008)
    • Investigated the factors behind extraordinary success.
  8. "The 4-Hour Workweek" by Timothy Ferriss (2007)
    • A guide to lifestyle design and escaping the 9-to-5 grind.
  9. "Execution: The Discipline of Getting Things Done" by Larry Bossidy and Ram Charan (2002)
    • Focused on the importance of implementation in strategy.
  10. "Lean In" by Sheryl Sandberg (2009)
    • A call for women to embrace leadership roles in business.

How to Win at Office Politics.

Something I learned from this book that influenced my decision-making for many years was, consider what you dont want and do the opposite. There is some benefit to this advice, and it has been useful at times, but I have come to like the advice less. I have caught myself saying, What I dont want is this is good, but only when what you dont want has a higher probability of occurring that what you do want. If what you dont want has a remote possibility of occurring and what you do want has a greater possibility of occurring and what you dont want can be mitigated in some way , then this advice can lead you to avoid rational risks. Every decision has varying outcomes and the risl of an unfavorable outcome. However, often we can mitigate or avoid the negative outcome before it unfolds, as it is unfolding or after it unfolds. I heard another piece of advice from another good decision maker, Howard Marks, former Chairman of Oakmark Capital. He said that if an outcome has an existential potential outcome, regardless of how small it may be, then that risk should be avoided. A simple example is Russian Roulette. There is only a 17% chance of getting a bullet (1/6 = 0.167), but all possibilities play out in the long run, so this type of risk must be avoid.

Combining these two pieces of advice have led me to a more effective decision making criteria. Identify any existential risk and do the opposite. Not everyone is going to adhere to this advise, because skydiving, mountain climbing, car racing, etc, all have existential risks, and they are taken on for the benefit of the experience. The space program, the Challenger shuttle accident comes to mind as existential risks taken because the potential benefit is so high.

That has me rethinking the combined advice into expectancy- the combination of the probabilities with the risk and reward

Television

 

With the massive volume of instantly available, high-definition video content today, its hard to imagine, that when I was growing up, there were only three over the Air (OTA) broadcast channels, in very rudimentary, black and white, resolution, and the content was determined and scheduled by the broadcaster.

If you wanted to watch content, you had to have a schedule of what was to be broadcast and be present to watch it when it aired. Or watch only whatever was being broadcast at the time. There was no way to record it and if you missed it, you missed it.

An episode of a season would be broadcast once per week at a set time-- not all at once. They would leave you with a cliff hanger (especially Lost in Space) and youd have to wait a week before the next episode. (Tune in next week, same time, same station) And at midnight the stations would play the national anthem and then go off the air and display at test card and a solid constant tone until the next morning around 5am!! I have woken up sevral times to the test card and tone having fallen asleep watching TV.

The good thing about the broadcast schedule and the inability to record was that the family would watch together. You couldnt binge watch

After school we would watch

News

Each station had news programs, but only for an hour and they started at 6pm. No live feeds from anywhere. I vaguely remember the news. I definitely remember Walter Cronkite. There was also one called Huntley and Brinkley. All were in black and white for us. I would listen to the news at night hearing about the death toll in the Vietnam war. Every night they would update the total.

TV Evolution

The expansion from the original three major over-the-air (OTA) broadcast networks (ABC, CBS, NBC) began in the 60s..

Reality TV

Reality TV's roots trace back to Candid Camera (1948) and Queen for a Day (1956), but An American Family on PBS (1973) is often considered the first modern reality TV series, documenting the lives of the Loud family.

However, modern reality TV, defined by unscripted drama, competitions, and personal stories, would explode in the late 1990s and early 2000s.

1992: MTVs The Real World introduced the "confession cam" format, where participants shared their thoughts, shaping the genre's future.

2000: The debut of Survivor and Big Brother marked the beginning of the reality TV boom.

  • 1948-1954: The Big Three Dominance
  •  
  • - ABC, CBS, and NBC were the dominant national networks.
  • 1955-1966: Regional and Public TV Emerges
  • o Local independent stations emerged in large cities, offering content like local sports and syndicated reruns.
  • 1969: PBS (Public Broadcasting Service) was officially founded.
  • Adding educational and cultural programming to the mix.
  • 1970s: Early Cable Networks
  • o Cable television began to expand, initially designed to provide better reception for OTA channels in rural and remote areas.
  •  
  • o Networks like HBO (launched in 1972) and TBS (Turner Broadcasting System, launched in 1976) introduced premium content and national broadcasting over cable.
  • 1980s: Explosion of Cable Channels
  • o Cable programming expanded significantly, adding specialty channels like

  • ESPN (1979, sports),

  • Nickelodeon (1979, kids' programming).

  • CNN (1980, 24-hour news),

  • MTV (1981, music video


Fox (launched in 1986)


  • Big hits like The Simpsons
  • and The X-Files.
  • Satellite technology allowed more channels to reach wider audiences, breaking the "Big Three" monopoly.
  • 1990s: The Rise of Additional Broadcast Networks

  • The WB (1995) and

  • UPN (1995) were launched to target younger demographics but

  • later merged to form The CW (2006).
  • 2000s: Streaming and On-Demand
  • o The dominance of cable began to decline with the rise of digital streaming platforms like
  • Netflix (streaming launched in 2007) and
  • Hulu (2008).
  • Over-the-air channels also expanded with the introduction of digital subchannels after the U.S. digital transition in 2009.

 

Miscellaneous

 

Do you believe in ghosts?

Ive never seen any ghosts, but I have seen some photos that didnt seem to be altered that showed the possibility of ghosts. I think it is possible that ghosts exist, but I am not particularly afraid of them.

Do you believe in UFOs?

There seems to be too much evidence of UFOs not to believe they exist. Many commercial and military pilots say they have seen them. Some have been caught on radar. I think they exist. I used to think they came from space, and they may have, but there is also the possibility that they are remnants of prior advanced life on this planet. There is also a theory that they could be humans from the future that have discovered time travel. I have even heard that they could be evil spirits.

It doesnt impact my daily life, so whether they do or do not is not really relevant. The fact that there seems to be so much evidence, yet people do not talk about it and the evidence is not made mainstream, why that is is curious. Are those who know afraid for everyone else to know either because it threatens their authority or because there is something to fear from the aliens. Are the aliens orchestrating world affairs behind the scenes and they keep themselves hidden.

Do you believe in life after death?

I do believe in life after death. Another issue that does not have hard evidence to prove, but comments from many who have died or almost died and came back believe there is.

Some say that this could be super realistic hallucinations or dreams brought on by chemical releases near death, and that could be true. And, while it does seem that some of the stories could be influenced by beliefs they already held, some of the stories seem to be so counter to what they believed beforehand that they seem to be real.

Do you believe there is life on other planets?

It seems to me that as vast and old as the universe is, it seems the probablility is not zero.

Which past time would you like to travel to?

I have always been fascinated with the Romans, but I am also fascinated by the unexplained monolithic structures on various continents. I would not like to have lived in any of the past times where people were basically warring with each other all the time in the most viscious ways.

What are you superstitious about?

Im not superstitious. In fact, I am not very stitious at all!

I do not believe in superstitions. There is nothing inherently dangerous about walking under a ladder or having a black cat cross your path. These are beliefs taken from random, unrelated events as if they have some causal relationship.

Wile some see superstitions as a harmless, perhaps humorous beliefs, I think they are actually harmful. Humans have done great harm to others in the past because of the beliefs they had about the cause and effect relationships of things. Beleiving that walking under a ladder is bad luck or that having collards for New Years day are not harmful in themselves, the mental laziness that allows them to persist lead to other illogical inferences that do cause issues.

What have been some of your life's greatest surprises, disappointments?

I have had several people that have influenced by life. Mostly good, and from some I learned to do the opposite of their example.

First, of course, Id have to say my mother and father had the most influence on me.

I think I got a lot of my compassion from my mother. She is a very kind and compassionate person. How she dealt with 4 boys with only 4 years between them and maintained he composure so much of the time is a sign of her kindness and compassion. She rarely wanted anything for herself. She was always giving to us

What is the best gift youve ever received?

The Gift of Responsibility

From my father, first I received the gift of discipline. While I hated hearing it at the time, he would frequently remind us of the big Rresponsibility. I might have been a slow learner on that one because I know I resisted it. But ultimately the lesson took hold, and it has been one of my strengths. I cover this in another short story, but, while I didnt learn the saying until much later, it retroactively applied. If its to be, its up to me.!

What is your greatest achievement?

My greatest achievement in life is helping raise three of the best and most capable people you will ever find in this world. I mad plenty of mistakes, but I think I got enough right that I helped infuse in them with responsibility, confidence, compassion and capability to do anything they ever want to do and hopefully pay it forward to their families.

Adventures

 

What adventures have you had?

It would probably be clich to say my whole life has been an adventure, but I think that is what life is. I feel like I have been on a lot of adventures. I like adventures.

I think that is a lot of what life is about. Exploring what there is to explore and experiencing the senses and the emotions of those experiences.

Hilton Head

Moving from Taylors to Greenville was a big move and adventure for us and me. We had good friends and didn't want to move, but it was good for us.

Going to college was a great adventure. The first time I ever lived alone.

Transferring from USC to Clemson. I had already invested 2 years at Carolina. There were things I liked and things I didnt like. Dad suggested I try summer school at Clemson and see how I liked it.I loved it and easily made the move.

Taking my first job at USC was an adventure.

I graduated with no job, but got a call shortly after.

I took it because I thought I would get to be involved in international business.

I was.

I travelled all over the US meeting with companies and bringing executives to speak at the business school.

I eventually took over the Latin America track and travelled throughout Central and South America.

After three years I was either going to be an academic or get into business.

I took a job with NCR as an analyst at the local plant where they manufactured the first multi-user computers.

Moving from Columbia to Atlanta was a huge adventure.

The day we drove our cars and U-haul trailer into Atlanta with a highway that at that time was probably only 4 lanes, but huge to us. (now it is at least 6). But it was very intimidating.

Moving to Europe was another great adventure. When I got the offer, Kerri was much more understanding and willing to make that move.

We were able to travel all over Europe and give the kids adventures of their own very early in their lives, and I think this was helpful for them.

 

Moving back to the US was an adventure.

Leaving Lanier for a startup was an adventure. It didn't work out, but other things did.

Working for Caribiner in New York, commuting three weeks a month.

Joining McKesson after they had just uncovered huge fraud that needed to be cleaned up.

Working as CFO at McKesson was an adventure, Leaving McKesson was an adventure.

I say this carefully, but getting a divorce was an adventure. It was likely one of the biggest unknowns. It was one that in many ways I was afraid to take, but at the time believed I had to take.

Its not that I believe I shouldnt have taken it, it is just that you only have your current beliefs to inform your decisions.

Looking back with different beliefs is not a fair comparison because you make the decision with what you have at the time, and you then make the next decision that comes.

Moving to Tennessee has been a great adventure.

 

Food

 

When I was growing up, my mother was a great cook. She did all the cooking all the time. I dont think Dad ever cooked anything in the kitchen. His realm was the grill or campfire.

Her style is what she learned from her mother and others, which was southern meals...fried chicken, meatloaf, green beans, mashed potatoes, macaroni and cheese.

Traditions

Thanksgiving - turkey, dressing, cranberry sauce and casseroles.

New Years pork loin, collard greens, a symbol of money and black-eyed peas for good luck.

Christmas Sausage balls, Chex mix,

 

Salmon croquets, which were ground up salmon made into patties and fried in a pan. I liked them but remember getting the little round spine bones in some of them.

Meatloaf

Spaghetti

Bologna Hats

My Favorites Then and Now

My favorites growing up were:

Dessert

Then

Rice pudding and banana pudding. Mom had a particular brown ceramic bowl that she would make these in. The rice pudding had raisins. The banana pudding was layers of vanilla wafers, crme filling and bananas. I also liked coconut cake.

Now

Carrot cake

 

Cinnamon toast (white bread, butter, and cinnamon sugar.) toasted in the oven.

Asparagus casserole, with canned asparagus, mushroom soup and almonds on top.

Coconut cake, Carrot cake. Key lime pie, pecan pie, pumpkin pie,

And, from my travels in Latin America, I really like flan, avocados and pineapple.

 

Least Favorites

Rutabagas, they just sound bad.

Sauerkraut. Still hate it. Not a fan of anything vinegary.

 

Have these changed over time?

When I was a kid, I did not like beets. They tasted like dirt. Now I love them. I didnt like spinach, but I love it now.

 

Holidays

 

By far my favorite was Christmas! One of the first I remember was on Creighton Street. Mom and Dad decorated the house and built a Santa Claus climbing in through the window on the front porch, with a spot light. They won best decorations in the neighborhood!! Mom and Dad always made Christmas great! Over the years, we got bicycles, and motorcycles, and snow skis. It was always a great surprise.

Snoring Keeping Santa Away

One year when I was little, my grandparents came to stay with us. Granddaddy slept in my room. We were all anxious to go to bed so Santa Claus could come, but Granddaddy was snoring so loud I could not sleep. I laid there awake afraid Santa would not come to our house because I was not asleep. He did come and everything was great!

Santas Helper

I seemed to be a late bloomer mentally. Perhaps because I had younger brothers that held on to the beliefs, but I was older before I learned that Santa, the Easter Bunny and the Tooth Fairy were not real. One Christmas, Dad let me help him play Santa. He had hidden some bicycles at his manufacturing warehouse, and he took me with him to get them. It was late at night and we were rummaging around in his building. It was an exciting adventure.

 

Fights

 

Have you ever gotten into a fight?

Unfortunately, I have been in more fights than I would like to admit. Normally, I was not a fighting kid. I would always do everything to avoid confrontation. I would only engage if I absolutely had to. That was the case in all my fights, except the last one.

Middle School

When I was in the sixth grade, I had a girlfriend for a brief time. She and her friends had finished lunch and gone outside to play in the front yard of the school. For some reason, I was still eating and didnt go. But a few minutes later, a friend of mine came in and said, Hey Alan, Tandy (the name of this black kid) is picking on Valerie. This may sound strange these days, but our schools had just been integrated the year before, when I was in the fifth grade. I had been one of the students chosen to help welcome the new black kids into our class. But Tandy was just always causing trouble with someone. At first, I tried to ignore him and then made some excuse why I wasnt going out there. But he persisted until I finally had to go.

When I got out there, there were kids all in a circle and Tandy was in the middle with my girlfriend and a couple of her friends and he was taunting her about something. I walked into the circle and told him to stop bothering her. Well, of course, he turned his taunting on me. I initially tried to resist it, but it was pretty clear he was not going to stop, and the trigger went off and I hit him several times in a row. He tried to fight back a little, but I fought even harder, and he ran away. I never had any trouble with Tandy after that.

High School

Another time, I think I was a senior in high school. This girl I knew, that was the daughter of a man that worked with my father, and I had had a crush relationship a few times over the years, before high school. But we lived far apart and didnt go to the same school so it wasnt much of a thing.

Well, somehow this guy I knew, who was kind of in our friend group, was dating her, and somehow got the idea that I was encroaching on his territory. I had not seen or talked to her in years. I dont even know how the subject could have come up. We had this place we would go after school and at night, called Petes drive-in. It was this hole-in-the wall hamburger place that had a big parking lot. We would go there, park and get out and talk or eat. Just socializing. One night, I was up there with some other friends, and he came over to me in a pretty aggressive way and started accusing me of trying to date his girl and threatening me.

I wasnt doing that, and I told him that multiple times, but he just wouldn't back off. I tried to avoid it for as long as I could, and then the trigger went off and I hit him about three times in the face and head as he tried to get away. It lasted about 5 seconds. He never bothered me again.

College

The last time I got in a fight was in college. Up until that time, every time I had gotten in a fight it was initiated by the other person, and I had tried to do everything I could to avoid it. But if I couldnt, I would trigger and make sure they never bothered me again.

Well, this time was different. We had been at this all-day fraternity party called Greek Day. Every fraternity was there and there were all kinds of silly competitive games. It was basically a big party. At the end, everyone was trying to get out with their cars, from this big field and there was no direction. It was just a big free-for-all. Well, this other driver and I got upset with each other and he communicated his thoughts with a hand gesture, which I didn't take well.

We chased him around Clemson for a long time. Eventually he stopped and I went up to his car and punched him in the face. The neighbors came out and asked what was going on. In the meantime, we were standing around talking, and apparently the guy had gotten out of his car. He came up behind me and hit me full force in my left eye. I went down and when I was getting up I knew immediately something was wrong. I was seeing everything double. I got my friends attention and said we have to go. So he drove me to Redfern, the medical facility on campus. They sent me to the hospital in Greenville where I met my parents and I ended up having to have surgery.The opcipital lobe, the bottom of the bone socket that my eye sits in was broken and it had trapped the muscle that controls my eye and would not let it move. So I was seeing double. The surgery was to release the muscle and put a piece of fabric over the crack so it could heal and not catch the muscle again. As far as I know, its still in there.

Of course, I had a black eye. And, like good fraternity friends will do for you, they came up with a nickname for mePeedee, the dog on Little Rascals with the black eye. I never lived that down and some of my fraternity buddies still call me that when they see me.

Not one of my proudest moments. But I havent been in a fight since.

Apart from that, I am proud of many things.

Elizabeth, on the other hand, was so afraid of what might happen that she wouldn't take her foot off the brake pedal. Eventually, she started letting the car roll forward very slowly. Now she's probably one of the most aggressive drivers I know.

Historical Events

 

What world events impacted you?

Keeping up with the news gives us a sense of understanding or possibly even influence or control over the events that happen. But this is an illusion. Unless we are directly involved, only the very macro events have any affect on our lives.The Cuban Missile Crisis, The Vietnam War, Watergate, Apollo, The Iranian Hostage Crisis, the Challenger Explosion, 9/11, the middle east wars, etc. None of them had a direct impact.

 

What political changes affected you?

 

What economic conditions shaped choices?

 

What technological changes occurred?

 

What cultural shifts influenced you?

 

First Moon Walk

When Neil Armstrong walked on the moon. My mother got us up in the middle of the night to watch it on our little black and white TV.One small step for man. One giant leap for mankind.

Vietnam War

I remember the protests of the Vietnam war and the shooting at Kent State.

Richard Nixon Resignation

The election of Richard Nixon and his resignation. We were on vacation in Florida in a Winnebago on Daytona Beach gathered around the radio looking out over the ocean the night he gave his resignation speech.

I remember the Watergate Break-in, the congressional hearings, the missing 13 minutes of recordings. At the time, from the press reports, I thought he should have resigned. And perhaps he should have. But I was very uninformed and immature to have very sophisticated thoughts about it. .

9/11

I was at my desk at McKesson listening to a trader doing a live broadcast getting ready for the market open. As he was talking, I didnt hear anything, but he said, hold on a minute folks I just heard something outside. He went away and came back a few minutes later and said something like I don't know what is going on, but I heard something, and I have to go check it out. Without any more information, he just went off the air.

A few minutes later I could see a guy at his cubicle outside my office (our office walls that faced the hall were glass) looking around kind of like what is going on. I walked to the opening of my door, and he was saying something like they are saying a plane flew into the World Trade Center.

We all ran down to the cafeteria where there was a television. People were already gathering and watching the news feeds. We all spent most the day watching.

The trader guy that had been broadcasting later sent an email saying he had lost many friends in the towers, and he was quitting trading. I never heard of him again. I still don't know exactly where he was at the time, but it must have been in some of the surrounding buildings.

Shuttle Challenger Explosion

I was at my desk at USC when Kerri called crying saying, It blew up! I asked, What blew up? And she said, The shuttle!

At that, we did not have cablt TV at the office and we didnt have the internet! So I could not look into any of it. I had to wait until I got home to watch it on TV.

 

Differences

 

How has life turned out differently than you imagined?

Thats an interesting question, because when I was growing up, I don't remember having thoughts about how I expected life to be. At the time, I was just doing whatever was in front of me and whatever was next. I went from grade to grade and did the things that were going on at the time. I went to college because that was the thing to do after high school. I had some semblance of wanting to go into the MIBS program, but that was not a very concrete expectation. I was going to work for my Dad, but I had no real idea what that was going to be like. Dad always had a higher expectation of people with college degrees, and I think he thought that I would be able to take over his business, but I was really nave and inexperienced at the time. There was no way I could have done that over the older, more mature and experienced people that he had working for him. Even after graduating from there, I had no real idea of what I would do or even wanted to do.

In hindsight, the real catalyst was taking the job with Lanier and moving to Atlanta, which almost didnt happen. It was the perfect job for me at the time. It aligned with my experience and interests and I had the great fortune to work for a guy named Tom Campbell. He involved me in everything about the business, which was great experience. I travelled a lot, learned a lot and contributed a lot. First in Latin America and then in Europe. Those are experiences that I could never have imagined happening growing up.

Another way that life has turned out differently than I imagined is having children. I think I was just naive about a lot of things growing up. I just either didn't or was not able to see things differently than they were. I could not imagine what having children would be like. I was never around anyone that was having children that was anywhere near my age.

But having children has exploded a dimension of my life that I could never have imagined. Each on is similar and completely different. You cannot understand how this is until you have them for yourself, but you love each one of them fully and completely. There is no favoritism. I remember the first time William started talking and expressing his own ideas. Until then, he had seemed just an extension of us. But instantly I saw him as a being with his own thoughts and ideas. Elizabeth and Caroline went through the same.

Looking at them now, with their own lives and families and friends, its just not something I could have ever imagined.

 

 

Blessings

 

I have been blessed with a good upringing, wonderful experiences, beautiful children, excellent career, financial success, excellent health.

Has Life been good to you?

What are you grateful for?

My life has been great so far, and I look forward to it getting even better! I am grateful for the love of my children and the experiences that I have had with them and what I have learned about myself and how to be a better man in being their father. I am grateful to my wonderful parents who have provided for me both spiritually, mentally, and materially in so many fantastic ways and provided me the opportunity to have lived such a great life so far and provide for those that came after me. I am grateful for the things I learned from your grandmother. We were not good together for each other, but we were great parents and I think we both learned a lot and are better for it.

 

What were your disappointments?

 

I am having a wonderful life! I am very happy with most things, and I cannot remember too many disappointments and most have been minor in the scheme of things.

Didnt Make the Team

When I was about 12, I had been playing baseball in the YMCA league. I was a pretty good pitcher. My fast ball was good and my coach taught me to throw a special kind of curve ball--a knuckle curve. Don't remember the statistics, but we didnt lose many games when I was pitching. I tried out for a higher level baseball team, the Kiwanis club. It was like a travelling team that William eventually played on. But, while I could pitch, I hadn't learn to hold runners on base. When I tried out, I pitched okay, but if anyone got on base, I couldn't keep them from stealing. That stung a little bit.

Didnt Make the Golf Team

I started playing golf when I was 12 and played a lot. Never had many lessons, but I could play okay. I tried out for the golf team as a freshman and didnt make it. I was disappointed, but I kept playing and I made it the second. I also tried out for the golf team in college and didn't make it. I really just wasn't good enough. But, I joined a fraternity and made great friends and memories.

She Broke Up With Me

The summer before I went to college, I had a girlfriend and I got very close to her. I would write her letters and come home on the weekends to see her. One weekend she broke up with me and really broke my heart.

My Marriage

This is a difficult subject to talk about. Not so much for me, but because it has such an impact on my children. My purpose is not to place blame, because I am equally responsible for it, but rather to just try and give a little insight into my perspective.



 

What were your surpirses

 

 

 

What are your regrets?

 

That is a very hard question to answer, because having watched time travel movies, any one thing that would have been different could have and likely would have had an unpredictable impact on every other aspect of my life, from that point forward, and I am very happy with much of my life. But of course, every decision I made (or didnt make) precluded anything else happening prior to that. So, it is a real difficult mental question to answer.

I cannot imagine my life without my children. They have been and still are the joys of my life. If anything that I might have done differently had changed that aspect of my life, I would not want to change it.

This part is for adults only. However, without getting into reasons and explanations and complicated details, the one big regret I have is not experiencing all the other great things in my life with companionship. That, combined with all of the other great aspects of my life, would have made my life a dream life.

         I regret that I was too immature to be deciding about marriage and making the choices I did.

         I regret the impact of my divorce on my childrens and their childrens lives.

         I regret not recognizing I was better than I thought and demanding what I was worth in the market.

         And while I believe I made time for all of my kids events, I regret not making even more time for experiencing other dimensions of life, putting work in a tighter window. However, there is no way of knowing the impact that that might have had on my ability to advance and experience what I experienced and provide as I was able to provide.

         I regret not landscaping the Amberglen side yard.

         I regret not finishing the Edgewater basement so it could have been enjoyed more.

         I regret not finishing the Andelle basement for the same reasons.

         I regret not playing golf more competitively.

         I regret wearing my hair so long as an insecure teenager.

         I regret trying to exchange money in the Cartegena old city and getting taken advantage of for $50!

         I regret not taking better care of myself physically to the point of better fitness. Not that it was so bad, but that it could have been better.

         I regret not taking better care of my skin as a kid in the sun. I would not or forget to wear sunscreen and get sunburned playing golf or in the water and now I have issues.

         I regret not understanding what I now understand about beliefs far earlier.

         I regret not following up with a girl I met at South Carolina at the end of my sophmore year.

         I regret some of the hangovers I had. But not all of them.

         I regret not winning the Punt, Pass and Kick tournament when I was ten.

         I regret not suing McKesson for age discrimination, which it was. Jeff Campbell, the CFO once said in front of me, not realizing I was over 50, We need to get rid of all these 50 year olds and replace them with younger people.

         I regret not being an example of a loving husband to my children.

         I regret lying to my Dad about wrecking the car.

         I regret saying I do.

         I regret how I acted after Martha broke up with me.

         I regret being too hard on the kids.

         I regret not being taught what I have come to know as the mind framework as a child or at least teenager/young adult.

What mistakes have you made?

I made plenty of mistakes, but got enough right to help infuse responsibility, confidence, compassion and capability in my children. I hope they'll pay it forward to their families.

 

What would you do differently?

What would you consider your motto?

I dont consider that I have a motto, but if I did, I think it would be, If its to be, its up to me.

I think there is a good aspect of this and a not so good aspect of it.

Dad taught me to be responsible and so I take responsibility for myself in every area. However, that can be a bit extreme and I dont let others in to help, either believing or wanting to do it myself.

 

Advice

 

What advice would you give your 20, 30, 40, 50, 60 year old self?

What advice would you give your great grandchildren?

 

 

What makes you Optimistic or Pessimistic about the younger generation

I am optimistic that young people are always curious and creative and they will continue to discover and invent technological advances.

What worries me is that people seem to have lost a sense of responsibility to the community. They are focused on themselves and their freedom to do whatever they want, and not caring about the impact of what they may want has on other people.

Who had the biggest influence on your life?

I have had several people that have influenced by life. Mostly good, and from some I learned to do the opposite of their example.

First, of course, Id have to say my mother and father had the most influence on me.

I think I got a lot of my compassion from my mother. She is a very kind and compassionate person. How she dealt with 4 boys with only 4 years between them and maintained he composure so much of the time is a sign of her kindness and compassion. She rarely wanted anything for herself. She was always giving to us.

From my father, first I received the gift of discipline. While I hated hearing it at the time, he would frequently remind us of the big Rresponsibility. I might have been a slow learner on that one because I know I resisted it. But ultimately the lesson took hold, and it has been one of my strengths. I cover this in another short story, but, while I didn;t learn the saying until much later, it retroactively applied. If its to be, its up to me.!

The other broad thing I learned from him was how to discipline, but also how to love my children. There is no doubt he loved his chidren. He did a lot of things in his life, but his kids were always a tope priority. I recently found some postcards that he had written from Europe individually to each of us, individually encouraging us, and in hindsight in the way that would uniquely apply to us individually. In everything we did, he was always looking for ways to facilitate what was good for us.

When I was in the fifth grade, the school put on a program of orchestra instruments trying to encourage and interest studuents in taking up one of the musical instruments. When I got home I asked my mother it I could play the violin. She said Id have to ask my father. I was axious all day as to what he would say. When he got home, I told him about the program and asked about playing the violin. Without hestitation, he said yes. Needed not other details. He was like that about everything when it came to us. I always looked and still look for ways I can help my children.

I have had a couple of work-related people greatly influence my life. The first was Tom Campbell at Lanier. He threw me into every issue that he was ever involved in at Lanier and gave me exposure and opportunity to get involved in a wide range of topics. He supported me during some challenging political situations and generally gave me the confidence to take on more and grow.

The other one I would mention is the CFO at McKesson that I worked for, Craig Niemiec. He taught me the concept of Run it so te best people love it. He was referring to how he managed. I came to see this as the best people want opportunity, challenge and recognition and reward. It is similar to what Tom Campbell did for me.

The two sayings, If its to be, its up to me. and Run it so the best people love it. helped guide my individual performance and managerial approach that lead to the successes that I had i business.

What is your greatest achievement?

My greatest achievement in life is helping raise three of the best and most capable people you will ever find in this world. I made plenty of mistakes, but I think I got enough right that I helped infuse in them with responsibility, confidence, compassion and capability to do anything they ever want to do and hopefully pay it forward to their families.

Smallest decision, biggest impact?

What is your favorite holiday?

By far my favorite was Christmas! One of the first I remember was on Creighton Street. Mom and Dad decorated the house and built a Santa Claus climbing in through the window on the front porch, with a spot light. They won best decorations in the neighborhood!! Mom and Dad always made Christmas great! Over the years, we got bicycles, and motor cycles, and snow skis. It was always a great surprise. One year when I was little, my grandparents came to stay with us. Granddaddy slept in my room. We were all anxious to go to bed so Santa Claus could come, but Granddaddy was snoring so loud I could not sleep. I laid there awake afraid Santa would not come to our house because I was not asleep. He did come and everything was great!

What are your happiest moments?

Without a doubt, my happiest moments have been raising William, Elizabeth and Caroline. I could not have asked for more perfect children. They went through all of the challenging stages, but the great times far, far, far outweigh any of those times--I barely remember them. I remember the great times. The days they were born

Cost of things.food, gas, cars, movies, houses

When I was little, bubble gum was one cent. A candy bar was about ten cents. When I was about 7 or 8 and wanted money for candy, I would ride my bicycle along the side of the road (there were ditches on each side of the road) looking for soft drink bottles that people had thrown out of their cars. I would take the bottles to the convenience store near our house and they would give me 5 cents per bottle. It was a way to try and keep people from littering. I put a wire basket on the front of my bicycle and would keep searching until it would not hold any more, usually about 8 or 10 bottles. I would 40 or 50 cents and buy candy with it.

I also remember gasoline being about 19 cents per gallon and my mother complaining about how high the price was!! I think the house my parents bought when I was about 5 cost around $8,000.

What were your hobbies?

When I was little, I used to build model airplanes and model cars. We did not have video games. We mostly played outside. We rode our bikes everywhere. There was a creek down at the end of the street and we would use bricks and rocks and clay to build dams in the creek. We would catch "crawdads". I also played football, baseball, basketball. I played at the YMCA and at church. I was pretty good at baseball. We would go to the ice cream store after a game and another dad would give me a dollar if I had hit a homerun! Football was always hard to get started in because it was always so hot, but Dad would make us go, and pretty soon we were into it and like it. I was okay at basketball, but not great. In college, I didnt play much, but I practiced and was able to dunk the ball. I was also a Boy Scout. I started as a Cub Scout and made it to Webelo. I liked earning the badges. My dad was the Scout Master for a while. We did the "Pinewood Derby" several years. Everyone would buy a kit to make a wooden car. It had to be carved, sanded and painted to look like a car and the wheels had to be put on with nails, and you had to drill a hole in the car and pour melted lead in to it to make it heavy and go faster. Except there was a weight limit and the car had to be weighed before it could be raced.

Have you known some colorful characters?

My uncle Toby was a colorful character. We was married to my Father's sister, Nell. He was a very big man. He worked for the Navy as an entomologist (studied insects). He was always smiling. Whenever we left his house after a visit, he would always shake your hand (and he had enormous hands) and say, "I'm glad you got to see me!" with a giant smile! On one visit, we went to the beach. My brother Greg was on Uncle Toby's shoulders as we were walking through the sand dunes. You could not see the ocean, but as Greg got high enough to see the ocean (and he had never seen it before) he said, "Man, what a pool!" Uncle Toby thought that was one of the greatest things he had ever heard! He smiled every time he told that story--and he told it a lot!

Who did you look up to then and now?

I look up to my father and mother. My father grew up without a father himself. He left when my Dad was about 12. he was raised by his mother and older sister. His mother at one point worked in a shirt factory, sewing collars and sleeves onto shirts for 5 cents a piece. They lived in a house in south Atlanta and had to set and clean out rat traps under the house. He had a paper route and worked in a grocery store to make money. He had a decent, but not great high school record, and he never went to college. He joined the navy rather than get drafted into the army, and after he got out, he worked for a company selling machinery parts. He started his own business with about $1,500 dollars and built it to one stage where it had $12 million in revenue and won the Export award from South Carolina! He taught me right from wrong and a great work ethic, even when I didn't want to learn it. He taught me to be analytical, which has helped me be successful in business. He loved us and gave us everything we could have wanted---nice homes, cars, food clothing, vacations, sports, everything. And, he made sure we all got a college education. He even paid for me to get a Masters degree that has led to the most amazing life experiences around the world. My mother is a saint. She never asked for anything that I can remember. She did everything for us. She was loyal wife. They have always loved each other and still do. She taught me kindness and doing things for other people.

How has the world changed for better/worse?

The world has change a lot for the better. When I was growing up, we had a black and white television and we got 3 channels that were not always clear transmitted like a radio. You had to use an antenna called "rabbit ears" and you had to adjust it just right to pick up the signal. Phones were connected to the wall; there were no cell phones. There were "pay phones" where you would go into a booth, insert money like a Coke machine and pay by the minute. Computers did not exist. No video games. The Internet did not existno Google, Facebook, Instagram, Pinterest, Twitter. Cars are much safer now. Houses are so much better. There was no electronic banking. No ATM's. You had to go to a bank or sometimes a store with and "cash a check". There a lots of things that are better.

What do you miss about the 'old' days?

It could be that I just do not remember or was not aware that it was going on, but it seems that the world is not as "nice" as it used to be. People seem to be more selfish than I remember. Politicians, teachers. I used to trust that the government was going to do the right thing. Now I do not believe the government can be trusted. Perhaps it will change, but I am concerned for my children and their children about the state of the government and the impact it is having on the economy, the motivation to be a capitalist. The government has become more socialistic and people have gotten lazy and want the government to take care of them. This structure will collapse like the structures have in Europe.

How have you become wiser?

What are the best things money can't buy?

Money cannot buy the joy of raising children, of appreciating the wonderful, beautiful world we live in. Nature is incredible.

What are the best things about being a grandparent?

The best thing about being a grandparent is being able to experience my grandchildren the same way I enjoyed my children, and be reminded of them at the same time. It excites me to think about their future and the things they will experience and learn and enjoy. I want to do everything I can to make their lives as enjoyable or even more enjoyable than my own.

What is the secret to staying young?

The secret to staying young it to keep yourself in physically good shape. Take care of yourself, and stay current on what is going on in the world and with the newer generations. Don't get too locked into the way things used to be. Go with the flow a little bit, unless it is not good for you.

 

Issues

 

What are your thoughts on the issues of the day?

Wages

Minimum Wage?

On a social/cultural note, there is currently heated debate about hourly rates for employees, with many pushing for $15 per hour. That shows how much wages have been compressed over time. I dont believe that every job should carry a wage that would allow someone to live off of ita living wage. Jobs should be compensated for what they are worth. Otherwise, the natural laws of supply and demand get distorted. However, wages have certainly be compressed. It is a complex problem, whose solution lies in individuals educating and preparing themselves to be able to provide greater value and therefore demand and get paid higher wages. However, there is an unequal balance of power between companies and employees that allows them to take advantage of the over-supply of uneducated labor to fill the low value jobs. There should be some mechanism that allows for the sharing of the value that is being created by the employees with the employees, instead of the majority of the value going only to those that provide the ideas or the capital. All the ideas and capital in the world would not have allowed Amazon and others to become the behemoths they are without the efforts, however uneducated or unskilled they may be, of vast numbers of people. Those with the ideas and capital should want to share the value with those that help create it so that society as a whole can be more capable to behave and raise their families in ways that benefit society as a whole. It is a fine balance to avoid the negatives of

Minimum Wage and Living Wage: How should wages reflect cost of living, inflation, and job value? And Universal Basic Income (UBI): Is a guaranteed income feasible or desirable in today's economy?

Wages have been compressed by the system imbalances allowed into capitalism. I am unsure of Universal Basic Income. On one hand, while I think like every other governmental direct subsidy, it short circuits the laws of supply and demand and human nature is not forced to make oneself more valuable if all the basic needs are met. However, from what I have read about AI, it may displace a very large percentage of the current workforce, whether prepared or not. And, it may not be possible to have jobs for millions of people replaced by either AI that does he thinking or robots that do the physical work.

I do not know how this will play out. On one hand, people say that UBI will allow everyone to live at a comfortable level, so they will be less stressed and able to channel their efforts into the arts and creativity. But on the other hand, it will cause massive inflation, because free money will be chasing goods, and it seems that they inflation will outstrip the productivity gains that make the provision of UBI possible. It is similar to any system where the laws of supply and demand are short circuited.

Unless something fundamental changes in the way humans choose to live, I cannot imagine that UBI will work as envisioned. And I am not confident that humans can change fast enough.

I see big trouble ahead.

Remote Work vs. In-Office Work:

Balancing productivity, flexibility, and collaboration in the modern workforce.

I have been considering this dilemma since my commutes in Atlanta that continued to grow to the point of absurdity. How can we continue to extend a system that is so flawed? Why do millions of people get up everyday, get into a vehicle, clog massive infrastructures of highways and roads for hours per day, everyday without consideration of viable alternatives.

The debate seems to be raging on the wrong dimensions of the issue. Remote or in-office work should be a function of the nature of the work and the ability to execute it efficiently and effectively. The shortcoming, in my opinion, is leadership not considering the full scope of their objectives and the means to obtain them. Leadership or management seem to be more about control of the location and time spent of employes rather than the outcomes they produce. I had a boss once that was more concerned about the time an employee got to work and left than the outcomes they achieved, regardless of where they were.

Some jobs benefit from the location of employees and others dont. If the issue is productivity, then set objectives for the work to be done.

The cost of insisting that workers be in a particular location or not is being pushed on to governments and ultimately the people. Companies are not having to pay directly for the cost of the commutes, which include the infrastructure, the injuries, the cost of vehicles, fuel, repairs, insurance, etc.

Gig Economy and Worker Rights:

How do we address issues like benefits, job security, and fair pay in the gig economy?

Wealth Inequality:

The growing disparity between the wealthy and everyone else.

Wealth inequality in my opinion is a function of two things. Corporations allowed to exploit employees and society. Individuals not taking responsibility for making themselves into valuable components that can be employed by companies engaged in positive societal work. This has been prompted by and continually exacerbated by the government getting directly involved in economic payments to people regardless of their value to companies. The moment government started giving stipends to people for whatever reason, welfare, etc. the incentive to self improve has been replaced with an increasing reliance on the government for handouts. The government has to get out of the business of providing direct assistance, and into the business of providing a system of preparation. Let charities and other altruistic organizations take care of those that fall out of the system. The necessity and lack of fall back will incent greater self-reliance.

Social and Cultural Topics

Capitalism versus Socialism

Pure socialsim has resulted in the deaths of hundreds of millions of people, at least partially because of the authoritarian form of its leadership and the failure to properly employ the law of supply and demand.

Proponents of democracy and capitalism claim it has resulted in the lifting out of poverty of hundreds of millions, if not billions of people, and is the greatest system ever devised by man.

Its success is certainly by the removal to a great extent of absolute authoritarianism, but also because it employs the law of supply and demand. However, democracy and capitalism still do not sufficiently address the social issues of humanity. The only way for democracy and capitalism to work for everyone is if everyone engages and competes to the full extent possible, by preparing themselves as a good or service employed by the system. However, no matter how engaged and prepared one may be, there will still be winners and losers. Unless we are prepared to allow an not insignificant portion of our population to lose, suffer and die, as what may described as the downside of the greatest system, elements of socialism must be employed to save millions form misery and death caused either by their losing fair and square in the competition of life, or being grossly exploited by the power of those that run the capitalist machine. The labor movements of the 30s, 40s, 50s that continue today, emerged because capitalism was happy to exploit millions of people in the concentration of the majority of the wealth into the hands of a few. Labor unions helped concentrate the fragmented power of employees to help counter the power of the employers. Legislation since that time has tried to stem the excesses if capitalism. However, Unions and legislation alone cannot balance the scale. The levers of capital are far stronger. And legislation tends to err on the side of short circuiting the laws of supply and demand. What is necessary is an education or preparation system that prepares humans to be valuable, and what would amount to a conscious compassion amongst employers to spread the value that the collective ideas, capital and labor create with those that help create it.

A large part of the issue of the ill-effects of capitalism stem from the fact that companies or corporations are not held responsible for all of the costs of the elements that go into their operation. Many examples exist. Housing developers are not held responsible for the cost of the infrastructure requirements that their housing projects demand, including roads, utilities, security (police, fire) etc. Companies are not held responsible for the costs they impose on people and ultimately government for the cost of commuting to and from work. The cost of roads, vehicles, fuel, repairs, insurance, etc. If they were, they would be more selective of employees. Instead, governments take on these costs, ultimately transferring them to the people, by not only providing the infrastructure, but offering tax breaks for the employers to locate in their jurisdictions, not properly assessing the costs and benefits.

Also, companies are not held responsible for the impacts they make on other aspects of life. Their waste and/or damage to the environment. Plastic is allowed to be used to create products for pennies, sold for dollars and the waste is cast into the environment. More of the cost of the protection of the social/environmental fabric of the world should be born by companies.

The counter argument is, well they cant afford it and will not bring the jobs. Then perhaps we dnon;t ned what they are bringing? And what we should demand is that companies bring the things that are net benefits to society, not the corporations. We can live perfectly well with basic shelter, food water and clothing. Everything else provided by corporations should be a net positive add to the societal good.

Education

The role of public vs. private schools, college affordability, and student loan forgiveness.

The role and process of education needs to be rethought completely. The purpose of education is to establish the beliefs of the internal and external domains of the world that facilitiates the functional manifestation of what one desires, including what is desired itself. The current system was designed to produce workers. This is less and less required. What is required is fundamental knowledge of how the world worsk, how to participate in the economic system and or how to create eons own place in the economic system. We need to recognize this need. Reprioritize this need, and instill self-responsibility to educate oneself to be able to sustain oneself. The system should be private, but with societal guardrails installed by government to protect against exploitation.

Healthcare System:

Single-payer healthcare, access to care, and drug pricing.

We do not have a health care system, we have a sick care system run by those interested in profiting from the sick. The people need to understand the difference and prioritize health care over sick care. The system should be capitalistic and based on insurance and actuarial analysis, but legislated to avoid exploitation.

Free Speech vs. Censorship:

Balancing the right to speak freely with the need to regulate harmful speech.

Speech is only harmful to the extent that those without the ability to discern the greater good adopt ultimately bad ideas. The lack of debate around COVID and the legitimacy of the ruling party has resulted in the death of millions.

Diversity and Inclusion:

The challenges of creating equitable opportunities in business and society.

While discrimination may always be a problem to some extent, because it is our lesser nature to discriminate against those different from us. The structural impediments that once existed have been mostly removed. Perhaps not completely, but completely enough that if one desires and dedicates them selves to education and preparation, there is enough demand for skills that race, gender, national origin, social preferences, are not going to be the impediment that they once were. Enforce non discrimination for any demographic characteristics, and allow the supply and demand of the market guide outcomes. My concern with the current efforts and social biases on this issue are not seeking equality in terms of opportunity, but rather outcome, and to the point that discrimination and even retribution applied against a demographic that was a majority, but will shortly be a minority.

Immigration:

How should nations balance security, cultural integration, and economic needs?

America was founded on freedom and extended an invitation to those around the world to come share in this freedom. Some of this was essentially global altruism, to give anyone who wanted one and opportunity to gain and live in freedom. Many people were also needed to explore and settle the land and construct its infrastructure. Those needs have changed and the motives and mobility of those that would harm the country have changed. We want to offer the potential for freedom, but it can only done in a way that preserves the freedom and rights of its citizens. Law enforcement within the country must intercede and separate those that would do others harm once in the country, and immigration law should protect against allowing those that may do harm before they enter. Also, while it would be preferable for existing citizens and their children to educate themselves for the betterment of themselves and the country, we can also benefit from allowing those in that have already educated and prepared themselves and allow them to employ those skills to ther betterment of themselves and the country.

Technology and Innovation

Artificial Intelligence (AI):

Impacts on employment, ethics, and daily life.

Climate Change and Renewable Energy:

The balance between technological innovation and environmental sustainability.

I dont believe that man is smart enough to figure out the complexities of climate change. We should focus on environmentally safe and clean processes, but the current focus on energy absolutism is extreme and misplaced, likely to result in poor alternatives.

Privacy and Surveillance:

Striking a balance between security and individual freedom.

It seems to me that privacy and freedom should be based on an old saying, Your freedom ends and the end of your fist and the tip of my nose.

Social Media's Role in Society:

Its effects on communication, mental health, and misinformation.

Cryptocurrency and Decentralized Finance:

The future of money and its regulation.

For money to play a proper role, it must be backed by something of value. Taking the dollar off the gold standard allowed for the printing of money and the stoking of inflation. Unless whatever form of money is based on something of value, this will always be the case. I am generally for a cryptocurrency, for its privacy and safety, but it is not backed by value other than its scarcity, which may be all it needs, because gold is somewhat like this. There are some industrial uses for it, but it is mostly its scarcity.

However, I do not see governments allowing a true cryptocurrency to exist because they then lose the ability to manipulate its value to their designs, which is the benefit to all others of this type of money.

Governance and Global Relations

Government Spending and Debt:

How should nations manage long-term financial obligations?

Political Polarization:

Strategies for reducing divisiveness and improving public discourse.

Globalization vs. Protectionism:

Finding a balance between global trade and local industry.

Human Rights:

Navigating global inequality and cultural differences in rights and freedoms.

Military and Defense Spending:

Balancing national security with the cost of militarization.

Ethical and Philosophical Questions

The Value of Work: How do we define meaningful work in a post-industrial world?

Consumerism: Balancing economic growth with sustainable consumption.

Aging Population: Challenges of healthcare, retirement, and intergenerational equity.

The Role of Religion in Public Life: Navigating faith in increasingly secular societies.

Moral Implications of Technology: Ethical dilemmas in biotech, robotics, and AI.

exploitive capitalism and malfunctioning socialism.
