The Decades

 


I recall the feeling of being able to say I remember something that had happened 5 years ago, then 10 years ago., then 15 years ago. I shake my head as I can now say that I remember things 20, 30, 40, 50, even 60 years ago. Our minds are remarkable.

With the help of AI, I took a look at the major things happening in the world since I was born in the areas of politics, science, business and culture, and how they influenced life in general for me and others.

 

The 1960s

 

The 1960s were my early childhood, and I was ages 1 through 10from an infant through elementary school.

I had what feels like a pretty normal and good childhood. We lived in 4 different houses in Spartanburg and Greenville. So we moved a lot. But I was only aware of the last two and we spent 5 years in that one, so, to me things were stable. I had friends at school and friends in the neighborhood.

 

Of course, I wasnt very much aware of anything outside of our family and school, but the things happening at that time shaped the world I would live in years later.

Society & Culture

The 1960s were a period of great societal change. There was a confluence of several factors, including civil rights, womens rights, dissatisfaction with government, dissatisfaction with corporations. Those that initiated it were perhaps well-intended, but in my opinion started the unraveling of society.

These resulted in a focus on the individual over the community and a rejection of what previous norms. The rejection pushed to the opposite extreme, expressed in the style and color of clothing, hair styles, beards and mustaches, including experimentation with drugs. And the newly discovered contraception in the Pill, set society reeling in a direction of which no one could anticipate the outcome.

It was reflected in society in the styles that people adopted. The conservatism of the past was thrown overboard in favor of extremes in the opposite direction in hairstyles, clothing styles, colors, etc.

While it is hard to imagine the situation before. But before the pill simplified and improved contraception, ideas about sex were very protective because the risk of pregnancy, and before Roe vs Wade and the ease of getting an abortion had enormous ramifications for men and women.

Hippies

The rejection of conservatism to the opposite extreme, included increased experimentation with drugs. The most extreme of these people were called hippies. I remember a trip to Atlanta where we drove through this particular part of town just to see the hippies.

The styles influenced us as kids and we started letting our hair grow longer and we wore bell-bottom pants and shirts with long wide collars and the labels of suits became extremely wide. The mixture of colors that had previously not been acceptable, were all suddenly the way to go.

Integrated Classroom

The civil rights movement was strong. Martin Luther King gave his I have a dream speech. And schools were integrated when I was in the 5th grade. Three black children joined our class that year. Looking back at the news, there were a lot of protests and problems, but in our school, we didnt have anything like that. They were just 3 other kids and we all got along fine together.

Womens Rights

A movement called womens liberation started advocating for equal rights in employment and reproductive rights (the pill.) There was a show on television called Laugh In which seemed to be highlighting all of these cultural changes, in clothing, hairstyles, music and social behavior becoming much more sexual.

Music

In the 60s the Beatles came to America. The Rolling Stones and the Beach Boys were the big bands. Other famous artists were The Supremes, Marvin Gaye and Stevie Wonder. Folk music was popular with musicians like Bob Dylan, Neil Young, Eric Clapton.

The Vietnam War

The United States was in the Vietnam war, and I remember hearing the news announce every night how many soldiers had been killed that day.

Science and Technology

Man on the Moon

The astronauts landed on the moon. We got up in the middle of the night to watch it on television.

JFK Assassination

John F Kennedy was assassinated in 1963, Malcomb X in 1965 and Martin Luther King in 1968.

I can still picture Chet Huntley and David Brinkly doing the Huntley and Brinkley Report, and Walter Cronkite doing the CBS News on our black and white television

Muhammed Ali

Muhammed Ali became heavyweight champion. I loved watching him box.

Business

The 1960s were a pivotal decade, where breakthroughs in technology, business practices, and culture converged, shaping the foundation of the modern global economy.

1959

Xerox introduced the first plain paper copier forever altering office work.

The microchip was invented, sparking the tech revolution.

General Motors was the largest U.S. corporation by revenue.

American Express launched its first charge card, expanding consumer finance.

Alaska and Hawaii became the 49th and 50th states, influencing energy and natural resource sectors.

1960

1960 also marked a post-WWII peak in U.S. economic growth, with GDP hitting $527 billion.

IBM Introduced the first commercial mainframe, making computing more accessible to businesses.

AT&T developed the first commercial modem. Setting the stage for the communications revolution.

Ford introduced the Ford Falcon, a compact car that challenges larger vehicle dominance.

The Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries (OPEC) was formed. laying the groundwork for future global energy policies.

The American Stock Exchange merged with the New York Curb Exchange.

1961

IBM developed the Selectric typewriter, a game-changer in office technology.

Six Flags Over Texas opened, expanding the entertainment industry.

FM radio became more popular, influencing the music and advertising landscape.

The Dow Jones crossed 700 points

1962

Walmart opened its first store, disrupting retail.

The Cuban Missile Crisis prompted defense industry innovation.

The first Kmart store opened, expanding discount retail to the U.S. market.

John Glenn's orbital flight boosts aerospace and tech industries.

The SEC mandated the disclosure of corporate proxy voting policies.

Meanwhile, inflation started to take hold, as US Steel's price increases contributed to rising costs across sectors.

 

1963

McDonald's First International Franchise, beginning its glbal expansion.

The U.S. introduced the ZIP Code system, streamlining postal services and logistics.

Martin Luther King Jr.'s "I Have a Dream" speech influences workplace diversity efforts.

Douglas Engelbart patents the computer mouse, paving the way for modern computing.

The first push-button telephone is introduced by AT&T.

Boeing begins development of the 727, transforming commercial air travel.

1964

IBM releases the System/360, the first family of computers, revolutionizing business computing.

The Civil Rights Act of 1964 is signed, impacting workplace equality and corporate policies.

The Ford Mustang debuts, creating the "pony car" market segment

. The Dow Jones Industrial Average surpasses 800 points for the first time.

1965

Walmart Founded

Gordon Moore introduces Moore's Law, forecasting exponential growth in computing power.

The Medicare and Medicaid programs are signed into law, reshaping the healthcare industry.

Intel co-founder Robert Noyce develops the first silicon integrated circuit.

Sony introduces an early consumer video recorder.

The New York Stock Exchange experiences its first-ever trading volume of over 10 million shares.

1966

The first credit card with a magnetic strip, developed by IBM, is introduced changing how financial transactions took place.

General Motors becomes the first U.S. corporation to earn over $1 billion in a single year.

The U.S. Minimum Wage Act is expanded, affecting labor markets and corporate costs.

NASAs Apollo program boosts aerospace technology investments.

Electronic Data Systems (EDS) goes public, signaling growth in IT services.

1967

The first Super Bowl is played, marking the commercialization of sports.

Boeing rolls out the prototype for the 747 jumbo jet, further revolutionizing air travel.

The first ATMs (automated teller machines) are developed, redefining the way consumers interacted with money


Texas Instruments introduces the first handheld calculator moving away from the 10-key paper tape, making office work and personal finances more efficient.

 

The Big Mac is introduced by McDonald's, a fast-food milestone.

1968

Intel Corporation is founded by Gordon Moore and Robert Noyce.

The stock market enters a prolonged bull market, with the Dow Jones Industrial Average reaching 900 points.

The U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development promotes urban renewal. which had lasting impacts on real estate and construction industries.

The UAW-GM strike highlights labor relations in the auto industry.

The first public demonstrations of ARPANET (precursor to the internet) are held.

1969

The first successful moon landing by Apollo 11 inspires global tech innovation.

The ARPANET sends its first message, laying the foundation for the internet.

The Concorde supersonic jet completes its first test flight, transforming aviation.

The Woodstock Festival underscores the economic impact of counterculture.

The Boeing 747 entered commercial service changing travel.

 

 


 

Cultural

         Society experienced significant change, with the rise of the counterculture movement.

         Hippies became prominent, characterized by distinctive clothing, long hair, and drug use.

         Fashion shifted from conservative to more relaxed styles, with longer hair, bell-bottom pants, and wide-lapel suits.

         The civil rights movement led to school integration.

         Womens liberation advocated for equal employment rights and reproductive freedom.

         "Laugh-In" reflected and amplified changing cultural trends.

         The Beatles, The Rolling Stones, and The Beach Boys dominated music, alongside artists like The Supremes, Marvin Gaye, and Stevie Wonder.

         Folk music gained popularity with Bob Dylan, Neil Young, and Eric Clapton.

         The Vietnam War was ongoing, with daily news reports on soldier casualties.

         The moon landing was a significant event, watched live on television.

         Major assassinations: John F. Kennedy (1963), Malcolm X (1965), Martin Luther King Jr. (1968).

         News anchors like Chet Huntley, David Brinkley, and Walter Cronkite were household names.

         Muhammad Ali became heavyweight champion, and his matches were highly anticipated.

Political

         The U.S. was deeply involved in the Vietnam War, leading to widespread protests and political unrest.

         The civil rights movement peaked, with the passage of landmark legislation.

 

The 1970s

 

In the 1970s, I was age 11-20, from the fifth grade into college. I grew from an elementary school boy in a small southern town to a college student . I grew from pre-teen, to teen to young adult.. A lot happened in that time in the world, in culture, in business and in me.

The Watergate Scandal, that seems a lot less scandalous compared to the outright criminality of politicians today, happened in 1972 and ended in 1974 when President Nixon resigned. I was in the 9th grade,

Elvis Presley died, Margaret Thatcher first female Prime Minister.

The Vietnam war ended in 1975, when I was in the 10th grade,

Clothing and hairstyles in the 70s continued to evolve from the 60s. The latter part of the 70s started being influenced by disco music and styles.

In 72 Fall-73 Spring I was in middle school.

In 73 Fall-77 Spring, I was in high school.

The 70s saw environmental awareness leading to the establishment of Earth Day and the Environmental Protection Agency in 1970.

Technology started to advance rapidly into microprocessors and personal computers.

In music, disco dominated with artists like Donna Summer, the Bee Gees and ABBA.

 

If the 1960s saw a lot of change, they have nothing on the 1970s. Despite horrific governmental leadership for the entire decade, the seeds of a technology boom had been sown and were germinating and taking root. While I was mostly oblivious, except as a nave spectator, the 1970s experienced tremendous political, scientific and business changes was a transformative decade, marked by economic volatility, technological innovation, and societal changes that reshaped industries and global disruption of economies and governmental regulation in response to global environmental concerns.

In politics, we entered the decade with Richard Nixon as president. The Vietnam war was continuing and the economy suffering. In reaction to the poor economy Nixon ended the gold standard that had helped maintain the value of the dollar. As a result, inflation started its upward climb. While the NASDAQ launched in 1971, the OPEC Oil Embargo of 1973, the Dow crash in 1973-74. Vanguard would launch its first mutual fund two years later. Nixons Watergate disaster resulted in his resignation, Gerald Ford taking over until the 1976 election and the country turning to peanut farmer Jimmy Carter, who ended up being the worst president in history, mismanaging the economy into record inflation that required high double digit interest rates to bring under control and world politics, with the Iranian hostage crisis. Lasting over 400 days. It was not until the 1980 election of Ronald Reagan would the country begin to see any light at the end of the tunnel.

However, science and technology continued to evolve, setting the stage for an eighties boom that no one could yet see coming. Microprocessors advanced finding their way into new products such as computers that required software. Microsoft and Apple were founded, the first video games emerged. Digital photography was born, Betamax video tapes developed, and Motorola introduced the first mobile phone, Each of these technological seeds were about to break above the ground.

On the personal side, Bond Textile continued to grow. Dad started with one building. Rapidly adding three more at the Airport Road location, but then expanding further to a 10,000 square foot office space and 50,000 square feet of manufacturing space. Business grew domestically and internationally in Mexico, Argentina, Egypt and Japan. Bond Textile won the South Carolina Export Award in 1977 and hosted the Governor at a reception and award ceremony at the Bond location. In hindsight, this is a testament to Dads leadership of the business. I recall conversations about 18% interest rates, that he was not immune from. Yet, he still managed to expand. I wasnt aware enough to understand how unique and different this was at the time. His success was just taken for granted, when the alternative could have been much worse.

 

The 1970s - Economics

 

While the economy of the 1970s suffered greatly from the oil embargo, stock market crash and massive inflation, they were when the seeds of innovations were planted that have massive influence over the economies of the next 50 years.

1970,

The Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) was established changing the way industry operated for ever.

 

Walmart opened its first distribution center, marking the beginning of its logistics innovation that would propel its rise in retail.

The Dow Jones fell below 700 during an economic downturn, signaling turbulence in the stock market.

The Occupational Safety and Health Act (OSHA) also impacted workplace safety standards.

The first Earth Day highlights the importance of environmental business practices.

1971,

Intel released the 4004 microprocessor, the first commercially available microprocessor.

 

The NASDAQ stock exchange began operations, pioneering electronic trading.

 

President Nixon ended the gold standard, introducing floating currency exchange rates changing the global financial system.

Starbucks opened its first store in Seattle, starting a coffee culture revolution.

 

The first email is sent, marking the rise of digital communication.

 

1972

Atari released Pong, the first commercially successful video game, marking the start of the gaming industry.

The Consumer Product Safety Commission was founded to establish safety standards for manufacturing.

The Equal Employment Opportunity Act reshaped workplace diversity and practices,

the Dow Jones broke the 1,000-point barrier for the first time.

The Clean Water Act passed putting new constraints on industrial pollution.

1973

The OPEC oil embargo caused an energy crisis, reshaping global economics.

Federal Express (FedEx) launched its overnight delivery service, transforming distribution

 

Motorola develops the first handheld mobile phone prototype.

The Endangered Species Act is signed, influencing land use and development.

The Supreme Courts Roe v. Wade decision impacts healthcare and legal industries.

1974

Microsoft is founded by Bill Gates and Paul Allen, starting the PC revolution.

 

The Dow dropped below 600 during the 197374 stock market crash, cutting the index by over half.

The Rubiks Cube is invented, becoming a global consumer product phenomenon.

The worlds first digital camera is invented by Kodak engineer Steve Sasson.

 

1975,

Microsoft releases its first product, Altair BASIC, for the Altair 8800.

Sony releases the Betamax video cassette recorder (VCR), sparking the "VCR wars."

1976,

Apple Computer is founded by Steve Jobs, Steve Wozniak, and Ronald Wayne.

Concorde begins commercial flights, redefining international air travel.

 

Vanguard launches the first index mutual fund, revolutionizing investment strategies.

1977

The year I graduated from high school and started college,

Rise of Silicon Valley

Oracle Corporation is founded, pioneering relational database technology.

The first mass-market personal computer, the Commodore PET, is released.

The Department of Energy (DOE) is established, centralizing U.S. energy policy.

The New York City blackout highlighted vulnerabilities in urban infrastructure.

Boeing announced plans to develop the 767, setting new standards in commercial aviation.

1978,

The Airline Deregulation Act is passed, reshaping the U.S. aviation industry.

Toyota introduces the first Celica Supra, boosting Japanese automobile sales in the U.S.

The Humphrey-Hawkins Act mandates the Federal Reserve to promote full employment and stable prices.

The Sony Walkman is released in Japan, transforming portable entertainment.

Intel debuts the 8086 microprocessor, laying the groundwork for modern computing.

1979

The year I turned 20,

The second oil crisis occurred after the Iranian Revolution, impacting global economies.

ESPN launched, marking the rise of dedicated sports broadcasting.

The Federal Reserve under Paul Volcker raised interest rates to combat inflation.

The Three Mile Island nuclear accident occurred, influencing energy policy.

Chrysler received a federal loan guarantee, saving the company from bankruptcy.

 

The 1980s

 

In the 80s, I was ages 21-30. I turned 21, got out of college, started grad school, got married, got out of grad school, started my first job, bought a house, had, 2 children, moved to Atlanta, started my career in international business, built a new house, and turned 30.

While a lot happened, I was just getting warmed up in my career.

The 80 started with the Reagan Era, 1981- 89. He was president for almost the entire decade.

Tensions with the Soviet Union were high

The 80s saw tremendous economic growth and the rise of the corporate culture. The term yuppy, young urban professionals, was coined.

Personal computing became mainstream with the IBM PC and the Apple Macintosh.

Styles shifted to the preppy look, khakis, polo shrts and boat shoes. Workout wear became casual wear driven by the fitness craze.

Pop music surged with artists like Michael Jackson, Madonna and Prince, New Wave bands like Duran Duran and Depeche Mode. Hip hop emerged in NY. The craze was fueled by the introduction of the Walkman, a portable cassette tape player.

Nancy Reagan launched the War on Drugs and Just Say No to try and combat the epidemic of drug use that started in the sixties.

The space shuttle Challenger exploded on take off in 1984. I was at my desk at my new job as Associate Director of the MIBS program at the University when I heard the news.

Business

The 1980s were transformative for both the global business environment and my personal life. The decade was defined by rapid technological advancements, deregulation, and an evolving media landscape, all of which directly shaped industries and my own career path.

As I reflect on the 1980s, the decade was one of both opportunity and turbulencewhere technological and cultural shifts influenced not only the global economy but also my own personal and professional journey. From the birth of personal computing to the rise of global media and financial deregulation, the changes I witnessed in the business world were as profound as the personal decisions I was making about career and direction.

1980

IBM selected Microsofts MS-DOS as the operating system for its PCs.

CNN launched, becoming the first 24-hour news network.

The Reagan administration began implementing deregulation policies.

Apple launched the Apple III, though it suffered from technical flaws.

Gold prices reached an all-time high of $850 per ounce amid inflation fears.

1981

MTV launches, revolutionizing the music and entertainment industries.

The first IBM PC is introduced, standardizing personal computing.

Ronald Reagan introduces massive tax cuts, impacting corporate profits.

American Airlines implements the first frequent flyer program.

The Dow Jones Industrial Average drops 24% in one day during the early '80s recession.

1982

AT&T agrees to divest its local phone companies, ending its monopoly on telecommunications.

The first compact discs (CDs) are sold in Japan, transforming the music industry.

The Johnson & Johnson Tylenol recall reshapes product safety protocols.

The S&P 500 introduces stock index futures, a major development in financial markets

. Time Inc. merges with Warner Communications, forming Time Warner.

1983

The first mobile phones are sold commercially by Motorola (DynaTAC 8000X).

The internets Domain Name System (DNS) is developed, enabling easier access to web resources.

Microsoft introduces Word, its first word processing software.

The U.S. Social Security system undergoes major reforms to ensure solvency.

Chrysler launches the first minivan, reshaping family vehicles.

1984

Apple launches the Macintosh with its iconic Super Bowl commercial.

AT&T completes its breakup, creating seven regional Baby Bells.

Michael Milken and Drexel Burnham Lambert popularize junk bonds, spurring leveraged buyouts.

The Dow Jones Industrial Average surpassed 1,200 points, recovering completely from its 1973-74 crash.

The first TED conference is held, blending technology, entertainment, and design.

1985

Microsoft releases Windows 1.0, introducing a graphical user interface for PCs.

Coca-Cola launches and then retracts "New Coke", a marketing lesson in customer loyalty.

The Nintendo Entertainment System (NES) is released in the U.S., revitalizing the video game industry

. Rupert Murdoch acquires 20th Century Fox, laying the foundation for Fox Broadcasting.

The Dow Jones Industrial Average surpasses 1,500 points.

1986

The Space Shuttle Challenger disaster shifts NASAs safety protocols and funding.

The first case of insider trading convictions occurs in the Ivan Boesky scandal.

The U.S. Tax Reform Act of 1986 simplifies the tax code and lowers corporate tax rates.

Microsoft goes public, making Bill Gates the youngest billionaire.

The Big Bang deregulation of the London Stock Exchange modernizes global financial markets.

1987

The Black Monday stock market crash sees the Dow drop 22% in a single day.

Prozac is approved by the FDA, transforming the pharmaceutical industry.

IBM and Microsoft introduce OS/2, though it struggles against Windows.

The Louvre Museum opens its new glass pyramid entrance, part of a broader cultural commercialization.

Sun Microsystems introduces Java programming language, shaping software development.

1988

The first Starbucks outside Seattle opens, marking the chains rapid expansion.

The first transatlantic fiber-optic cable, TAT-8, is completed, advancing global communication.

Time Inc. and Warner Communications merge to form Time Warner, a media giant.

The Dow Jones rebounds to surpass 2,000 points after the 1987 crash.

Nintendo introduces the Game Boy, revolutionizing handheld gaming.

1989

It turned 30 this year

Savings & Loan Crisis

The Berlin Wall falls, signaling the beginning of Eastern European market integration.

Tim Berners-Lee invents the World Wide Web, setting the stage for the internet revolution.

Exxon Valdez oil spill prompts environmental regulation changes.

Sony acquires Columbia Pictures, entering the U.S. entertainment market.

The Nikkei stock index hits an all-time high, preceding Japans economic downturn.

 

The 1990s

 

In the 90s, I was 31 to 40 and turned out to be a decade of finding my car.

I took the Controller position and moved the family to Brussels, Belgium for almost three years and returned. Caroline was born, I left Lanier to join a startup software company, got fired and joined Caribiner, and left there and joined McKesson in 1999. And turned 40.

The Soviet Union dissolved in 1991

The internet became a widespread thing, and the dot com bubble started to inflate.

Cellular phones were introduced and gained widespread popularity and availability.

The Gulf War was 1990-1991 while we were in Brussels.

Bill Clinton was elected and the era of the democrat scandals began.

The 90s saw Friends and Seinfeld, The X Files, and ER

The stock market went on a tremendous rise and the mania that revenue and profit was not required to justify valuations took hold, leading to the eventual burst of the bubble in the early 2000s.

1990

We moved to Brussels in January

The Gulf War causes oil prices to spike, impacting global markets.

The Hubble Space Telescope is launched, expanding aerospace innovation.

Microsoft introduces Windows 3.0, a major milestone in personal computing.

McDonalds opens its first restaurant in Moscow, symbolizing globalization.

The S&P 500 launches its first exchange-traded fund (ETF).

Politics

The first text message is sent, marking the rise of mobile communication.

Sonys PlayStation is released in Japan, transforming the video game industry

Yahoo Created

eBay launches as an online auction site, transforming e-commerce.

Stock Market Boom Continues

The Telecommunications Act of 1996 deregulates the telecom industry, encouraging mergers.

AOL acquires Netscape

Dow Crosses 11,000

Exxon and Mobil Merge

Euro notes and coins are distributed in participating EU countries.

 

The 2000s

 

In the 2000s I was 41-50. I spent all of the 2000s at McKesson, the kids were involved in school and sports activities and we built 2 houses. I got divorced and turned 50.

The fearmongering of the catastrophes that would happen with the turn of the clocks past midnight of 1999 turned out to be nothing, But the optimism of the financial markets peaked and crashed shortly thereafter, starting the decade with its first calamity.

2000

The dot-com bubble bursts, leading to a dramatic market correction.

AOL and Time Warner announce a $182 billion merger, creating a media behemoth.

Microsoft is ruled a monopoly by a federal court in its antitrust case.

Sony releases the PlayStation 2, becoming the best-selling console of all time

. The Nasdaq Composite reaches its all-time high of 5,048 before the crash.

2001

Enron files for bankruptcy after its accounting fraud scandal, reshaping corporate governance.

Apple introduces the iPod, revolutionizing digital music.

The 9/11 attacks impact global markets, leading to a brief stock market closure.

The Dow Jones falls below 8,000 points during the post-9/11 downturn.

China joins the World Trade Organization, boosting global trade.

2002

Sarbanes-Oxley Act passes, increasing corporate accountability

. The euro becomes the sole currency in 12 EU countries.

Amazon Web Services (AWS) launches, pioneering cloud computing.

WorldCom files for bankruptcy after a massive accounting scandal.

Tesla Motors is founded, beginning its journey in electric vehicles.

2003

Google launches AdSense, transforming online advertising.

Apple introduces iTunes for Windows, broadening its customer base.

Myspace debuts, marking the rise of social media.

The Dow Jones surpasses 10,000 points again after recovering from the dot-com crash.

The Human Genome Project is completed, advancing biotechnology.

2004

The Gig Economy (Uber)

Fannie Mae and Freddi Mac Mortgage Scandals

Facebook is founded, becoming a major force in social networking.

Google goes public in one of the most successful IPOs in history.

Apple releases the iPod Mini, expanding its market dominance.

IBM sells its PC division to Lenovo, signaling industry shifts.

The Nasdaq recovers to surpass 2,000 points.

2005

Housing Boom Begins to Peak

YouTube is founded, reshaping how video content is consumed online.

Apple introduces the iPod Nano and announces plans to switch to Intel processors.

Disney acquires Pixar for $7.4 billion, strengthening its animation dominance.

The Dow Jones surpasses 10,800 points after years of post-dot-com recovery.

Google acquires Android, paving the way for its mobile operating system.

2006

Google purchases YouTube for $1.65 billion, cementing its position in online video.

Twitter is launched, introducing microblogging to the social media landscape.

Nintendo releases the Wii, redefining interactive gaming.

Facebook opens to the public, expanding beyond college networks.

ExxonMobil reports record profits amid rising oil prices.

2007

Subprime Mortgage Crisis Intensifies

Bernie Madoff Ponzi Scheme

Apple unveils the first iPhone, revolutionizing smartphones and mobile computing.

The Dow Jones reaches an all-time high of 14,164 before the financial crisis begins.

Netflix introduces streaming, reshaping media consumption.

The global financial crisis begins with the collapse of the subprime mortgage market.

2008

Spotify

The year I turned 50.

Auto Industry Bailout - Government

The 2010s

 

In the 2010s I was 51 o 60.

 

The 2010s were defined by incredible advances in technology, shifts in consumer behavior, and the rise of new markets that would reshape the business world for decades to come. It was a decade of innovation, controversy, and dramatic changes that forever altered industries and our daily lives.

Business

2010

Apple First Trillion Dollar Company

Apple launched the iPad, creating the tablet computing market

. Instagram was founded, changing the dynamics of social media sharing.

The Affordable Care Act was signed into law, impacting the healthcare industry.

The Dow Jones surpassed 11,000 points as the economy recovers.

Facebook introduced the Like button, changing online engagement metrics.

2011

US Economy Recovery Begais

Netflix Expanded Internationally

Steve Jobs passed away, marking a significant moment for Apple and the tech world.

IBMs Watson defeated humans on Jeopardy!, showcasing advancements in AI.

Spotify launched in the U.S., reshaping music streaming.

Netflix split its DVD and streaming services, causing controversy but paving the way for streaming dominance.

The Occupy Wall Street movement began, highlighting inequality and corporate influence.

2012

Microsoft acquired Skype

Facebook went public, achieving a valuation of over $100 billion.

SpaceX successfully launched the Dragon spacecraft, revolutionizing private space travel.

Google introduced Google Glass, a precursor to augmented reality technology.

Tesla introduced the Model S, redefining electric vehicles.

Facebook acquired Instagram for $1 billion, expanding its social media domination.

2013

Tesla went Public

Bitcoin hit $1,000 for the first time, signaling growing interest in cryptocurrency.

Amazon introduced same-day delivery, accelerating e-commerce.

Twitter went public, raising over $1.8 billion.

Disney released Frozen, becoming the highest-grossing animated film at the time.

Edward Snowden revealed NSA surveillance programs, sparking privacy debates.

2014

Amazon acquired Twitch

Alibabas IPO raised $25 billion, the largest IPO in history at the time.

Amazon launched Alexa and the Echo, bringing AI assistants to the mainstream.

The Dow Jones surpassed 18,000 points.

Amazon Prime Day Launched

Volkswagen Emission Scandal

Tesla introduced the Powerwall, entering the renewable energy market.

Alphabet Inc. was created as the parent company of Google.

The Dow Jones surpassed 18,300 points.

2016

Uber expanded globally

Microsoft acquired LinkedIn for $26.2 billion, expanding its enterprise services.

Pokmon GO launched, introducing augmented reality gaming to the mainstream.

AT&T merged with Time Warner.

The United Kingdom voted to leave the European Union (Brexit), impacting global markets.

The Dow Jones surpassed 19,000 points for the first time.

2017

Amazon acquired Whole Foods for $13.7 billion, entering the grocery sector.

Bitcoin hits an all-time high of nearly $20,000, sparking cryptocurrency mania.

Uber lost its license in London but maintains global growth.

Tesla launched the Model 3, bringing electric vehicles to a broader market.

The Dow Jones surpassed 24,000 points.

2018

In January of 2018 (2017?) I joined Dune Medical as CFO to help turn around a business that seemed to have promise in the breast cancer detection business. By the next January I resigned seeing the company was failing and the investors had no nterest in putting in more money. They simply wanted to sell, which they did shortly after I left.

Amazon became the Most Valuable Company, surpassing Apple.

Theranos Scandal

Facebook faced scrutiny over the Cambridge Analytica data scandal.

Amazon became the second U.S. company to hit a $1 trillion valuation.

Apple introduced the first $1,000 iPhone with the iPhone XS Max.

Microsoft overtook Apple as the worlds most valuable company.

The Dow Jones hit an all-time high of 26,828 points before a market correction.

2019

The year I turned 60.

Disney launched Disney+, entering the streaming wars.

Uber went public in one of the most anticipated IPOs, but its stock struggles.

WeWork's failed IPO highlighted issues in tech unicorn valuations.

Tesla turned profitable, leading to a surge in its stock price.

The Dow Jones reached an all-time high of 28,462 points.

 

The 2020s

 

The 2020s will be the decade I am 61 to 70! Wow. Cant believe it.

It has gotten off to a crazy start with a contrived pandemic caused by the US government that killed millions of people.

The big tech companies continue to get bigger and the delivery of AI to the public is facilitating massived rapid change.

Politics

The first four years were almost the death of the US as we know it. In combination with the pandemic, the left wing of the government tried to get rid of free speech and the right to bear arms. It was one corrupt decision after another. Feuling the Ukraine war

Thankfully, they failed and the form of government prevailed and we elected a leader in 2024 that has already started making massive moves to root out the deep state.

Business

2020

The COVID-19 pandemic disrupted global markets and economies.

The U.S. government approved a $2 trillion stimulus package, the largest in history.

The Dow Jones dropped below 19,000 points in March but recovered to end the year above 30,000 points.

Tech Growth Due to Pandemic Amazon, Zoom, Netflix

Tesla became the worlds most valuable car company, surpassing Toyota.

Zoom usage soared as remote work and online learning become the norm.

 

2021

In November, heading to Nashville for Thanksgiving, I hit a deer and disabled my car. Thankfully William drove and allowed me to make it.

Stock Market Volatility

Cryptocurrency Surge

GameStop and AMC stocks surged in a Reddit-fueled short squeeze.

Bitcoin reached an all-time high of $68,789 before experiencing a major correction.

Rivians IPO became the largest for an electric vehicle company.

2022

I sold my house in Atlanta and moved to Nashville in May 0f 2022.

Cryptocurrency Collapse

Metaverse NFTs

2023

Tech Privacy

OpenAI launched ChatGPT, driving widespread adoption of generative AI.

The BRICS nations announced plans for a new trade currency, challenging the U.S. dollar.

Nvidias stock soared, fueled by AI demand and its dominance in GPUs.

2024

Personal

In May, I moved to McEwen Northside, to be closer to family. Turned out to be a great move. The apartment and complex and surrounding area is better than downtown where I was. We spent many weekends at the pool.

Politics

Donald Trump defeated corrupt Joe Biden and Kamala Harris to become the 47th president.

Apple's Vision Pro headset launched, advancing mixed reality technology.

The global transition to renewable energy accelerated, led by China and the U.S.

Amazon unveiled its autonomous delivery drones for large-scale deployment.

 

The U.S. introduced federal regulations on AI, addressing ethical concerns.

 

The Dow Jones surpassed 37,000 points, reflecting strong market performance, but there remains uncertainty on what will sustain it and drive it higher.

2025

Donald Trump was inaugurated, his cabinet has been unanimously confirmed and the administration has started dismantling the deep state cutting waste, fraud and abuse and going after criminality, closed the border, negotiated a ceasefire in Ukraine, imposed tariffs to balance trade. No one has ever seen such activity in the first month of a presidency!
